Qisas — Retaliation
beginner
6 min
General Principle of Qisas for Injuries Less Than Life
States the general rule of qisas fima duna al-nafs with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi principle for qisas fima duna al-nafs and apply it to identify whether qisas or diya applies for a given injury.

Core Idea
Qisas is only wajib when exact similarity (mumathala) is possible; otherwise diya applies.

In this lesson, we examine the foundational Hanafi ruling on qisas (retaliation) for injuries short of death. The passage lays down a clear general principle: qisas is only obligatory when precise equivalence between the injury and the retaliation is feasible. Where such equivalence is impossible, the remedy shifts to diya (blood money). We will see how this principle is applied to specific injuries like the eye, teeth, and bones, and why shubh amd does not exist in this domain.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is an intentional injury less than life. The ruling is either qisas (wajib) or diya, depending on mumathala.
2
State the general principle
Qisas applies where mumathala is possible; where not, diya is wajib.
3
Analyze the example of the eye
Gouging out an eye: no qisas because exact replication is impossible without risk of greater harm.
Eye is delicate and not precisely reproducible.
4
Analyze the example of tooth vs. other bone
Tooth: qisas is wajib because teeth are countable and similar. Other bone: no qisas because bones vary greatly in size and shape.
The passage explicitly states 'dant tornay main qisas wajib hai' and 'kisi badi kay tornay main qisas nahi'.
5
Note the absence of shubh amd
For injuries less than life, the category of shubh amd does not exist; only intentional (amd) and accidental (khata) are recognized.
This is a distinctive Hanafi ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القصاص فيما دون النفس
القصاص فيما دون النفس میں اصول کلی ان صورتوں میں قصاص ہوتا ہے اور کن میں نہیں کن جن میں مماثلت ممکن ہو وہاں قصاص ہے اس کے بر عکس میں نہیں ، آنکھ نکالنے میں قصاص نہیں
دانت توڑنے میں قصاص واجب ہے دانت کے علاوہ کسی بڑی کے توڑنے میں قصاص نہیں
مادون النفس میں شبہ عمد نہیں
Chapter of Qisas for Less than Life. In qisas for less than life, the general principle: in those cases where similarity is possible, qisas occurs; in its opposite, not. Extracting an eye: no qisas. Breaking a tooth: qisas is obligatory. Breaking any bone other than tooth: no qisas. In less-than-life, shubh amd does not exist.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage presents the foundational Hanafi ruling on qisas (retaliation) for injuries short of death. The author begins by stating the chapter heading, then lays down the general principle: qisas is only wajib (obligatory) when exact similarity (mumathala) between the injury inflicted and the retaliation is demonstrably possible. Where such precise equivalence is not feasible, qisas is not applied; instead, diya (blood money) becomes the default. Three illustrative rulings follow: (1) Goughing out an eye does not incur qisas because exact retaliation could cause greater harm or death, and the eye's structure prevents identical replication. (2) Breaking a tooth does incur qisas because teeth are countable, of similar size, and a tooth-for-tooth exchange is feasible without excess. (3) Breaking any other bone (e.g., a limb bone) does not incur qisas, as bones vary greatly in size and shape, making exact equivalence impossible. Finally, the author notes that the category of shubh amd (semi-intentional homicide/injury) does not apply to injuries less than life; for such injuries, only 'amd (intentional) and khata' (accidental) are recognized. This fine-grained approach reflects the Hanafi commitment to precise justice and prevention of disproportionate retaliation.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for a physical injury, applied when exact similarity is possible.
مماثلت (mumathala): Exact similarity between the original injury and the retaliatory act, both in type and degree.
شبہ عمد (shubh amd): A category of homicide/injury between intentional and accidental, where the act is intentional but without intent to kill (or serious harm). The text says it does not exist in injuries less than life.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle stated in this passage, why is qisas not applied for gouging out an eye?
A) Because the eye is not a limb subject to qisas at all.
B) Because exact similarity (mumathala) is not possible without risk of greater harm.
C) Because the victim can only claim diya, not qisas, for any facial injury.
D) Because the Quran explicitly prohibits qisas for the eye.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle for qisas fima duna al-nafs hinges on the feasibility of exact retaliation; where mumathala is possible, qisas is wajib; otherwise, diya.

Qisas for Teeth vs. Other Bones
States the rule for qisas in breaking teeth vs. other bones

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas for tooth breaking and distinguish it from other bones, and apply the underlying principle of precise equivalence.

Core Idea
Qisas is wajib for teeth only, not for any other bone — precision of retaliation determines applicability.

In Hanafi criminal law, the principle of qisas (retaliation in kind) is applied strictly to injuries where exact equivalence can be achieved. This lesson clarifies a key distinction: while breaking a tooth mandates qisas, breaking any other bone incurs only financial compensation. Understanding this rule prevents common misconceptions about the scope of qisas.

Guided Path
1
Separate the two cases explicitly
Read the text and note that it gives two distinct rulings: for a tooth, qisas is wajib; for any other bone (e.g., finger, arm, rib), there is no qisas. Memorize this division.
The word 'wajib' indicates an obligatory punishment, not merely recommended.
2
Identify the underlying principle (illah)
The Hanafi school limits qisas to injuries where exact retaliation is possible. Teeth are uniform in shape and countable, so an equivalent tooth can be broken. Other bones vary in size, curvature, and strength, making precise retaliation uncertain. Hence, only financial compensation (diyah or arsh) applies.
This principle is derived from the Quranic verse on qisas (5:45) and the general rule that qisas requires equivalence.
3
Apply the rule to a new scenario
Consider a case where someone breaks another's finger. Since a finger is a bone other than a tooth, qisas is not applicable. The perpetrator must pay the appropriate diyah (blood money) based on the injury's severity.
This step reinforces the categorical distinction and prevents overgeneralization.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دانت توڑنے میں قصاص واجب ہے دانت کے علاوہ کسی بڑی کے توڑنے میں قصاص نہیں
In breaking a tooth, qisas is wajib; in breaking any bone other than a tooth, there is no qisas.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the Hanafi school regarding qisas for bodily injuries. The text establishes a distinction: for the deliberate breaking of a tooth, qisas (retaliation in kind) is wajib (obligatory), but for breaking any other bone (e.g., a finger or arm bone), qisas is not applicable. Instead, only monetary compensation (diyah or arsh) is due. This rule is based on the principle that qisas is limited to wounds where precise equivalence is possible; teeth can be counted and matched, whereas other bones vary in size and shape, making exact retaliation uncertain.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for intentional bodily harm or murder, as prescribed in Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in the text, which of the following requires qisas?
A) Breaking a finger bone
B) Breaking a tooth
C) Breaking an arm bone
D) Breaking a rib

Key Takeaway
Qisas for intentional bodily harm is only wajib for teeth, not for other bones, due to the requirement of precise equivalence.

Qisas Between Different Legal Categories
Rulings on applicability of qisas for wounds between different persons.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on qisas for wounds between different categories of persons and identify when diyah replaces qisas.

Core Idea
Qisas requires precise equivalence; between man-woman, free-slave, and healed wounds, only diyah applies.

This lesson presents key Hanafi rulings on when qisas (retributive justice) is applicable for wounds and when it is not. Understanding these distinctions is critical for correct application of Islamic criminal law, as qisas is not a blanket rule but depends on the categories and conditions of the injury.

Guided Path
1
Identify excluded categories
From the first sentence, list the pairs where qisas is not applicable for wounds: man-woman, free-slave, two slaves.
These pairs are excluded entirely; only diyah is due.
2
Identify the included category
The second sentence states that qisas is wajib between a Muslim and a dhimmi (non-Muslim protected citizen).
This shows equality in inviolability of life and limb.
3
Note the effect of healing
If a wound heals completely with no residual defect, qisas falls away because exact equivalence is lost.
The passage gives the example of cutting half the hand from the wrist.
4
Understand the option when limbs differ
If the victim's limb is sound and the offender's is defective (paralyzed or missing fingers), the victim may choose either qisas (if feasible) or diyah.
This option arises because exact equivalence is possible only if both limbs are similar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مرد اور عورت ، آزاد اور غلام اور دو غلاموں کے درمیان ایک دوسرے کو زخمی کرنے میں قصاص نہیں، اقوال فقہاء مسلم اور ذمی کے درمیان قصاص واجب ہے جس نے کسی کا نصف کلائی سے ہاتھ کاٹا اور جا کہ کفہ زخم لگایا پھر بھی درست ہو گیا اس میں قصاص نہ ہوگا ایک کا ہاتھ صحیح سالم ہے اور دوسرے کا شل (خشک) یا انگلیاں کم ہیں، تو قصاص لینے میں اور دیت لینے میں اختیار ہے
Between a man and a woman, a free person and a slave, and two slaves, there is no qisas for wounding one another. The sayings of the jurists: qisas is wajib between a Muslim and a dhimmi. One who cuts half of someone's hand from the wrist and inflicts a wound that later heals, there is no qisas. If one person's hand is sound and healthy and the other's is paralyzed (dry) or has fewer fingers, then there is choice between taking qisas or taking diyah.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage collects several rulings from the Hanafi school on qisas for injuries. First, it states that between a man and a woman, a free person and a slave, and two slaves, qisas is not applicable for wounds; only diyah (blood money) is payable. However, between a Muslim and a dhimmi (non-Muslim protected citizen), qisas is wajib. Next, if a person cuts off half of another's hand from the wrist and the wound heals completely, there is no qisas because the harm is not precisely equivalent. Finally, if one person's hand is fully functional and the other's is paralyzed or has missing fingers, the victim has the option to choose either qisas (if possible) or diyah. This highlights the principle that qisas requires exact equality in the type and extent of injury.

Key Terms
ذمی (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject living under Muslim rule with a contract of protection.
دیت (diyah): Monetary compensation for bodily harm or death, paid to the victim or heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling for qisas between a Muslim and a dhimmi for a wound?
A) No qisas, only diyah
B) Qisas is wajib
C) Qisas is optional
D) Only if the dhimmi agrees

Key Takeaway
Qisas for wounds requires exact equivalence; when conditions are not met, diyah is the alternative.

Qisas — Retaliation

Hanafi vs Shafi'i on Qisas for Group Killing
Dispute on qisas for multiple killers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on qisas for a group killing and explain the key difference with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
If a group kills one person, all are executed – each participant bears full responsibility.

The Hanafi school holds that when a group jointly commits an intentional murder, every participant is subject to qisas, even if only one life was taken. This directly opposes Imam al-Shafi'i's view that only one life can be taken for one life. This lesson examines the core disagreement, the proofs cited by each side, and the practical consequences in Islamic criminal law.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Ruling
Identify the specific ruling: if a group intentionally kills one person, qisas is taken from all members of the group. Note that this applies regardless of the number of participants.
2
Identify the Hanafi Proof
Locate the evidence the Hanafis rely on. The passage mentions 'proof of the Hanafis' – this is derived from hadith and qiyas. The Prophet ﷺ is reported to have applied qisas to a group in a case of collective killing.
The full hadith is not quoted in the passage due to OCR truncation, but the principle is established.
3
Contrast with the Shafi'i Proof
Identify Imam al-Shafi'i's argument: qisas is a penalty for taking a life, and since only one life was lost, executing multiple people violates the principle of equivalence. The passage references 'proof of Imam Shafi'i' but does not elaborate due to text cut-off.
4
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Assess the practical difference. Under the Hanafi view, all participants are executed. Under the Shafi'i view, only one killer is executed, and the others may face discretionary punishment or diyah. This affects how capital punishment is applied in cases of mob violence or joint criminal ventures.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک جماعت ایک آدمی کو عمدا قتل کر دے تو سب سے قصاص لیا جائے گا۔ ایک نے پوری جماعت کو قتل کر دیا اور تمام اولیاء مقتولین جمع ہو گئے تو قصاص میں یہی قاتل اکیلا ہی قتل ہو گا۔ اقوال فقہاء امام شافعی کی دلیل، احناف کی دلیل۔ جس قاتل پر قصاص تھا وہ فوت ہو جائے تو قصاص ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔
If a group intentionally kills one person, then qisas will be taken from all of them. If one person kills an entire group and all the heirs of the killed persons gather, then in qisas this single killer will be executed alone. Sayings of the jurists: The proof of Imam Shafi'i, the proof of the Hanafis. If the killer on whom qisas was due dies, then qisas is dropped.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage presents a key inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding qisas when multiple persons are involved. The first ruling states that if a group (jama'ah) intentionally kills one person, qisas is applied to all of them according to the Hanafi school. The second ruling states that if one person kills multiple people, he is executed only once, even if all heirs demand qisas. Then the text indicates that the arguments (dalil) of both schools are presented. Unfortunately, the OCR cuts off before the full proofs, but the passage shows the Hanafi position: the entire group can be executed for one murder. The Shafi'i position holds that only one killer can be executed for one life. The text also notes a corollary: if the killer dies before execution, qisas is dropped and diyah may be due. This reflects the Hanafi principle that qisas is a personal right that extinguishes with the death of the obligor.

Key Terms
ولی مقتول (wali al-maqtul): The heir or guardian of the murdered person who has the right to demand qisas or accept diyah.
جماعت (jama'ah): A group of persons who jointly commit an act, here a murder.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for intentional murder or bodily harm, specifically execution in capital cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this lesson, if a group of six people intentionally kills one person, how many are executed in qisas?
A) None; they pay diyah
B) Only the one who struck the fatal blow
C) All six
D) Only one, chosen by the heirs

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that all participants in a group killing are liable for qisas, while the Shafi'i school limits execution to one killer.

Intentional Murder (Qatl Amd): Definition, Proof, and Obligation of Qisas
Defines intentional murder and provides textual proofs for its sin and qisas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of intentional murder, cite the primary textual evidence for its sinfulness and the obligation of qisas, and explain why qisas is restricted to intentional killing.

Core Idea
Intentional murder requires lethal intent plus fatal weapon; it incurs sin and qisas, not diyah.

In this passage from the chapter on crimes, the author provides a detailed treatment of intentional murder (qatl amd). He first defines it by two elements: intention to kill and use of a lethal weapon. He then establishes its rulings through Quranic verses, hadith, and consensus. Understanding this foundational definition is essential for distinguishing intentional murder from other types and for applying the correct punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its two elements
Read the definition: intentional murder requires both the intention to kill (internal) and the use of a weapon or instrument that is typically fatal (external evidence of intention). This distinguishes it from other homicides.
Intention is inferred from the lethal means used.
2
Locate the Quranic proof for sin
Find the verse Surah An-Nisa 93: 'Whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell...' This establishes that intentional murder is a major sin (haram).
Also supported by many hadith and ijma.
3
Locate the proof for qisas obligation
Examine the combination of Surah Al-Baqarah 178 ('Prescribed for you is qisas in cases of murder') and the Prophet's hadith 'al-amdu qawad' (intentional murder is subject to qisas). The hadith restricts the general verse to intentional killing.
Qisas is the maximum punishment, only for the most complete crime.
4
Understand why qisas is restricted to intentional murder
Reflect on the wisdom: intentionality completes the crime (the crime is fully realized) and fulfills the deterrent purpose (zajr). Only intentional killing is a crime of such magnitude that it deserves the ultimate punishment.
This reasoning is used to limit the scope of the qisas verse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الجنايات
وہ دلیل عمد قتل کرنے والے ہتھیار کا استعمال ہے تو وہ اس وقت قتل میں تعمد کرنے والا ہو گا اور قتل عمد کا موجب گناہ ہے۔ اللہ تعالیٰ کے فرمان من يقتل مؤمنا متعمدا فجزاءه جهنم .... الآیۃ کی وجہ سے اور اس کے سلسلہ میں ( قتل میں گناہ کے سلسلہ میں ) بہت سی حدیثیں ناطق ہیں اور اس کے اوپر امت کا اجماع منعقد ہو چکا ہے۔
تشریح پہلے مصنف نے قتل کی پانچ قسمیں بیان فرمائیں۔ یہاں سے قتل عمد کا تفصیلی ذکر ہے۔ تو فرمایا کہ جب کسی انسان کو مارنے کا ارادہ ہو اور اسکے لئے ایسا ہتھیار استعمال کیا جائے جو قتل کرنے والا ہے تو یہ قتل عمد ہے جیسے تلوار، ریوالور، بندوق، توپ وغیرہ ، اور جیسے دھار دار لکڑی اور دھار دار بانس کا چھلکا اور دھار دار پتھر اور جیسے آگ ۔ وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ قتل عمد کے لئے قتل کا ارادہ درکار ہے۔ ارادہ ایک مخفی اور پوشیدہ چیز ہے لہذا جب ارادہ قتل کی دلیل پائی جائے گی تو اسی پر اکتفا کر لیا جائے گا
اور اس کو قتل عمد کہا جائے گا ۔ اور جب قاتل نے ایسے آلات و ہتھیار استعمال کئے جن سے قتل واقع ہوتا ہے تو یہ عمد کی دلیل ہوگی ۔ اور قتل عمد کا حکم یہ ہے کہ اس میں دیت اور کفارہ لازم نہیں آتا بلکہ گناہ اور قصاص لازم آتا ہے اس کو مصنف نے فرمایا کہ قتل عمد کا موجب گناہ ہے اب فرمائیں گے کہ قتل عمد سے گناہ ہوتا ہے اس کی دلیل ایک تو یہ آیت ہے وَمَنْ يَقْتُلْ مُؤْمِنًا مُتَعَمِّدًا فَجَزَاءُ هُ جَهَنَّمَ خَالِدًا فِيهَا وَغَضِبَ اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَ لَعَنَهُ وَ أَعَدَّ لَهُ عَذَابًا عَظِيمًا “ اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ قتل مؤمن گناہ ہے۔ نیز بہت سی احادیث سے قتل کا گناہ ہونا معلوم ہے نیز قتل عمد کے گناہ ہونے پر امت کا اجماع ہے۔
تنبیہ اس آیت پر تفصیلی گفتگو ہم جواہر الفرائد شرح شرح العقائد میں کر چکے ہیں۔ قصاص کون سے قتل سے واجب ہوتا ہے
قال والقود لقوله تعالى كتب عليكم القصاص في القتلى الا انه تقيد بوصف العمدية لقوله عليه السلام "العمد قود" أى موجبه ولان الجناية بها تتكامل وحكمة الزجر عليها تتوفر والعقوبة المتناهية لا شرع لها دون ذلک
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور قصاص اللہ تعالیٰ کے فرمان کُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمُ الْقِصَاصُ فِى الْقَتْلى کی وجہ سے مگر قصاص عمدیت کے وصف کے ساتھ مقید ہے، نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان کی وجہ سے العمد قود ( عمد قصاص ہے ) یعنی عمد کا موجب و حکم قصاص ہے اور اس لئے کہ عمدیت کی وجہ سے جنایت کامل ہو جاتی ہے اور زجر کی حکمت عمدیت پر پوری ہوتی ہے اور آخری درجہ کی عقوبت (سزا ) اس کے لئے قصاص کے علاوہ کوئی چیز مشروع نہیں ہے۔
تشریح گناہ کے ساتھ ساتھ قتل عمد میں قصاص بھی واجب ہوتا ہے کیونکہ قرآن کریم کی یہ آية كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمُ الْقِصَاصُ فِي الْقَتلى وجوب قصاص پر دال ہے۔ سوال آیت میں تو قتل عمد کا ذکر نہیں بلکہ مطلق قتل کا ذکر ہے۔
جواب ایک حدیث نے اس آیت کی تفسیر فرمادی کہ یہاں قتل سے قتل عمد مراد ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے العمد قود یعنی قصاص کا سبب ہے۔
اور آیت میں قتل سے مراد قتل عمد ہے اس کی دلیل یہ بھی ہے کہ پورا پورا جرم عمدیت کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے اور زجر کا بھر پور نفع وفائدہ بھی اسی وقت حاصل ہوگا جب کہ جنایت میں اس نے تعمد کیا ہو نیز سب سے بڑا جرم دنیا میں کسی کوقتل کرنا ہے اور سب سے بڑی سزا قصاص ہے تو قصاص بڑی جنایت میں واجب ہوگا اور قتل بڑی جنایت جب ہو گا جب کہ اس کا عمد ہو ، اس لئے آیت مذکورہ میں وجوب قصاص کو عمدیت کے ساتھ مقید مانا جائے گا۔
قتل عمد کی سزا اور اس کا حکم
قال الا ان يعفو الاولياء او يصالحوا لان الحق لهم ثم هو واجب عينا وليس للولى اخذ الدية الا برضا القاتل وهو احد قولى الشافعى الا ان له حق العدول الى المال من غير مرضاة القاتل لانه تعين مدفعا للهلاك فيجوز بدون رضاه وفي قول الواجب احدهما لا بعينه ويتعين باختياره لان حق العبد شرع جابرا وفي كل واحد نوع جبر فيتخير
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا مگر یہ کہ اولیا معاف کر دیں یا مصالحت کر لیں اس لئے کہ حق اولیاء کا ہے پھر قصاص فرض عین ہے اور ولی کو قاتل کی رضا مندی کے بغیر دیت لینے کا حق نہیں ہے۔ اور یہی شافعی کے دو قولوں میں سے ایک قول ہے، مگر ولی کے لئے قاتل کی رضا مندی کے بغیر مال کی جانب عدول کا حق ہے اس لئے کہ مال ہلاکت کو دور کرنے کا ذریعہ متعین ہے، پس عدول جائز ہوگا بغیر رضاء قاتل کے اور ایک قول میں ہے کہ ان دونوں (قصاص ودیت) میں سے ایک واجب ہے نہ کہ معین طریقہ پر اور کوئی ایک ولی کے اختیار سے متعین ہوتا ہے اس لئے کہ بندہ کا حق مشروع ہوا ہے جابر بن کر ۔ اور ہر ایک میں جبر نقصان ہے تو ولی مختار ہوگا ۔ تشریح قتل عمد کی اصل را قصاص ہے اور یہ بھی فرض عین ہے جس نے قتل کیا ہے اس سے قصاص لیا جائے گا اس کے بدلہ میں دوسرے سے نہیں لیا جائے گا لیکن قصاص اولیاء کا حق ہے اگر وہ معاف کر دیں تو ختم ہو جائے گا یا وہ مصالحت کر لیں اور اس کے بدلہ میں کچھ لے کر قصاص کو چھوڑ دیں تو جائز ہے۔ لیکن قصاص کے بجائے دیت اس وقت واجب ہوگی جب کہ قاتل بھی دیت دینے پر راضی ہو جائے ۔ امام شافعی کے اس میں دو
قول ہیں :- قتل عمد کی سزا تو قصاص ہے لیکن اگر ولی بجائے قصاص کے دیت لینے پر راضی ہو جائے تو اس کو حق ہے، قاتل کی رضامندی ضروری نہیں ہے، وہ فرماتے ہیں کیونکہ دیت دینے سے قاتل کی جان بچ جائے گی۔ اور جان جس طریقہ پر بھی بچ جائے اس کو بچانا حتی الامکان واجب ہے اس لئے جب ولی راضی ہو گیا تو اب قاتل کی رضا مندی کے بغیر بھی اس پر دیت واجب کی جائے گی ۔ - ان کا دوسرا قول یہ ہے کہ قتل عمد میں قصاص اور دیت میں سے ایک واجب ہے جس کو متعین کرنا ولی کے اختیار میں ہے کیونکہ قصاص ہو یا دیت دونوں بندہ کے حق ہیں اور بندہ کا حق وہ ہوتا ہے جس میں نقصان کی تلافی کر دی گئی ہو اور نقصان کی تلافی قصاص میں بھی ہے اور دیت میں بھی تو اب ولی کو اختیار ہوگا جس کو چاہے اختیار کرے۔
Chapter of Crimes: That is the proof of intentional murder: the use of a weapon that kills. So at that time he is one who intends to kill, and intentional murder incurs sin. Due to the command of Allah Most High: 'Whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell...' the verse, and there are many hadiths about it (regarding sin in murder), and the consensus of the Ummah has been established upon it. Commentary: Previously the author stated five types of murder. From here is the detailed mention of intentional murder. He said: When there is an intention to kill a person and for that a weapon is used that is fatal, then it is intentional murder, like a sword, revolver, gun, cannon, etc., and like a sharp stick, sharp bamboo peel, sharp stone, and like fire. The reason is that intentional murder requires the intention to kill. Intention is a hidden and concealed thing; therefore when evidence of intention to kill is found, it will be relied upon and it will be called intentional murder. And when the killer uses such instruments and weapons from which death occurs, that is evidence of intentionality. The ruling of intentional murder is that diyah and kaffarah are not obligatory; rather sin and qisas become obligatory. The author said that intentional murder causes sin. Now he will state that sin occurs from intentional murder. Its proof is this verse: 'And whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell, abiding therein, and Allah has become angry with him and has cursed him and has prepared for him a great punishment.' From this verse it is known that killing a believer is a sin. Also from many hadiths it is known that murder is a sin; also there is consensus of the Ummah on the sinfulness of intentional murder. Note: We have discussed this verse in detail in Jawahir al-Fara'id Sharh Sharh al-'Aqa'id. From which murder does qisas become obligatory? He (al-Quduri) said: 'And qisas, because of Allah's command: 'Prescribed for you is qisas in cases of murder.' But it is restricted by the description of intentionality due to his (peace be upon him) statement: 'Intentional (murder) is qisas,' i.e., its requirement. And because the crime is completed through it, and the wisdom of deterrence is fully realized by it, and there is no extreme punishment legislated other than that.' Translation: al-Quduri said: And qisas is because of Allah's command: 'Prescribed for you is qisas in cases of murder,' but qisas is restricted by the description of intentionality due to the Prophet's statement: 'Intentional (murder) is qisas,' i.e., intentional murder necessitates and is the ruling of qisas. And because through intentionality the crime becomes complete, and the wisdom of deterrence is fully realized upon intentionality, and no extreme punishment other than qisas is legislated for it. Commentary: Along with sin, qisas also becomes obligatory in intentional murder, because this Quranic verse 'Prescribed for you is qisas in cases of murder' indicates the obligation of qisas. Question: The verse does not mention intentional murder but rather absolute murder. Answer: A hadith interpreted this verse: here murder means intentional murder. The hadith states: 'Intentional (murder) is qisas,' i.e., it is the cause of qisas. And that murder in the verse means intentional murder is also evidenced by the fact that the complete crime occurs due to intentionality, and full benefit of deterrence will also be attained only when the crime was committed intentionally. Also, the greatest crime in the world is killing someone, and the greatest punishment is qisas. So qisas will be obligatory for the greatest crime, and murder is the greatest crime only when it is intentional. Therefore, in the mentioned verse, the obligation of qisas will be considered restricted to intentionality. The punishment and ruling of intentional murder: He (al-Quduri) said: 'Unless the heirs pardon or make a compromise, because the right belongs to them. Then it (qisas) is personally obligatory. And the heir does not have the right to take diyah except with the consent of the killer. And this is one of the two sayings of al-Shafi‘i, except that he (al-Shafi‘i) has the right to turn to wealth without the killer's consent, because wealth has been determined as a means of preventing destruction, so it is permissible without his consent. And in one saying: one of the two (qisas and diyah) is obligatory, not specified, and it becomes specified by the heir's choice, because the right of the servant has been legislated as compensatory, and in each there is a type of compensation, so he chooses.' Translation: al-Quduri said: Unless the heirs pardon or make a compromise, because the right belongs to them. Then qisas is fard 'ayn. And the heir does not have the right to take diyah without the killer's consent. And this is one of the two sayings of al-Shafi‘i, except that the heir has the right to turn to wealth without the killer's consent, because wealth is determined as a means of preventing destruction, so turning to it is permissible without the killer's consent. And in one saying: one of the two (qisas and diyah) is obligatory, not on a specified basis, and one becomes specified by the heir's choice, because the servant's right has been legislated as compensatory, and in each there is a type of compensation, so the heir is given a choice. Commentary: The original ruling of intentional murder is qisas, and it is also fard 'ayn. Qisas will be taken from the one who killed, not from someone else. But qisas is the right of the heirs; if they pardon, it becomes void, or they may compromise and take something in exchange and abandon qisas—this is permissible. But diyah in place of qisas will become obligatory only when the killer also agrees to pay diyah. Imam al-Shafi‘i has two sayings in this: First: The punishment of intentional murder is qisas, but if the heir agrees to take diyah instead of qisas, he has the right; the killer's consent is not necessary. He says because paying diyah saves the killer's life, and saving life by any means possible is obligatory. Therefore, when the heir agrees, diyah will be made obligatory on the killer without his consent. His second saying is: In intentional murder, one of the two (qisas or diyah) is obligatory, and it is up to the heir to specify which one, because both qisas and diyah are rights of the servant, and the right of the servant is that in which compensation has been provided. And compensation is found in both qisas and diyah; therefore the heir will have the choice to choose whichever he wants.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a detailed treatment of intentional murder (qatl amd) from the chapter on crimes. It begins by defining intentional murder: it requires both the intention to kill and the use of a weapon or instrument that is typically fatal. Intention is internal, so the law looks to external evidence—if the killer used a lethal weapon, the law presumes intentionality. The author then states the primary ruling: intentional murder incurs sin (ithm) and qisas (retributive execution), not diyah (blood money) or kaffarah (expiation). As proof, he cites the Quranic verse threatening Hell for the intentional killer of a believer, numerous hadiths, and consensus of the Ummah. The passage then addresses the obligation of qisas specifically. The base text from al-Quduri explains that the Quranic command for qisas in cases of murder is restricted by the description of intentionality, as clarified by the Prophet's hadith 'al-amdu qawad' (intentional murder is subject to qisas). The reason is that the crime is fully realized only with intent, and the deterrent purpose of punishment is fully served only when the crime was deliberate. The ultimate punishment (qisas) is only legislated for such a complete crime. The passage then moves to the ruling of qisas: it is a fard 'ayn (personal obligation on the killer) but it is the right of the heirs (awliya). The heirs may pardon or accept a compromise (sulh) in exchange for wealth. However, according to the Hanafi school, they cannot take diyah without the killer's consent. The author then contrasts Imam al-Shafi‘i's two opinions: one that the heirs can take diyah without the killer's consent (because it saves the killer's life), and another that either qisas or diyah is obligatory, and the heir may choose. The Hanafi position insists on the killer's consent because diyah is a substitute for qisas, and the killer must agree to substitute execution with a monetary payment. This passage thus defines the crime, establishes its punishment, and clarifies the procedural rights of both the heirs and the killer within Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
قتل عمد (qatl amd): Intentional murder: killing a person with the intention to kill and using a weapon or instrument that is typically fatal.
قصاص (qisas): Retributive punishment, specifically execution, for intentional murder. It is the right of the heirs, but if they pardon or compromise, it is waived.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT a requirement for an act to be classified as intentional murder (qatl amd)?
A) Intention to kill
B) Use of a weapon that is typically fatal
C) The victim must be a Muslim
D) The victim must die from the act

Key Takeaway
Intentional murder (qatl amd) is defined by intention plus lethal tool; its proof is from Quran, hadith, and ijma, and it mandates sin and qisas.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
7 min
The Heirs' Options: Qisas, Pardon, and the Hanafi–Shafi‘i Dispute on Diyah
Discusses the heirs' right to qisas, pardon, or compromise, and the dispute over taking diyah without the killer's consent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether the heirs can take diyah without the killer's consent, compare it with Imam al-Shafi‘i's two opinions, and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
The heirs may pardon or compromise, but diyah requires the killer's consent in the Hanafi school.

We now turn to the crucial question: what options do the victim's heirs have after an intentional murder? The text explains that while qisas is the default, the heirs may pardon or accept a compromise. However, if they wish to take blood money (diyah), the Hanafi school requires the killer's consent. This sets up a sharp contrast with Imam al-Shafi‘i's two opinions, which allow the heir more control. Understanding this dispute helps clarify the nature of qisas as a right of the heirs versus the killer's right over his own life.

Guided Path
1
State the default: qisas is obligatory but belongs to the heirs
The text states that qisas is fard 'ayn (personally obligatory on the killer) but it is the right of the heirs (awliya). They can demand it, pardon, or make a compromise (sulh).
The killer cannot unilaterally avoid qisas.
2
Identify the Hanafi restriction on diyah
The Hanafi position: 'The heir does not have the right to take diyah except with the consent of the killer.' So diyah requires mutual agreement.
This is the core of the dispute.
3
State the Shafi‘i first opinion (qawl)
Imam al-Shafi‘i's first opinion: the heir can take diyah without the killer's consent because diyah saves the killer's life, and saving life is obligatory.
The killer's life is preserved even without his agreement.
4
State the Shafi‘i second opinion
The second opinion: either qisas or diyah is obligatory, not predetermined, and the heir may choose which to demand. The choice is the heir's.
Both options are seen as compensatory.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In Hanafi: if heir demands diyah but killer refuses, qisas stands. In Shafi‘i first opinion: heir can collect diyah even if killer objects. In second opinion: heir can pick either, and killer complies.
This affects plea bargaining and settlement dynamics.

وہ دلیل عمد قتل کرنے والے ہتھیار کا استعمال ہے تو وہ اس وقت قتل میں تعمد کرنے والا ہو گا اور قتل عمد کا موجب گناہ ہے۔ اللہ تعالیٰ کے فرمان من يقتل مؤمنا متعمدا فجزاءه جهنم .... الآیۃ کی وجہ سے اور اس کے سلسلہ میں ( قتل میں گناہ کے سلسلہ میں ) بہت سی حدیثیں ناطق ہیں اور اس کے اوپر امت کا اجماع منعقد ہو چکا ہے۔
تشریح پہلے مصنف نے قتل کی پانچ قسمیں بیان فرمائیں۔ یہاں سے قتل عمد کا تفصیلی ذکر ہے۔ تو فرمایا کہ جب کسی انسان کو مارنے کا ارادہ ہو اور اسکے لئے ایسا ہتھیار استعمال کیا جائے جو قتل کرنے والا ہے تو یہ قتل عمد ہے جیسے تلوار، ریوالور، بندوق، توپ وغیرہ ، اور جیسے دھار دار لکڑی اور دھار دار بانس کا چھلکا اور دھار دار پتھر اور جیسے آگ ۔ وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ قتل عمد کے لئے قتل کا ارادہ درکار ہے۔ ارادہ ایک مخفی اور پوشیدہ چیز ہے لہذا جب ارادہ قتل کی دلیل پائی جائے گی تو اسی پر اکتفا کر لیا جائے گا
اور اس کو قتل عمد کہا جائے گا ۔ اور جب قاتل نے ایسے آلات و ہتھیار استعمال کئے جن سے قتل واقع ہوتا ہے تو یہ عمد کی دلیل ہوگی ۔ اور قتل عمد کا حکم یہ ہے کہ اس میں دیت اور کفارہ لازم نہیں آتا بلکہ گناہ اور قصاص لازم آتا ہے اس کو مصنف نے فرمایا کہ قتل عمد کا موجب گناہ ہے اب فرمائیں گے کہ قتل عمد سے گناہ ہوتا ہے اس کی دلیل ایک تو یہ آیت ہے وَمَنْ يَقْتُلْ مُؤْمِنًا مُتَعَمِّدًا فَجَزَاءُ هُ جَهَنَّمَ خَالِدًا فِيهَا وَغَضِبَ اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَ لَعَنَهُ وَ أَعَدَّ لَهُ عَذَابًا عَظِيمًا “ اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ قتل مؤمن گناہ ہے۔ نیز بہت سی احادیث سے قتل کا گناہ ہونا معلوم ہے نیز قتل عمد کے گناہ ہونے پر امت کا اجماع ہے۔
تنبیہ اس آیت پر تفصیلی گفتگو ہم جواہر الفرائد شرح شرح العقائد میں کر چکے ہیں۔ قصاص کون سے قتل سے واجب ہوتا ہے
قال والقود لقوله تعالى كتب عليكم القصاص في القتلى الا انه تقيد بوصف العمدية لقوله عليه السلام "العمد قود" أى موجبه ولان الجناية بها تتكامل وحكمة الزجر عليها تتوفر والعقوبة المتناهية لا شرع لها دون ذلک
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور قصاص اللہ تعالیٰ کے فرمان کُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمُ الْقِصَاصُ فِى الْقَتْلى کی وجہ سے مگر قصاص عمدیت کے وصف کے ساتھ مقید ہے، نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان کی وجہ سے العمد قود ( عمد قصاص ہے ) یعنی عمد کا موجب و حکم قصاص ہے اور اس لئے کہ عمدیت کی وجہ سے جنایت کامل ہو جاتی ہے اور زجر کی حکمت عمدیت پر پوری ہوتی ہے اور آخری درجہ کی عقوبت (سزا ) اس کے لئے قصاص کے علاوہ کوئی چیز مشروع نہیں ہے۔
تشریح گناہ کے ساتھ ساتھ قتل عمد میں قصاص بھی واجب ہوتا ہے کیونکہ قرآن کریم کی یہ آية كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمُ الْقِصَاصُ فِي الْقَتلى وجوب قصاص پر دال ہے۔ سوال آیت میں تو قتل عمد کا ذکر نہیں بلکہ مطلق قتل کا ذکر ہے۔
جواب ایک حدیث نے اس آیت کی تفسیر فرمادی کہ یہاں قتل سے قتل عمد مراد ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے العمد قود یعنی قصاص کا سبب ہے۔
اور آیت میں قتل سے مراد قتل عمد ہے اس کی دلیل یہ بھی ہے کہ پورا پورا جرم عمدیت کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے اور زجر کا بھر پور نفع وفائدہ بھی اسی وقت حاصل ہوگا جب کہ جنایت میں اس نے تعمد کیا ہو نیز سب سے بڑا جرم دنیا میں کسی کوقتل کرنا ہے اور سب سے بڑی سزا قصاص ہے تو قصاص بڑی جنایت میں واجب ہوگا اور قتل بڑی جنایت جب ہو گا جب کہ اس کا عمد ہو ، اس لئے آیت مذکورہ میں وجوب قصاص کو عمدیت کے ساتھ مقید مانا جائے گا۔
قتل عمد کی سزا اور اس کا حکم
قال الا ان يعفو الاولياء او يصالحوا لان الحق لهم ثم هو واجب عينا وليس للولى اخذ الدية الا برضا القاتل وهو احد قولى الشافعى الا ان له حق العدول الى المال من غير مرضاة القاتل لانه تعين مدفعا للهلاك فيجوز بدون رضاه وفي قول الواجب احدهما لا بعينه ويتعين باختياره لان حق العبد شرع جابرا وفي كل واحد نوع جبر فيتخير
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا مگر یہ کہ اولیا معاف کر دیں یا مصالحت کر لیں اس لئے کہ حق اولیاء کا ہے پھر قصاص فرض عین ہے اور ولی کو قاتل کی رضا مندی کے بغیر دیت لینے کا حق نہیں ہے۔ اور یہی شافعی کے دو قولوں میں سے ایک قول ہے، مگر ولی کے لئے قاتل کی رضا مندی کے بغیر مال کی جانب عدول کا حق ہے اس لئے کہ مال ہلاکت کو دور کرنے کا ذریعہ متعین ہے، پس عدول جائز ہوگا بغیر رضاء قاتل کے اور ایک قول میں ہے کہ ان دونوں (قصاص ودیت) میں سے ایک واجب ہے نہ کہ معین طریقہ پر اور کوئی ایک ولی کے اختیار سے متعین ہوتا ہے اس لئے کہ بندہ کا حق مشروع ہوا ہے جابر بن کر ۔ اور ہر ایک میں جبر نقصان ہے تو ولی مختار ہوگا ۔ تشریح قتل عمد کی اصل را قصاص ہے اور یہ بھی فرض عین ہے جس نے قتل کیا ہے اس سے قصاص لیا جائے گا اس کے بدلہ میں دوسرے سے نہیں لیا جائے گا لیکن قصاص اولیاء کا حق ہے اگر وہ معاف کر دیں تو ختم ہو جائے گا یا وہ مصالحت کر لیں اور اس کے بدلہ میں کچھ لے کر قصاص کو چھوڑ دیں تو جائز ہے۔ لیکن قصاص کے بجائے دیت اس وقت واجب ہوگی جب کہ قاتل بھی دیت دینے پر راضی ہو جائے ۔ امام شافعی کے اس میں دو
قول ہیں :- قتل عمد کی سزا تو قصاص ہے لیکن اگر ولی بجائے قصاص کے دیت لینے پر راضی ہو جائے تو اس کو حق ہے، قاتل کی رضامندی ضروری نہیں ہے، وہ فرماتے ہیں کیونکہ دیت دینے سے قاتل کی جان بچ جائے گی۔ اور جان جس طریقہ پر بھی بچ جائے اس کو بچانا حتی الامکان واجب ہے اس لئے جب ولی راضی ہو گیا تو اب قاتل کی رضا مندی کے بغیر بھی اس پر دیت واجب کی جائے گی ۔ - ان کا دوسرا قول یہ ہے کہ قتل عمد میں قصاص اور دیت میں سے ایک واجب ہے جس کو متعین کرنا ولی کے اختیار میں ہے کیونکہ قصاص ہو یا دیت دونوں بندہ کے حق ہیں اور بندہ کا حق وہ ہوتا ہے جس میں نقصان کی تلافی کر دی گئی ہو اور نقصان کی تلافی قصاص میں بھی ہے اور دیت میں بھی تو اب ولی کو اختیار ہوگا جس کو چاہے اختیار کرے۔
Chapter of Crimes: That is the proof of intentional murder: the use of a weapon that kills. So at that time he is one who intends to kill, and intentional murder incurs sin. Due to the command of Allah Most High: 'Whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell...' the verse, and there are many hadiths about it (regarding sin in murder), and the consensus of the Ummah has been established upon it. Commentary: Previously the author stated five types of murder. From here is the detailed mention of intentional murder. He said: When there is an intention to kill a person and for that a weapon is used that is fatal, then it is intentional murder, like a sword, revolver, gun, cannon, etc., and like a sharp stick, sharp bamboo peel, sharp stone, and like fire. The reason is that intentional murder requires the intention to kill. Intention is a hidden and concealed thing; therefore when evidence of intention to kill is found, it will be relied upon and it will be called intentional murder. And when the killer uses such instruments and weapons from which death occurs, that is evidence of intentionality. The ruling of intentional murder is that diyah and kaffarah are not obligatory; rather sin and qisas become obligatory. The author said that intentional murder causes sin. Now he will state that sin occurs from intentional murder. Its proof is this verse: 'And whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell, abiding therein, and Allah has become angry with him and has cursed him and has prepared for him a great punishment.' From this verse it is known that killing a believer is a sin. Also from many hadiths it is known that murder is a sin; also there is consensus of the Ummah on the sinfulness of intentional murder. Note: We have discussed this verse in detail in Jawahir al-Fara'id Sharh Sharh al-'Aqa'id. From which murder does qisas become obligatory? He (al-Quduri) said: 'And qisas, because of Allah's command: 'Prescribed for you is qisas in cases of murder.' But it is restricted by the description of intentionality due to his (peace be upon him) statement: 'Intentional (murder) is qisas,' i.e., its requirement. And because the crime is completed through it, and the wisdom of deterrence is fully realized by it, and there is no extreme punishment legislated other than that.' Translation: al-Quduri said: And qisas is because of Allah's command: 'Prescribed for you is qisas in cases of murder,' but qisas is restricted by the description of intentionality due to the Prophet's statement: 'Intentional (murder) is qisas,' i.e., intentional murder necessitates and is the ruling of qisas. And because through intentionality the crime becomes complete, and the wisdom of deterrence is fully realized upon intentionality, and no extreme punishment other than qisas is legislated for it. Commentary: Along with sin, qisas also becomes obligatory in intentional murder, because this Quranic verse 'Prescribed for you is qisas in cases of murder' indicates the obligation of qisas. Question: The verse does not mention intentional murder but rather absolute murder. Answer: A hadith interpreted this verse: here murder means intentional murder. The hadith states: 'Intentional (murder) is qisas,' i.e., it is the cause of qisas. And that murder in the verse means intentional murder is also evidenced by the fact that the complete crime occurs due to intentionality, and full benefit of deterrence will also be attained only when the crime was committed intentionally. Also, the greatest crime in the world is killing someone, and the greatest punishment is qisas. So qisas will be obligatory for the greatest crime, and murder is the greatest crime only when it is intentional. Therefore, in the mentioned verse, the obligation of qisas will be considered restricted to intentionality. The punishment and ruling of intentional murder: He (al-Quduri) said: 'Unless the heirs pardon or make a compromise, because the right belongs to them. Then it (qisas) is personally obligatory. And the heir does not have the right to take diyah except with the consent of the killer. And this is one of the two sayings of al-Shafi‘i, except that he (al-Shafi‘i) has the right to turn to wealth without the killer's consent, because wealth has been determined as a means of preventing destruction, so it is permissible without his consent. And in one saying: one of the two (qisas and diyah) is obligatory, not specified, and it becomes specified by the heir's choice, because the right of the servant has been legislated as compensatory, and in each there is a type of compensation, so he chooses.' Translation: al-Quduri said: Unless the heirs pardon or make a compromise, because the right belongs to them. Then qisas is fard 'ayn. And the heir does not have the right to take diyah without the killer's consent. And this is one of the two sayings of al-Shafi‘i, except that the heir has the right to turn to wealth without the killer's consent, because wealth is determined as a means of preventing destruction, so turning to it is permissible without the killer's consent. And in one saying: one of the two (qisas and diyah) is obligatory, not on a specified basis, and one becomes specified by the heir's choice, because the servant's right has been legislated as compensatory, and in each there is a type of compensation, so the heir is given a choice. Commentary: The original ruling of intentional murder is qisas, and it is also fard 'ayn. Qisas will be taken from the one who killed, not from someone else. But qisas is the right of the heirs; if they pardon, it becomes void, or they may compromise and take something in exchange and abandon qisas—this is permissible. But diyah in place of qisas will become obligatory only when the killer also agrees to pay diyah. Imam al-Shafi‘i has two sayings in this: First: The punishment of intentional murder is qisas, but if the heir agrees to take diyah instead of qisas, he has the right; the killer's consent is not necessary. He says because paying diyah saves the killer's life, and saving life by any means possible is obligatory. Therefore, when the heir agrees, diyah will be made obligatory on the killer without his consent. His second saying is: In intentional murder, one of the two (qisas or diyah) is obligatory, and it is up to the heir to specify which one, because both qisas and diyah are rights of the servant, and the right of the servant is that in which compensation has been provided. And compensation is found in both qisas and diyah; therefore the heir will have the choice to choose whichever he wants.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a detailed treatment of intentional murder (qatl amd) from the chapter on crimes. It begins by defining intentional murder: it requires both the intention to kill and the use of a weapon or instrument that is typically fatal. Intention is internal, so the law looks to external evidence—if the killer used a lethal weapon, the law presumes intentionality. The author then states the primary ruling: intentional murder incurs sin (ithm) and qisas (retributive execution), not diyah (blood money) or kaffarah (expiation). As proof, he cites the Quranic verse threatening Hell for the intentional killer of a believer, numerous hadiths, and consensus of the Ummah. The passage then addresses the obligation of qisas specifically. The base text from al-Quduri explains that the Quranic command for qisas in cases of murder is restricted by the description of intentionality, as clarified by the Prophet's hadith 'al-amdu qawad' (intentional murder is subject to qisas). The reason is that the crime is fully realized only with intent, and the deterrent purpose of punishment is fully served only when the crime was deliberate. The ultimate punishment (qisas) is only legislated for such a complete crime. The passage then moves to the ruling of qisas: it is a fard 'ayn (personal obligation on the killer) but it is the right of the heirs (awliya). The heirs may pardon or accept a compromise (sulh) in exchange for wealth. However, according to the Hanafi school, they cannot take diyah without the killer's consent. The author then contrasts Imam al-Shafi‘i's two opinions: one that the heirs can take diyah without the killer's consent (because it saves the killer's life), and another that either qisas or diyah is obligatory, and the heir may choose. The Hanafi position insists on the killer's consent because diyah is a substitute for qisas, and the killer must agree to substitute execution with a monetary payment. This passage thus defines the crime, establishes its punishment, and clarifies the procedural rights of both the heirs and the killer within Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
دیت (diyah): Blood money; a financial compensation paid to the heirs of the victim in lieu of qisas. In intentional murder, it requires the killer's consent according to the Hanafi school.
اولیاء (awliya): The legal heirs of the victim who have the right to demand qisas, pardon, or accept diyah or compromise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is required for the heirs to take diyah in exchange for qisas in intentional murder?
A) Only the heirs' consent
B) The killer's consent and the heirs' consent
C) A court order
D) Payment within one year

Key Takeaway
Qisas is the default; diyah in intentional murder requires the killer's consent according to the Hanafi school, unlike the Shafi‘i view that allows the heir to take it without consent.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
6 min
Why Qisas is Primary: Hanafi Proofs against Diyah for 'Amd
Stating the Hanafi evidence for qisas as the primary punishment for intentional murder

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the primary punishment for intentional murder, identify the textual and rational proofs, and explain why diyah is not a substitute without consent.

Core Idea
Property is not equivalent to life — qisas, not diyah, is the wajib punishment for intentional murder.

In this passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya, the author lays out the Hanafi case that qisas (retribution) is the only proper punishment for intentional murder (qatl 'amd), countering the Shafi'i view that diyah (blood money) may also serve. You will examine the key textual and rational proofs, including the Quranic imperative and the principle of mumathalah (equivalence).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling for intentional murder according to the Hanafi school: qisas is wajib, diyah is not an alternative.
The passage begins by contrasting the Hanafi view with that of Imam al-Shafi'i.
2
Identify the disagreement
Which school opposes and on what basis? The Shafi'i school holds that diyah can also be a punishment for intentional murder.
The specific Shafi'i proof is not detailed here, but the disagreement is clear.
3
Follow the Hanafi textual proof
What Quranic verse and hadith are cited, and how do they indicate obligation? The verse 'kutiba 'alaykum al-qisas fi al-qatla' (2:178) uses an imperative form indicating wajib. The hadith 'al-amdu qawad' (retaliation for intentional killing) reinforces this.
The passage mentions both proofs; note that 'al-amdu fawad' is likely a scribal error for 'al-amdu qawad'.
4
Analyse the rational proof
Why is property unsuitable? Explain the lack of mumathalah (equivalence) between property and life, and the social benefits of qisas: deterrence (zajr) and consolation (jabr).
The passage argues that a person is an owner, not an owned thing; thus life and property are incommensurable.
5
Determine the practical difference
Thamarah al-khilaf: how would a Hanafi vs Shafi'i judge rule? A Hanafi judge would enforce qisas unless the family pardons or compromises; a Shafi'i judge could impose diyah even without full consent.
This illustrates the real-world impact of the madhhab dispute.

ولنا ما تلونا من الكتاب وروينا من السنة ولان المال لا يصلح موجبا لعدم المماثلة والقصاص يصلح للتماثل وفيه مصلحة الاحياء زجرا وجبرا فيتعين وفى الخطأ وجوب المال ضرورة صون الدم عن الاهدار ولا يتيقن بعدم قصد الولى بعد اخذ المال فلا يتعين مدفعا للهلاك

سوال آپ بھی تو فرماتے ہیں کہ مصالحت میں مال لینا جائز ہے حالانکہ یہ گارنٹی تو وہاں بھی نہیں ہے؟ جواب ان دونوں میں فرق ہے ، مصالحت میں ولی نے مال لینے پر رضامندی ظاہر کی ہے تو یہاں ظاہر ہے کہ اب وہ ایسا نہیں کر دیگا۔ اور آپ نے فرمایا کہ بغیر قاتل کی رضا مندی کے اس پر بجائے قصاص کے مال واجب کر دیا جائے تو چونکہ یہاں طبیعت میں بغض ہے تو یہاں ظاہر حال یہ ہے کہ وہ دل کی بھڑاس نکالنے کیلئے موقع پا کر قتل کر سکتا ہے۔
This is the book of jinayat. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary of Hidaya volume 15. These are the sayings of Imam Shafi‘i, and in our view the original punishment for intentional murder is qisas, not diyah. Our proof is this. The rational and textual proofs of the Hanafis: And we have what we recited from the Book and what we narrated from the Sunnah, and because property is not suitable as a cause due to lack of equivalence, and qisas is suitable for equivalence, and in it is the benefit of life for deterrence and consolation, so it is determined. And in unintentional (murder), the obligation of property is out of necessity to protect blood from being wasted, and one cannot be certain of the lack of intention of the guardian after taking the property, so property is not determined as a deflector of destruction. Translation: And our proof is that verse of the Book of Allah which we have recited and that hadith which we have narrated. And because property does not have the capacity to become a cause for killing due to lack of equivalence, and qisas has the capacity due to equivalence, and qisas is a benefit for the living in terms of deterrence and consolation, so qisas is determined. And in unintentional killing, the obligation of property is based on the necessity of protecting the blood of the slain from being wasted. And after taking property, one cannot be certain of the guardian's intention, so property will not be determined as a deflector of destruction. Explanation: Here our proof is mentioned. The first proof is the mentioned verse: 'Prescribed for you is qisas in cases of killing', and the mentioned hadith, i.e., 'al-amdu fawad' (intentional killing demands blood money/retribution). From both it is understood that the original cause of killing is qisas. Rational proof: There is no equivalence between property and life because a person is an owner and property is owned, so there is no equivalence between property and life. However, between person and person there is equivalence, therefore qisas is determined. And the second reason is that in qisas there is benefit for the living, because when a person intends to kill his enemy, he will consider his end (qisas) and will refrain from his action. So in qisas there is deterrence and also consolation, because when the killer is executed in qisas, the heirs of the slain become fearless and satisfied, otherwise they would remain fearful because they fear being killed by the killer, as the killer worries that the heirs might take an opportunity to eliminate him, so he tries to eliminate them first. In any case, in qisas there is both deterrence and consolation, therefore qisas is the cause of killing. Question: When there is no equivalence between the slain and property, why is diyah made obligatory in unintentional killing? And killing is a very heavy crime, but in unintentional killing the killer is excused, so qisas becomes impossible. And if we let the killer go free, that is against the respect of humanity, and the respect of the sacred life does not disappear due to the excuse of unintentional killing. Therefore, so that blood does not go in vain, diyah is made obligatory. Question: What is the answer to 'because it is determined as a deflector of destruction'? Answer: What guarantee is there that after taking the property the guardian will not kill the killer? It is possible that he takes the property and then, given the opportunity, he also kills the killer. So to say that property is determined to deflect destruction is unproven. Question: You also say that in compromise (sulh) taking property is permissible, although there is no such guarantee there? Answer: There is a difference between these two. In sulh, the guardian has expressed consent to take the property, so it is apparent that now he will not do such a thing. And if one says that without the killer's consent property is made obligatory on him instead of qisas, since here there is enmity in nature, the apparent situation is that he may kill on getting an opportunity to vent his fury.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya presents the Hanafi proof that the primary punishment for intentional murder (qatl 'amd) is qisas (retaliation), not diyah (blood money). The author begins by stating that the Shafi'i view differs, and then provides both textual and rational arguments. The textual proof is the Quranic verse 'kutiba 'alaykum al-qisas fi al-qatla' (2:178) and a hadith (though the text records 'al-amdu fawad' which is likely a scribal error for 'al-amdu qawad' meaning intentional killing demands retaliation). The rational proof rests on the absence of equivalence (mumathala) between property and life: a person is a free owner (malik) while property is owned (mamluk), so no equivalence exists, whereas between two humans there is full equivalence, thus qisas is appropriate. Additionally, qisas serves a social benefit (maslaha): it deters potential killers and consoles the victim's family. The author then addresses two objections. First, why is diyah obligatory in unintentional killing? The answer is that in unintentional killing, qisas is impossible because the killer is not a deliberate aggressor, but to avoid the victim's blood being wasted, diyah is imposed as a practical measure. Second, if property (diyah) is said to be a 'deflector of destruction' (mudfa' lil halak), there is no guarantee that the guardian will not kill the killer after accepting diyah. The author distinguishes this from sulh (compromise) where the guardian's consent to accept property indicates he will not seek retaliation; here, absent consent, the guardian may still kill out of vengeance, so property cannot serve as a reliable substitute for qisas.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment of death for intentional homicide, equivalent to the crime.
دیت (diyah): Blood money paid to the victim's heirs as compensation for homicide.
مماثلت (mumathalah): Equivalence or similarity; in law, the basis for qisas is the equality of perpetrator and victim in essential human attributes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi proofs in this passage, why can diyah (blood money) not be the primary punishment for intentional murder?
A) Because the Quran explicitly prohibits diyah for intentional murder.
B) Because there is no equivalence (mumathalah) between property and life, so property cannot justly replace life.
C) Because the hadith states that the killer must be executed regardless of circumstances.
D) Because the victim's family always prefers qisas.

Key Takeaway
Qisas is the wajib punishment for intentional murder in Hanafi law; diyah cannot substitute without the guardian's consent due to the lack of equivalence between property and life.

The Hanafi Position on Kaffara for Intentional Murder
Stating the Hanafi position that kaffara is not required for intentional murder

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that no kaffara is due for intentional murder, explain the two Hanafi proofs, and evaluate the Shafi'i qiyas aulawi argument.

Core Idea
Kaffara is not attached to a pure major sin; it is a prescribed measure limited by the Lawgiver and not subject to analogy.

One of the most important inter-madhhab disputes in criminal fiqh is whether intentional murder (qatl al-'amd) requires kaffara (expiation). The Shafi'i school argues that if kaffara is required for unintentional murder (khata'), it should be all the more required for intentional murder. The Hanafi school rejects this, providing two decisive proofs rooted in the nature of sin and the law's structure. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi reasoning and the practical consequences of the disagreement.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What exactly does the Hanafi school hold regarding kaffara for intentional murder? Identify the ruling and its evidence.
The ruling is 'no kaffara' (لا كفارة).
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection and its proof
What is the Shafi'i argument? They use qiyas aulawi (a fortiori analogy) from unintentional murder. Understand the logic: if kaffara is wajib for a lesser sin, it should be wajib for a greater one.
This is a type of qiyas where the far' (new case) is more deserving of the ruling than the asl.
3
Analyse the first Hanafi response: the nature of the sin
The Hanafis argue that intentional murder is a 'pure major sin' (kabira mahda). Kaffara is an act of worship ('ibada) designed for purification. Worship cannot be attached to the utmost severity of sin.
This is a qualitative argument: the enormity of the sin prevents it from being the occasion for an act of worship.
4
Analyse the second Hanafi response: prescribed measures
Kaffara is a 'prescribed measure' (muqaddirat) limited to its textual occasions. The Lawgiver prescribed kaffara only for the lesser sin (unintentional murder). Extending it by analogy to a greater sin is invalid because muqaddirat are not subject to qiyas.
This is an usul al-fiqh principle: fixed measures cannot be extended by analogy.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference between the two schools in a real case? A Shafi'i judge would impose kaffara (e.g., fasting two months) in addition to qisas; a Hanafi judge would not. This affects the killer's obligations.
Also note an ancillary ruling: the killer is deprived of inheritance, which is agreed upon but mentioned here as a supporting point.

Is kaffara obligatory in intentional murder or not? Sayings of the jurists. And there is no kaffara in it according to us, and according to al-Shafi'i it is obligatory, because the need for expiation in intentional (murder) is more pressing than in unintentional (murder), so it is more deserving of being made obligatory. And our proof is that it is a pure major sin, and in kaffara there is the meaning of worship, so it is not attached to the likes of this (sin). And because kaffara is among the prescribed measures (muqaddirat), and its determination in the law is to repel the lesser (sin), it is not determined to repel the greater. And among its rulings is deprivation of inheritance due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'A killer does not inherit.' Translation: And according to us, there is no kaffara in it, and according to al-Shafi'i it is obligatory, because the need for expiation in intentional (murder) is more intense than the need in unintentional murder, so this (intentional murder) is more deserving of making kaffara obligatory. And our proof is that this is a pure major sin, and in kaffara there is the meaning of worship, so kaffara will not be attached to the like of this (sin). And because kaffara is among the prescribed measures in the law, and its determination in the law is to repel the lesser (sin), so kaffara will not be determined to repel the greater. And among the rulings of intentional murder is deprivation of inheritance due to the Prophet's statement: 'A killer does not inherit.' (There is no inheritance for a killer). Explanation: Is kaffara obligatory in intentional murder or not? So according to Imam al-Shafi'i it is obligatory, and according to us it is not obligatory. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that when kaffara is obligatory in unintentional murder, then in intentional murder it should be obligatory a fortiori (first of all). Our proof: 1. Intentional murder is a major sin (kabira) and a very severe major sin, and kaffara has the meaning of worship, so how can kaffara, which is worship, be attached to such a great sin? 2. Kaffara is not made obligatory by personal opinion, but by the determination of the law. And the law has determined kaffara to remove the sin that is in unintentional murder, and that sin is light. So through analogical contrivances (qiyasi tagbandiyan), kaffara cannot be determined to remove (the sin) that is in intentional murder, which is a very heavy sin. The ruling of intentional murder is that the killer will not receive inheritance, because the hadith states that the killer does not inherit, i.e., he does not inherit anything. (And we have detailed it in the lesson of al-Siraji).
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage addresses the dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding whether kaffara (expiation) is required for intentional murder. The Hanafi position, stated by the author, is that no kaffara is due for intentional murder. The Shafi'i argument, based on qiyas aulawi (a fortiori analogy), holds that if kaffara is required for unintentional murder, it should be all the more required for intentional murder, which is graver. The Hanafi response consists of two main arguments. First, intentional murder is a 'pure major sin' (kabira mahda). Kaffara, being an act of worship ('ibada), cannot be attached to such a severe sin, as worship is meant to purify from lesser faults, not to expiate a heinous crime that deserves punishment (qisas or the Hereafter). Second, kaffara belongs to the category of 'prescribed measures' (muqaddirat) in Islamic law, which are fixed by the Lawgiver for specific purposes. The Shari'a has prescribed kaffara only for the lesser sin of unintentional killing. One cannot extend this ruling to a greater sin through analogical reasoning (qiyas), because the law's limits must be respected. Additionally, the passage notes that among the rulings of intentional murder is that the killer is deprived of inheritance, citing the hadith 'a killer does not inherit' — this is mentioned as a parallel ruling that follows from the gravity of the crime, further supporting the idea that kaffara is not an appropriate remedy.

Key Terms
کفارہ (kaffara): Expiation or atonement for a sin, typically by fasting, feeding the poor, or freeing a slave, prescribed in the Shari'a for certain violations.
كبيرة (kabirah): A major sin (kabirah) as distinct from minor sins (sagha'ir).
مقادير (muqaddirat): Prescribed measures or fixed quantities in Islamic law, such as the number of lashes, the amount of diyah, or the specific acts of kaffara.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because intentional murder is a pure major sin, and kaffara is an act of worship that cannot be attached to such a sin.
C) Because the killer can pay diyah which replaces kaffara.
D) Because kaffara would be too easy and thus insufficient for intentional murder.

Key Takeaway
Kaffara is not obligatory for intentional murder because it is a pure major sin and kaffara is a prescribed measure not subject to analogy.

Kaffarah in Intentional Murder: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute over wajib of kaffarah in 'amd murder

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on kaffarah in 'amd murder and explain the two Hanafi proofs against its obligation.

Core Idea
Kaffarah in 'amd murder is wajib according to Shafi'i but not according to Hanafis because worship cannot be attached to a pure major sin.

This lesson examines a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the obligation of kaffarah (expiation) in intentional murder ('amd). While Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the greater sin demands greater expiation, the Hanafi school maintains that kaffarah is an act of worship that cannot be caused by a grave sin, and that its fixed measure cannot be extended by analogy. Understanding this dispute reveals important Hanafi principles regarding the nature of worship and the role of qiyas in ibadat.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school holds kaffarah is not wajib in 'amd murder. The matn states: 'Wa la kaffarata fihi indana'.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that kaffarah is wajib in 'amd murder, based on an a fortiori analogy (qiyas awla) from khata'.
The opposing dalil is a qiyas.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i argument: If kaffarah is wajib in accidental killing (which has less sin), then it should be even more obligatory in intentional killing (which has greater sin).
This is a form of qiyas awla or mafhum al-muwafaqa.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response has two parts: (1) 'Amd is a pure major sin, and kaffarah is worship; worship cannot be attached to such a sin. (2) Kaffarah is a fixed measure (tawqifi) specified for the lesser sin; it cannot be extended by qiyas to the greater.
The hadith on inheritance (la miratha li qatil) is cited as a separate ruling for 'amd.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: A Hanafi who commits 'amd murder does not perform kaffarah (only qisas or diyah apply), while a Shafi'i would owe kaffarah in addition to other penalties.
This difference affects the perpetrator's religious obligations.

Commentary: Is expiation obligatory in intentional murder or not? According to Imam al-Shafi'i, expiation is obligatory, and according to us it is not obligatory. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that when expiation is obligatory in unintentional killing, then in intentional killing it should be even more obligatory. Our proof: 1. Intentional murder is a major sin, and a very severe major sin, and expiation has the meaning of worship, so how can worship be made obligatory for such a major sin? 2. Expiation is not obligated by personal opinion but by the determination of the Shari'ah, and the Shari'ah has determined expiation for removing the sin that is in unintentional killing, which is a light sin, so through analogical constructions it cannot be determined for removing the sin that is in intentional murder, which is a very heavy sin. Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the obligation of kaffarah (expiation) in intentional murder ('amd). The base text is from al-Quduri's matn, and the sharh expands on it. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that kaffarah is wajib in 'amd murder, drawing an a fortiori analogy (qiyas awla) from khata' (unintentional) murder: if it is wajib in the lesser sin (khata'), it should be all the more wajib in the greater sin ('amd). The Hanafi school (represented by 'indana') holds that it is not wajib. Their proof is twofold: (1) 'Amd is a pure major sin (kabirah mahdah), and kaffarah is an act of worship ('ibadah). Worship is not attached to such a grave sin as its cause (sabab) — meaning that the Shari'ah does not make a major sin the occasion for an act of worship. (2) Kaffarah is a fixed measure (min al-maqadir) determined by the Shari'ah for a specific purpose — removing the lesser sin (al-adna). It cannot be extended by analogy to remove the greater sin (al-a'la). Additionally, the text mentions another ruling for 'amd: the killer is deprived of inheritance, based on the hadith 'la miratha li qatil'. The Hanafi position is that the killer does not inherit from the victim, regardless of whether the killing was intentional or unintentional, but here it is mentioned as a consequence of 'amd. The commentary further explains the two proofs in simpler Urdu, emphasizing that kaffarah cannot be established by human reasoning (qiyas) for such a heavy sin; it must be textually specified by the Shari'ah, and the text specifies it for khata' only.

Key Terms
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation; a compensatory act of worship (like fasting or feeding the poor) required for certain sins or omissions.
كبيرة محضة (kabirah mahdah): Pure major sin; a sin that is entirely grave with no mitigating factor.
مقادير (maqadir): Fixed measures or quantities determined by the Shari'ah (e.g., number of fasts, amount of food for kaffarah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis reject the obligation of kaffarah in 'amd murder, despite its wajib in khata'?
A) Because 'amd murder is a minor sin.
B) Because kaffarah is an act of worship, and worship cannot be attached to a pure major sin.
C) Because the hadith on inheritance overrides the qiyas.
D) Because the Shafi'i position is based on a weak hadith.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not require kaffarah for intentional murder because it is a pure major sin and the fixed measures of kaffarah cannot be extended by analogy.

Defining Qatl Shibh Amd: The Dispute Between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Defining qatl shibh amd and presenting the dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of qatl shibh amd according to Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and evaluate the difference based on the hadith proof.

Core Idea
The classification of killing as shibh amd or amd turns on the tool: nature vs. usual lethality.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah defines the third category of homicide—qatl shibh amd (quasi-intentional killing)—and presents a key dispute among the Hanafi masters. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree on what makes a killing 'quasi-intentional'. The dispute hinges on whether the tool's usual lethality matters or only its status as a weapon. This lesson unpacks the definitions, the hadith proof, and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Definitions
First, extract the precise definitions of qatl shibh amd given by Imam Abu Hanifa and by the Sahibayn (and Imam Shafi'i). Note the key phrase 'بما لا يقتل به غالبا' (that which does not usually cause death).
2
Analyze the Hadith Proof
Imam Abu Hanifa cites the hadith: 'إلا أن قتيل خطأ العمد قتيل السوط والعصا' (the victim of khata' al-amd is the victim of the whip and the stick). Identify the operative phrase and its absolute nature ('العصا' without qualification).
3
Compare the Interpretation of the Sahibayn
The Sahibayn restrict 'العصا' to a small stick (chhari) that does not usually kill, excluding a large stick (lathi) which they classify as amd. Understand why they differentiate based on usual lethality.
4
Evaluate the Wajh al-Dalalah
Determine how the hadith supports each view. The Hanafi response argues that restricting the absolute word is invalid (ibtal al-mutlaq). Understand the principle of 'al-mutlaq yajri 'ala itlaqihi'.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Calculate the practical difference: for a heavy stick or large stone, Abu Hanifa rules shibh amd (diyah on aqila, no qisas), while the Sahibayn rule amd (qisas). This difference can save or cost a life.

Book of Homicides. What is Qatl Shibh Amd? Statements of Fuqaha. He said: Shibh Amd according to Abu Hanifa is that he intentionally strikes with what is not a weapon nor considered equivalent to a weapon. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said, and it is also the statement of Shafi'i: If he strikes him with a large stone or a large piece of wood, it is Amd. Shibh Amd is that he intentionally strikes him with something that does not usually cause death. ... And for Abu Hanifa his proof is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Beware, the victim of Khata al-Amd is the victim of the whip and the stick, and for it one hundred camels.' And because the tool is not placed for killing nor used for it...
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage defines the legal concept of Qatl Shibh Amd (quasi-intentional killing) and presents the dispute among Hanafi imams and Imam Shafi'i. The text first gives the definition from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that Shibh Amd is when the killer intentionally strikes with something that is neither a weapon nor its equivalent, regardless of whether the tool is usually deadly. The Two Companions (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) and Imam Shafi'i differ: they consider the nature of the tool. If the tool is such that it usually causes death (like a large stone or heavy stick), it is Amd (intentional murder) requiring qisas. If the tool is small and not usually deadly (like a small stick), it is Shibh Amd. The passage then explains that the difference is one of scope: what the Sahibayn consider Shibh Amd is also Shibh Amd for Abu Hanifa, but some cases Abu Hanifa considers Shibh Amd are considered Amd by the Sahibayn. Then Imam Abu Hanifa's dalil is presented: the hadith mentioning the whip and stick as examples of Shibh Amd implies that any non-weapon tool qualifies. Another reason is that such tools are not designed for killing and cannot be used on a heedless victim in one blow, so the intentionality is reduced due to the nature of the tool. Thus, the tool determines the category.

Key Terms
شبه عمد (shibh amd): Qatl Shibh Amd: killing where the perpetrator intentionally strikes but with a tool not intended for killing, resulting in death; penalty is diyah mughallazah on the aqila.
عمد (amd): Intentional killing with a deadly weapon or equivalent; requires qisas.
خطأ العمد (khata' al-amd): Another term for shibh amd, meaning error in intent due to tool.
عصا (asa): Stick: the tool mentioned in the hadith; its absolute nature is central to the dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The definition of shibh amd hinges on the tool's nature versus its usual lethality, with Abu Hanifa relying on the absolute meaning of 'stick' in the hadith.
