Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
6 min
Abu Hanifa's Proof for Qatl Shibh al-Amd
Abu Hanifa's proof from hadith and reasoning on shibh al-amd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Abu Hanifa's hadith-based proof for shibh al-amd and distinguish his position from that of the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Hadith and tool-logic: a non-lethal tool makes a killing shibh al-amd, not 'amd — even if the tool is a club.

How do we classify a killing when the killer used a large club—is it intentional murder (ʿamd) or quasi-intentional (shibh al-ʿamd)? Imam Abu Hanifa cites a hadith and a rational argument to place it in the latter category, opposing his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. This lesson unpacks his proof and the practical consequences of the difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify Abu Hanifa's ruling: killing with any stick-like tool (including a large club) is shibh al-amd. The diyah is heavy and on the ʿāqila, with no qisas.
The ruling is based on the generality of the hadith.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) restrict the hadith's word 'ʿaṣā' to a small stick. For them, killing with a large club would be ʿamd, allowing qisas.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Sahibayn likely rely on custom or a contextual interpretation that restricts 'ʿaṣā' to smaller sticks. Their reasoning is that a large club can be a weapon.
Their specific dalil is not quoted here but inferred from the refutation.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa argues that the hadith is general and cannot be restricted without evidence. He adds a rational argument: a large club cannot be used by surprise (ghafilah) because multiple blows are needed, so the tool is not suitable for intentional killing.
Thus the killing lacks full intentionality (ʿamd) and becomes shibh al-amd.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: with a large club, Abu Hanifa says diyah on ʿāqila (no qisas), while Sahibayn say qisas is possible. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.

ترجمہ اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل نبی علیہ السلام کا فرمان ہے آگاہ ہو جاؤ شبہ عمد کا مقتول وہ کوڑے اور عصا کا مقتول ہے اور اس میں سو اونٹ ہیں اور اس لئے کہ آلہ قتل کے لئے نہ موضوع ہے اور نہ قتل میں استعمال کیا جاتا ہے اس لئے کہ اس آلہ کا استعمال ممکن نہیں اس شخص کی غفلت پر جس کے قتل کا قصد ہو اور اسی کی وجہ سے ( دھوکہ دے کر استعمال کی وجہ سے ) عموما قتل واقع ہوتا ہے تو آلہ کا لحاظ کرتے ہوئے عمدیت قاصر ہوگئی تو یہ شبہ عمد ہوگا کوڑے اور چھوٹی چھڑی کے مثل۔ تشریح اولا سمجھئے کہ شبہ عمد کو خطا عمد بھی کہتے ہیں ۔ عمد اس لئے کہتے ہیں کہ مارنے کا قصد ہے اور خطا اس لئے کہ ایسی چیز استعمال کر رہا ہے جو ہتھیار نہیں ہے اور نقل کے لئے موضوع ہے۔ یہ امام صاحب کی دلیل ہے کہ حدیث میں ہے الا ان قتيل خطا العمد لینی شبہ عمد مقتول وہ سے جس کو کوڑے اور لاٹھی سے مارا گیا ہو اور اس میں دیت کے سو اونٹ ہوتے ہیں۔
تو دیکھئے اس حدیث میں مطلق عصا کا ذکر ہے جو چھٹری اور لاٹھی دونوں کو شامل ہے تو صاحبین کا یہ فرمانا کہ اس سے مراد چھڑی ہے یہ مطلق کا ابطال ہے جو جائز نہیں ہے۔
پھر دوسری وجہ یہ بھی ہے کہ لٹھ ہو یا چھڑی ان دونوں کی وضع قتل کیلئے نہیں ہوتی اور نہ ان کو قتل کیلئے استعمال کیا جاتا ہے، کیونکہ ہتھیار تو وہ ہے کہ جس کو قتل کرنے کا ارادہ ہے وہ غافل ہے اور اچانک وار کیا اور وہ مر گیا جیسے ہتھیاروں میں ہوتا ہے مگر لاٹھی ہو یا چھٹڑی ان میں مقتول کی غفلت کے ساتھ استعمال ہی ناممکن ہے کیونکہ ان میں ایک دفعہ مارنا تو قتل کیلئے عموماً کافی نہ ہوگا بلکہ بار بار مارنا پڑے گا اور ایسی صورت میں غفلت نہیں رہے گی بلکہ غفلت صرف پہلی لاٹھی میں ہو سکتی ہے۔ اور چونکہ غفلت کی صورت میں ان کا استعمال ناممکن ہے اس وجہ سے قتل کے اندر عدیت کے معنی قاصر ہو گئے کیونکہ قاتل کے نفس قصد کا لحاظ نہیں بلکہ آلہ کا لحاظ ہے، لہذا لاٹھی وغیر قبل ایسے ہی شبہ عمدہ ہو گا جیسے کوڑے اور چھری سے قتل شبہ عمد ہوتا ہے۔
And he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed, the victim of quasi-intentional killing (khatā' al-ʿamd) is the victim of the whip and the stick, and for it one hundred camels.' And because the tool is not made for killing nor used in killing, since it cannot be used by surprise on the intended victim, and killing generally occurs by it, so intentionality falls short by considering the tool, thus it is quasi-intentional like killing with a whip or a small stick.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage presents Imam Abu Hanifa's proof for the classification of qatl shibh al-amd (quasi-intentional homicide). The passage begins by citing the hadith: 'The victim of quasi-intentional killing is the victim of the whip and the stick, and its diyah is one hundred camels.' Abu Hanifa argues that the word 'ʿaṣā' (stick) is general, including both a staff and a large club. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) restricted it to a small stick, but Abu Hanifa rejects this as an invalid restriction of the absolute (muthlaq). He then provides a rational argument: tools like sticks and clubs are not designed for killing, and they cannot be used to kill by surprise (ghafilah) because multiple strikes are usually needed, which eliminates the element of surprise. Therefore, intentionality is diminished by the nature of the tool, making it shibh al-amd. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute where the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa, as the hadith supports generality. The passage also notes that shibh al-amd is also called khatā' al-ʿamd (intentional error) because there is intent to strike but the tool is not a lethal weapon.

Key Terms
شبه العمد (shibh al-ʿamd): Quasi-intentional homicide: the killer intends to strike but uses a tool not ordinarily used for killing, resulting in death.
العصا (al-ʿaṣā): Stick or staff; in this context, any stick-like tool including a club or small stick.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa's proof, what is the primary reason that killing with a large club (laṭṭh) is considered shibh al-amd rather than ʿamd?
A) Because the killer did not intend to kill at all.
B) Because the tool is not designed for killing and cannot be used by surprise.
C) Because the victim was not a Muslim.
D) Because the diyah is less than one hundred camels.

Key Takeaway
The generality of the hadith 'qatīlu as-sawṭi wal-ʿaṣā' and the rational argument that non-lethal tools cannot be used by surprise form the basis of Abu Hanifa's classification of shibh al-amd.

Types and Ruling of Qatl Khata (Accidental Homicide)
Defines accidental homicide types and ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two types of accidental homicide and explain the ruling: kaffarah upon the killer and diyah upon the ʿāqila.

Core Idea
Accidental killing requires expiation and blood money on the clan, regardless of the error type.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the two forms of error in homicide and establishes a unified legal consequence. Both types—error in intent and error in action—trigger the same obligations: kaffarah (expiation) on the killer and diyah (blood money) on the ʿāqila. The ruling is firmly based on the Quranic verse 4:92.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of khaṭā
The passage names khaṭā fi al-qaṣd (error in intent) and khaṭā fi al-fiʿl (error in action). Recognize the examples: shooting at game but hitting a human, or shooting at a target but hitting a person.
Both are considered accidental; intention is irrelevant for this classification.
2
State the legal consequences (mu'jab)
The passage states that the consequence (mu'jab) is kaffarah and diyah. Kaffarah is specific to the killer; diyah is on the ʿāqila (clan).
Kaffarah is wajib, not merely recommended.
3
Cite the Quranic proof
The verse from Surah al-Nisa 4:92 is quoted: 'the freeing of a believing slave and a diyah handed over to his family.' This establishes the wajib obligation.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalalah, so the ruling is definitive.
4
Note the payment schedule
The diyah is paid by the ʿāqila over three years, as explained in the fuller context (referred to as 'as we have explained').
This is the standard Hanafi position for accidental homicide.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخطاء على نوعين خطا في القصد وهو ان يرمى شخصا يظنه صيدا فاذا هو آدمی او يظنه حربيا فاذا مسلم وخطأ فى الفعل وهو ان يرقى عرضا فيصيب ادميا و موجب ذلك الكفارة والدية على العاقلة لقول تعالى فتحرير رقبة مؤمنة ودية مسلمة الى اهله الآية وهى على عاقلة في ثلث سنين لما بيناه
And accidental killing is of two types: error in intent, which is when one shoots at a person thinking it is game, yet it is a human, or thinking he is a combatant, yet he is a Muslim; and error in action, which is when one shoots at a target and hits a human. And the consequence of that is kaffarah and diyah upon the ʿāqila, due to the saying of the Most High: 'the freeing of a believing slave and a diyah handed over to his family' (Quran 4:92). And it is upon the ʿāqila in three years, as we have explained.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage defines the two types of accidental homicide (khaṭā). The first is error in intention: the killer intended to kill something permissible (hunting game or an enemy combatant) but mistakenly killed a human or a Muslim. The second is error in action: the killer intended to shoot at an inanimate target but accidentally hit a person. The ruling for both types is identical: kaffarah (freeing a believing slave, or fasting two months if unable) and diyah upon the ʿāqila, payable in three years. The Quranic verse (Surah al-Nisa 4:92) is cited as proof. The 'āqila are the male agnatic relatives of the killer, and the diyah is standard (not heavy) for accidental killing. This is a foundational ruling in Hanafi fiqh for jinayat.

Key Terms
خطأ في القصد (khaṭā fi al-qaṣd): Error in intention: the killer intended a lawful act but made a mistake in who or what he targeted.
خطأ في الفعل (khaṭā fi al-fiʿl): Error in action: the killer intended one action but accidentally committed another, causing death.
العاقلة (al-ʿāqila): The male agnatic relatives of the killer who are jointly responsible for paying diyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling (hukm) for kaffarah in accidental homicide according to the Hanafi school?
A) Sunnah
B) Wajib
C) Fard
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Accidental homicide incurs kaffarah on the killer and diyah on the ʿāqila, based on the clear Quranic command.

Qatl Shibh al-Amd: Rulings, Diyah, and Inheritance Disqualification
Explains rulings of shibh al-amd and disputes with Malik

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for qatl shibh al-amd, explain why the diyah is upon the 'aqila and paid in three years, and evaluate Imam Malik's objection.

Core Idea
Shibh al-amd: diyah on 'aqila, not qisas, but inheritance is blocked – shubhah drops one, not the other.

This lesson examines the Hanafi category of quasi-intentional homicide (shibh al-amd). While the killer intended the act, the outcome lacked the typical lethality, so qisas is dropped. However, a heavy diyah (aggravated) is wajib on the 'aqila in three years, and the killer is deprived of inheritance. The passage also addresses Imam Malik's denial of this category and the Hanafi proof from tradition.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition
Define shibh al-amd: intentional strike with a tool that typically does not kill. Distinguish from 'amd (intentional with lethal means) and khata' (accidental).
The definition is key to the entire ruling.
2
Identify the rulings (hukm)
What components are wajib? Sin, kaffarah, and diyah mughallazah. The diyah is on the 'aqila, not the killer personally, because it is a direct consequence of the homicide.
Diyah is wajib, not fard, due to zanni evidence.
3
Trace the general principle (kulliya)
The passage states: 'every diyah obligated directly from homicide is on the 'aqila.' This differentiates from diyah arising later through sulh.
Analogy to qatl khata' reinforces this.
4
Apply the inheritance disqualification
The killer is deprived of inheritance because a killer does not inherit from the victim. Shubhah (likeness to accidental) drops qisas but does not affect inheritance.
Clarifies common misconception.
5
Handle the dispute with Malik
Imam Malik denies shibh al-amd, calling it simply 'amd. The Hanafi response cites evidence from al-Asl and the practice of 'Umar.
Know the practical difference: qisas vs. diyah.

Source Text

کلیہ یہ ہے کہ ہر وہ دیت جو قتل سے ابتداء، واجب ہو نہ کہ ایسے معنی کی وجہ سے جو بعد میں پیدا ہوں تو وہ دیت عاقلہ پر ہوگی قتل خطا پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور یہ دیت تین سالوں میں واجب ہو گی عمر بن الخطاب کے فیصلہ کی وجہ سے اور مغلظہ واجب ہوگی اور ہم عنقریب تغلیظ کی صفت کو بیان کریں گے۔ انشاء اللہ تعالی

Book of Homicide. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume 15. The general principle is that every diyah that is obligated from the beginning due to homicide, not due to a meaning that arises later, will be upon the 'aqila by analogy on qatl khata'. And this diyah will be obligated in three years because of the decision of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab. And it will be mughallazah (heavy), and we will soon describe the description of taghliz. Insha'Allah. Explanation: From here the author explains the cause and ruling of qatl shibh al-amd. Its cause is sin, kaffarah, and diyah. And the ruling of shibh al-amd according to the two parties is sin because he struck intentionally causing death. And kaffarah is wajib because it resembles qatl khata'. And an aggravated diyah is wajib, which is upon his family. The author will himself explain taghliz later. And the installments of diyah will be paid in three years because 'Umar Faruq gave such a decision. Why is the diyah upon the 'aqila? For that, the general principle is stated: that the diyah which is obligated directly from the homicide is upon the killer's family, and if after killing, diyah becomes wajib through reconciliation or something, then it is upon the killer himself. And here the diyah is obligated directly from the homicide. In intentional murder and quasi-intentional murder, the killer is deprived of inheritance. And related to it is deprivation of inheritance because it is a penalty for killing, and shubhah affects the dropping of qisas but not the deprivation of inheritance. And Malik, although he denied the knowledge of shibh al-amd, the proof against him is what we have narrated in al-Asl and what we have previously stated. Translation: And with it is related deprivation of inheritance because it is a penalty for killing, and shubhah is effective in dropping qisas but not in deprivation of inheritance. And Malik, even if he denied shibh al-amd, the proof against him is what we have narrated. Explanation: Just as in 'amd there is deprivation of inheritance, similarly in shibh al-amd he will be deprived of inheritance because it is an established principle that a killer does not inherit from his victim, and this too is killing. There is a question: it is killing but there is shubhah. Due to shubhah, qisas is dropped, but the deprivation of inheritance is not dropped. Imam Malik says: I do not know shibh al-amd; rather, it is just murder.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is a commentary on Al-Hidayah, specifically discussing the rulings of qatl shibh al-amd (quasi-intentional homicide). The author first presents the general principle (kulliya) that any diyah directly resulting from homicide is upon the 'aqila (the killer's paternal relatives), by analogy to qatl khata'. This diyah is mughallazah (heavier) and paid over three years, following the precedent of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab. The commentary then explains that shibh al-amd entails sin because the killer acted intentionally, kaffarah because it resembles qatl khata', and an aggravated diyah on the 'aqila. The killer is also disqualified from inheriting from the victim, because the principle is that a killer does not inherit. Although shubhah (suspicion) drops qisas (retaliation), it does not remove the deprivation of inheritance. The passage addresses a dissent from Imam Malik, who denied the category of shibh al-amd altogether. The Hanafi response is that the proof from the foundational texts (al-Asl) supports its existence. The ruling is based on the principle that the diyah is directly from the homicide, not from a subsequent cause.

Key Terms
شبه العمد (shibh al-amd): Homicide where the killer intentionally strikes but with a tool or means that typically does not cause death, resulting in a mistake in the outcome.
العاقلة (al-‘āqilah): The paternal relatives (asabah) of the killer who are responsible for paying the diyah in cases of khata’ and shibh al-amd.
دية مغلظة (diyah mughallaẓah): An aggravated diyah: heavier than standard diyah, typically 100 camels with specific age/type requirements, imposed for shibh al-amd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the killer in shibh al-amd deprived of inheritance from the victim despite the presence of shubhah?
A) Because shubhah applies only to qisas, not to inheritance disqualification.
B) Because the killer did not intentionally cause death.
C) Because the diyah is mughallazah.
D) Because Imam Malik denied shibh al-amd.

Key Takeaway
Shibh al-amd is a distinct Hanafi category where qisas is dropped but diyah mughallazah on the 'aqila and inheritance disqualification apply.

Rulings of Qatl Khata' (Unintentional Homicide) and Its Types
Defines two types of khata' and explains obligatory consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two types of qatl khata', identify its obligatory consequences (kaffarah, diyah on 'aqila in three years), and explain why the killer is deprived of inheritance despite no intentional sin.

Core Idea
Unintentional homicide still incurs expiation, blood money on the tribe, and inheritance disqualification—because negligence is a sin.

This passage from Al-Hidayah refines the definition of unintentional homicide (khata') into two distinct types and then clarifies the obligations that arise. It also resolves a seeming paradox: if there is no sin of intentional killing, why is the killer still deprived of inheritance? The answer lies in the nature of negligence and the prescription of kaffarah. Understanding this will help you apply the correct legal consequences in accidental death cases.

Guided Path
1
Define the two types of khata'
Identify from the passage: mistake in intention (e.g., shooting at what you think is game but is a person) and mistake in action (e.g., shooting at a target but hitting a person).
Both types share the same ruling; the distinction is for conceptual clarity.
2
List the three wajibat for qatl khata'
From the text: (1) kaffarah (freeing a slave or fasting), (2) diyah (blood money) payable by the 'aqila, and (3) deprivation of inheritance for the killer.
Diyah is paid over three years, as established earlier.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is Quran 4:92, which commands freeing a believing slave and delivering diyah. The imperative form indicates wujub.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalala, so the ruling is firmly wajib.
4
Analyze the paradox of 'no sin' vs. inheritance deprivation
Imam Quduri stated there is no sin in khata', yet the killer is deprived of inheritance. The mashai'ikh explain: there is no sin of intentional killing, but there is sin in the act itself due to negligence (abandoning caution), and the prescription of kaffarah proves this.
Thus, inheritance deprivation is consistent with the presence of a lesser sin (negligence).
5
Contrast with intentional killing (shabh 'amd)
The passage briefly contrasts: if someone strikes a body part intentionally and mistakenly hits another part causing death, it counts as 'amd (intentional) because the whole body is one unit.
This shows the importance of intent; in khata', there is no intent to harm at all.

والخطاء على نوعين خطا في القصد وهو ان يرمى شخصا يظنه صيدا فاذا هو آدمی او يظنه حربيا فاذا مسلم وخطأ فى الفعل وهو ان يرقى عرضا فيصيب ادميا و موجب ذلك الكفارة والدية على العاقلة لقول تعالى فتحرير رقبة مؤمنة ودية مسلمة الى اهله الآية وهى على عاقلة في ثلث سنين لما بيناه
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا قتل خطا دو قسم پر ہے ایک رادہ کی خطا اور وہ یہ ہے کہ تیر مارے کسی ایسے شخص کو جس کو وہ شکار سمجھ رہا ہے پس اچانک وہ آدمی ہے یا اس کو حر بی سمجھ رہا ہے پس اچانک وہ مسلمان ہے اور دوسری خطاً فی فعل میں اور وہ یہ ہے کہ کسی نشانہ پر تیر مارے ہیں وہ کسی آدمی کو لگ جائے اور اسکا موجب کفارہ اور دیت ہے عاقلہ پر اللہ تعالیٰ کے فرمان فتحرير رقبة مؤمنة ودية مسلمة الى اهله الآية " کی وجہ سے اور دیت قاتل کے عاقلہ پر تین سال میں ہوگی اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں ۔ تشریح قتل خطا کا موجب کفارہ اور دیت ہے اور دیت عاقلہ پر ہوگی اور اس کی ادائیگی تین سال میں ہوگی جس کی دلیل او پر گذر چکی ہے۔ اور خطا کی دوقسمیں ہیں ایک ارادہ کی خطاً اور دوسرے فعل کی خطا ۔ اول کی مثال جیسے ماررہاتھا ہرن کونگر وہ آدمی نگا ، یا مار رہا تھا حربی کو وہ مسلمان اگا ، سیہ ارادہ کی خطا ہے۔ ثانی کی مثال جیسے کسی نشانہ ہی مارا مگر وہاں نہیں لگا بلکہ کسی آدمی کو لگ گیا یہ فعل کی خطا ہے، بہر حال حکم دونوں کا ایک ہے کہ کفار اور دیت واجب ہے جس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے جو متن میں مذکور ہے۔
قتل خطا میں گناہ نہیں خواہ خطاً فی الارادہ ہو یا خطاً فی الفعل
ولا اثم فيه يعنى فى الوجهين قالو المراد اثم القتل فاما فى نفسه فلا يعرى عن الاثم من حيث ترك العزيمة والمبالغة في التثبت في حال الرمي اذ شرع الكفارة يوذن باعتبار هذا المعنى اور قتل خطا میں دونوں صورتوں میں گنا نہیں ہے۔ مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ مرا قتل کا گناہ ہے بہر حال فی نفسہ یہ فعل گناہ سے خالی نہیں ہے عزیمت کے ترک اور احتیاط میں مبالغہ کو ترک کرنے کی وجدت پھینکنے کے وقت اس لئے کہ کفارہ کا شروع ہوتا اس معنی کے اعتبار کی خبر ہ دیتا ہے۔ تشریح امام قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ قتل خطا میں گناہ نہیں خواہ خطا فی الا رادہ ہو یا خطا فی افعل ہو مگر یہ عجیب سی بات تھی کہ گناہ نہیں لیکن پھر بھی میراث سے محروم ہو گا ؟ تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ چونکہ اس نے قتل کا قصد نہیں گیا اس لئے جو قصد کا گناہ ہوتا ہے وہ نہ ہوگا لیکن نفس قبل یہاں بھی گناہ سے کیونکہ اس نے عزیمت پر عمل چھوڑا ، اور تیر پھینکنے کے وقت جس احتیاط سے کام لینا چاہئے وہ چھوڑا ۔ اور نفس قبل میں گناہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہاں کفارہ مشروع ہے اور بغیر گناہ کے کنارہ شروع نہ ہوگا اس لئے تو میراث سے محروم ہو گا،

البدن كالمحل الواحد
And khata' is of two types: mistake in intention, which is that he shoots at a person thinking he is a deer, then it turns out to be a human; or he thinks he is a harbi (enemy combatant) and then it turns out to be a Muslim. And mistake in action, which is that he shoots at a target and it hits a human. And the cause of that is kaffarah and diyah upon the 'aqila, due to the verse: 'Freeing a believing slave and delivering a diyah to his family...' and it is upon the 'aqila in three years, as we have explained. Translation: Quduri said: Qatl khata' is of two types: first, mistake in intention, and that is that he shoots an arrow at a person whom he thinks is game, then suddenly he is a human; or he thinks he is a harbi, then suddenly he is a Muslim. Second, mistake in action, and that is that he shoots at a target and it hits a human. Its cause is kaffarah and diyah upon the 'aqila, due to Allah's statement: 'Freeing a believing slave and delivering a diyah to his family...' and the diyah is upon the killer's 'aqila in three years, due to the proof we have already mentioned. Explanation: The cause of qatl khata' is kaffarah and diyah, and the diyah is upon the 'aqila, and its payment is in three years, the proof for which has passed. And khata' has two types: mistake in intention and mistake in action. Example of the first: he was shooting a deer and it turned out to be a human, or he was shooting a harbi and it turned out to be a Muslim. This is mistake in intention. Example of the second: he shot at a target but it did not hit that but hit a person. This is mistake in action. In any case, the ruling of both is the same: kaffarah and diyah are wajib, the proof of which is this verse mentioned in the text. There is no sin in qatl khata', whether it is mistake in intention or mistake in action. 'There is no sin in it' – meaning in both ways. They said: the intended meaning is the sin of killing. However, in itself, it is not free from sin in terms of abandoning resolution (azimah) and lack of thorough caution at the time of shooting, since the legislation of kaffarah indicates consideration of this meaning. And in qatl khata', there is no sin in both forms. The mashai'ikh said: the meaning is the sin of killing. Nevertheless, in itself, this act is not free from sin because he abandoned resolution and neglected the thorough caution that should be exercised at the time of shooting, because the legislation of kaffarah indicates the consideration of this meaning. Explanation: Imam Quduri said that there is no sin in qatl khata', whether it is mistake in intention or mistake in action. But this is a strange thing: if there is no sin, then why is he deprived of inheritance? The answer given is that because he did not intend to kill, the sin of intention is not there, but in itself, there is sin because he abandoned resolution and neglected the caution that should be taken at the time of shooting. And the proof of sin in itself is that kaffarah is legislated here, and kaffarah is not prescribed without sin. Therefore, he is deprived of inheritance. Hence he said: The killer in khata' is also deprived of inheritance. 'He is deprived of inheritance' because there is (that meaning) in it, so it is valid to attach deprivation to it. This is unlike the case where he intentionally strikes a part of his body and mistakenly hits another part, and death occurs, where qisas is obligatory because the killing occurred with intent towards some part of his body, and the entire body is like a single location.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on qatl khata' (unintentional homicide). It begins by defining the two types: mistake in intention (like shooting a person thinking it is game or an enemy combatant) and mistake in action (like shooting at a target but hitting a person). Both types have the same ruling: kaffarah (expiation) and diyah (blood money) payable by the 'aqila over three years. The proof is the Quranic verse (4:92) which prescribes freeing a believing slave and paying diyah. The commentary then addresses a seeming paradox: Imam Quduri stated there is no sin in khata', but the killer is still deprived of inheritance. The mashai'ikh (senior scholars) clarify: there is no sin of intentional killing, but there is sin in the act itself due to lack of precaution and abandonment of resolution (azimah), evidenced by the very prescription of kaffarah, which is only required for sins. Thus, the killer in khata' is also disqualified from inheriting. The passage concludes with a contrasting case: if someone intentionally strikes a part of the body but misses and hits another part, causing death, that is considered 'amd because the whole body is treated as one unit, and qisas applies. The overall lesson is that unintentional killing still carries consequences of kaffarah, diyah, and inheritance disqualification, though no criminal sin of intentional murder is attributed.

Key Terms
خطأ (khaṭa’): Unintentional mistake in action or intention leading to death, without any intent to kill.
كفارة (kaffārah): Expiation for accidental killing: freeing a believing slave, or fasting two consecutive months if unable.
حرمان الميراث (ḥirmān al-mīrāth): Deprivation of inheritance; a killer cannot inherit from the victim, even in khata'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the legislation of kaffarah indicates the presence of sin in the act itself due to negligence.
B) Because the killer is always deprived regardless of circumstances.
C) Because the victim's family requests it.
D) Because the killer is not a Muslim.

Key Takeaway
Qatl khata' incurs three obligations: kaffarah, diyah on the 'aqila, and inheritance disqualification, all rooted in Quran 4:92 and the principle that negligence is a sin.

Causative Killing (Qatl Sabab): Kaffarah and Inheritance Deprivation – Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on the consequences of causative killing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on kaffarah and inheritance deprivation for qatl sabab, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and evaluate the Hanafi response based on the distinction between liability and criminal consequences.

Core Idea
Causative killing is not true killing: diyah is wajib, but kaffarah and inheritance deprivation are not.

This lesson examines a classic ikhtilaf between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: does indirect causation of death (qatl sabab) trigger the same consequences as direct killing? The Hanafi school, relying on the absence of actual killing, limits the consequence to diyah, while the Shafi'i school argues that the Shari'ah has treated causative killing as a form of killing, thus requiring kaffarah and preventing inheritance. Understanding this dispute reveals the Hanafi methodology of distinguishing between liability (daman) and religious/criminal consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What exactly is being disputed? Determine the specific ruling in question: does qatl sabab require kaffarah (expiation) and deprive the killer of inheritance (hurman)?
The point of dispute is not the diyah (blood money) – both schools agree on that. Focus on the additional consequences.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi school holds that only diyah is wajib; no kaffarah and no inheritance deprivation. The proof: actual killing (haqiqat al-qatl) is absent; the person is sinful for the cause (digging the well), not for the death itself.
The Hanafi emphasis is on the reality of the act: a cause is not a direct act of killing.
3
Present the Shafi'i proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the Shari'ah has placed causative killing in the rank of killing (qatl). Its closest type is accidental killing (qatl khata), so all rulings of qatl khata, including kaffarah and inheritance deprivation, should apply by analogy.
The Shafi'i use qiyas (analogy) to annex qatl sabab to qatl khata based on a shared 'illa (effective cause): being a cause of death.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that the annexation (ilhaq) is only for liability (daman), not for religious or inheritance consequences. They maintain the original ruling that for kaffarah and hurman, actual killing must be present. The sin is for the prohibited act of digging, not for the death.
This highlights a key usul principle: the scope of qiyas can be limited by context and by the presence of countervailing considerations (istihsan).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In a case of qatl sabab (e.g., digging a well on public land causing a death), a Hanafi judge would only order diyah and allow the killer to inherit; a Shafi'i judge would also require kaffarah and prevent inheritance.
Understand that this difference stems from a deeper methodological divergence about the nature of causation in Islamic law.

قالوا وهذه كفارة ذنب القتل وكذا الحرمان بسبه

ترجمہ اور شافعی نے فرمایا کہ اس کو (قتل سبب) کو قتل خطا کے ساتھ لاحق کر دیا جائے گا اس کے احکام میں اس لئے کہ شریعت نے اس کو قاتل کے درجہ میں اتار دیا ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس کی طرف سے حقیقت قتل معدوم ہے تو اس کو ضمان کے حق میں قتل خطا کے ساتھ لاحق کر دیا گیا ہے۔ پس [ممانعت؟] کے حق میں قتل سبب اصل پر برقرار رہے گا اور سبب مسبب اگر چہ غیر ملک میں کنواں کھودنے کی وجہ سے گنہگار ہوگا ( لیکن ) موت کی وجہ سے گنہ گار نہ ہو گا جیسا کہ مشائخ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اور یہ کفارہ قتل ) قتل کے گناہ کا کفارہ ہے اور ایسے ہی میراث سے حرمان گناہ کے سبب سے ہے۔ ہمارے نزدیک قتل سبب میں صرف دیت ہے کفارہ نہیں اور نہ حرمان [ارث] ہے امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ کفارہ بھی ہے اور میراث سے محروم ہونا بھی ہے کیونکہ شریعت نے جو اس کو قتل قرار دیا ہے اور قتل کا بلکہ درجہ قتل خطا ہے [بندہ] [قتل] خطا کے احکام اس پر جاری ہوں گے۔

ہم نے جواب دیا کہ حقیقت قاتل کی جانب سے قتل معدوم ہے البتہ یہ صرف قتل کا سبب ہے تو اس سبب ہونے کی وجہ سے ہم نے اس کے اوپر دیت واجب کردی لیکن کفارہ اور حرمان ارث کے بارے میں ہم نے اس کو اس کی حقیقت پر برقرار رکھا کہ یہ اس کی جانب سے قتل نہیں ہے بنا [نہ] کفارہ ہوگا اور نہ میراث سے محروم ہو گا۔ اور کفارہ قتل اور میراث سے حرمان جب ہوتا ہے کہ قتل کی [وجہ] [سے] گنہگار ہو اور یہ موت کی وجہ سے گنہ گار ہی نہیں بلکہ غیر ملک میں کنواں کھودنے کی وجہ سے گنہگار ہے۔
They said: This is the expiation for the sin of killing, and similarly deprivation due to it. Translation: And al-Shafi'i said that this (causative killing) should be annexed to accidental killing (qatl khata) in its rulings because the Shari'ah has placed it in the rank of killer. And our proof is that actual killing is non-existent from his side, so it has been annexed to accidental killing in matters of liability. Therefore, in matters of prevention? causative killing remains on its original ruling. And the cause and the caused: although he becomes sinful due to digging a well in someone else's property, he does not become sinful due to death. As the mashayikh said: And this expiation (kaffarah) is for the sin of killing, and similarly deprivation from inheritance is due to sin. According to us, in causative killing there is only diyah, no kaffarah, and no deprivation of inheritance. Imam al-Shafi'i says: There is kaffarah and deprivation of inheritance because the Shari'ah has declared it killing, and its nearest degree is accidental killing (qatl khata), so the rulings of qatl khata would apply to it. We replied: Actual killing is non-existent from the killer's side; rather, this is only a cause of killing. So due to being a cause, we made diyah wajib upon him. But regarding kaffarah and deprivation of inheritance, we left it on its reality: that it is not killing from his side, so there will be no kaffarah and he will not be deprived of inheritance. And the kaffarah of killing and deprivation of inheritance occurs when he is sinful due to the killing, and he is not sinful due to death; rather, he is sinful due to digging a well in another's property.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding qatl sabab (causative killing). The issue is whether the person who causes death through an indirect act (like digging a well in another's property) is subject to kaffarah (expiation) and deprivation of inheritance (hurman min al-mirath). The Shafi'i school argues that since the Shari'ah treats causative killing as a form of killing, it should be annexed to qatl khata (accidental killing) in all its rulings, including kaffarah and inheritance deprivation. The Hanafi school, as represented by the author, distinguishes between liability (daman) and criminal consequences. In liability, causative killing is treated like qatl khata, so diyah is wajib. However, for kaffarah and inheritance deprivation, the Hanafis consider the actual act of killing (haqiqat al-qatl) absent; the person is sinful for the cause (digging) but not for the death itself. Therefore, kaffarah and deprivation do not apply. The author presents the Shafi'i proof and then provides the Hanafi response, emphasizing the distinction between causing and actual killing.

Key Terms
قتل سبب (qatl sabab): Indirect causation of death, e.g., digging a well in non-owned land causing someone to fall in.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation due to accidental killing, usually freeing a slave or fasting.
حرمان (hurman): Deprivation of inheritance due to killing the testator.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on kaffarah for causative killing (qatl sabab)?
A) Kaffarah is wajib
B) Kaffarah is not wajib
C) Kaffarah is wajib only if the killer intended death
D) Kaffarah is wajib but only fasting

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, causative killing (qatl sabab) does not incur kaffarah or inheritance deprivation because the death is not directly caused; the sin is for the act of causing, not the death itself.

Conditions for Qisas: Protected Blood and the Free-Slave Dispute
Ruling on conditions for qisas and opening of the free-slave dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of perpetually protected blood for qisas and explain why the Hanafi school holds that a free man is executed for killing a slave, and contrast the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Qisas requires blood that is perpetually protected; temporary protection is insufficient.

This lesson builds on the general rule that intentional killing necessitates qisas. However, not every intentional killing triggers retaliation — the victim's blood must be perpetually inviolable. We will examine the two conditions from al-Quduri's matn, understand the rationale behind perpetual protection, and then enter the classic Hanafi-Shafi'i disagreement on cross-status killings: can a free man be executed for murdering a slave?

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Condition
Al-Quduri states: Qisas is wajib for killing every person whose blood is perpetually protected (mahqun al-dam 'ala al-ta'bid) when done intentionally. Identify the two key conditions: intentional killing and perpetual protection of blood.
The condition of perpetual protection is specific; it excludes harbis, apostates, rebels, musta'mins, and others whose blood is not permanently inviolable.
2
Understand the Rationale for Perpetual Protection
The commentary gives two reasons: (1) to remove any suspicion that the victim's blood was permissible (shubha al-ibaha), and (2) to ensure equality (musawat) between the victim and the killer. Understand why each is necessary for qisas.
Suspicion of permissibility nullifies qisas because the Prophet ﷺ said, 'Avert the hudud by doubts.'
3
Distinguish Temporary vs. Permanent Protection
The passage addresses a potential objection: a person who becomes Muslim in dar al-harb is protected, yet qisas is not taken from his killer. The answer distinguishes temporary protection (ismat muwaqqata) from permanent protection (ismat muqawwama) obtained by residing in dar al-Islam.
This distinction is unique to Hanafi fiqh and is covered in Kitab al-Siyar.
4
Enter the Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute on Free Killing Slave
The Hanafi school holds that a free man is executed for killing a slave based on general proofs (al-umumat) from the Quran and Sunnah which do not differentiate between free and slave when blood is protected. The Shafi'i school argues from the verse 'The free for the free, and the slave for the slave' (Quran 2:178) that cross-execution is not allowed.
The text cuts off before the full Hanafi response, but we can identify the basis of the dispute: whether the verse is restrictive or simply states the general rule.
5
Evaluate the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
Under the Hanafi view, a free person who kills a slave is subject to qisas unless the owner waives it (or diya is taken). Under the Shafi'i view, a free person is never executed for a slave; only diya applies.
The Hanafi position relies on the broader principle that all protected lives are equal in inviolability.

باب ما يوجب القصاص وما لا يوجبه

ترجمہ باب ان امور کے بیان میں جو موجب قصاص ہیں اور جو نہیں ہیں

تشریح مصنف اقسام قتل بیان فرما چکے ہیں جن میں ایک قتل عمد تھا جو موجب قصاص تھا لیکن یہ ہر وقت قصاص واجب نہیں کرتا بلکہ کبھی کرتا ہے اور کبھی نہیں کرتا اس لئے تفصیل کی حاجت پیش آئی اس باب میں مصنف اس کی تفصیل بیان فرمائیں گے۔ قصاص کون سے قتل سے واجب ہوتا ہے

قال القصاص واجب بقتل كل محقون الدم على التابيد اذا قتل عمدا اما العمدية فلما بيناه واما حقن الدم على التابيد فلتنتفى شبهة الاباحة وتتحقق المساواة.

ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا ہر وہ شخص جو ہمیشہ کے لئے محفوظ الدم ہو اس کے قتل سے قصاص واجب ہوتا ہے جب کہ وہ عمد قتل کیا جائے بہر حال عملیت پس اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور بہر حال ہمیشہ کے لئے خون کا محفوظ ہونا پس تا کہ خون کی اباحت کا شبہ منتفی ہو جائے اور مساوات متحقق ہو جائے۔

تشریح قتل عمد میں قصاص واجب ہو گا جب کہ مقتول ایسا شخص ہو جس کا خون ہمیشہ کیلئے محفوظ ہو جیسے مسلمان یا ذمی کیونکہ ذمی کا امان بھی دائمی ہے کافر حربی، مرتد، باغی، مستامن یہ سب اس فہرست سے خارج ہیں لہذا ان کے قتل سے قصاص واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اب مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ قدوری نے دو قید لگائی ہیں
1 عمدیت اس کا بیان تو کتاب الجنایات کے شروع میں گذر چکا ہے۔
2 ہمیشہ کے لئے محفوظ الدم ہونا تو اس کی دو وجہ ہیں۔
(1) اگر یہ شرط نہ ہو گی تو اس مقتول کے مباح الدم ہونے کا شبہ باقی رہے گا اور شبہ آتے ہی قصاص ختم ہو جاتا ہے۔ (2) تا کہ مقتول اور قاتل کے درمیان مساوات ہو سکے کہ مقتول محفوظ الدم تھا تو اسکے بدلہ میں محفوظ الدم قاتل بھی قتل کیا جا سکے۔ سوال جو شخص دار الحرب میں مسلمان ہوگیا تو وہ بھی ہمیشہ کیلئے محفوظ الدم ہو گیا حالانکہ اس کے قاتل سے قصاص نہیں لیا جاتا ؟ جواب ابھی اسلام لانے سے اس کو عصمت [موقته؟] حاصل ہوئی ہے اور عصمت [مقومہ] دار الاسلام سے حاصل ہوتی ہے اور بغیر عصمت مقومہ کے حصول کے قصاص نہیں لیا جائے گا۔ (ومر لهذا البحث في كتاب السير)

قال ويقتل الحر بالحر والحر بالعبد للعمومات وقال الشافعي لا يقتل الحر بالعبد لقوله تعالى الحر بالحر والعبد بالعبد ومن ضرورة هذه المقابلة ان لا يقتل حر بعبد ولان مبنى القصاص على المساواة وهي منتفية بين المالك والمملوك ولهذا لا يثبت قصاص الطرف بطرفه وبخلاف العبد حيث يقتل بالحر لانه تفاوت الى
Chapter on what necessitates qisas and what does not. Translation: Chapter on the matters that necessitate qisas and those that do not. Commentary: The author has already explained the types of killing, among which is intentional killing that necessitates qisas, but it does not always necessitate qisas; sometimes it does and sometimes not, so there is need for detail. In this chapter, the author will explain the detail. Which killing necessitates qisas? He (al-Quduri) said: Qisas is wajib for killing every person whose blood is perpetually protected, when killed intentionally. As for intention, due to what we have explained; as for perpetual protection of blood, to negate the suspicion of permissibility and to establish equality. Translation: Al-Quduri said: Qisas is wajib for killing every person who is perpetually protected in blood, when killed intentionally. As for intention, due to the proof we have explained; as for perpetual protection of blood, to negate the suspicion of permissibility and to establish equality. Commentary: In intentional killing, qisas is wajib when the victim is a person whose blood is perpetually protected, like a Muslim or a dhimmi, because the aman of a dhimmi is also perpetual. A harbi, apostate, rebel, musta'min – all are excluded from this list, so qisas is not wajib for killing them. Now the author says that al-Quduri laid down two conditions: (1) Intention – its explanation has passed at the beginning of Kitab al-Jinayat. (2) Perpetual protection of blood – this has two reasons: (i) If this condition were not present, there would remain the suspicion that the victim's blood was permissible, and with suspicion qisas is dropped. (ii) So that equality between victim and killer is achieved: the victim was protected, so in retaliation a protected killer can be killed. Question: If a person becomes Muslim in dar al-harb, he becomes perpetually protected in blood, yet qisas is not taken from his killer? Answer: By embracing Islam, he obtains temporary protection (ismat muwaqqata?), and permanent protection (ismat muqawwama) is obtained by residing in dar al-Islam, and without attaining permanent protection, qisas is not taken. (This research has passed in Kitab al-Siyar.) He said: A free man is executed for a free man and a free man for a slave because of general proofs. And al-Shafi'i said: A free man is not executed for a slave because of the verse: 'The free for the free, and the slave for the slave,' and the necessary implication of this juxtaposition is that a free man is not executed for a slave. And because qisas is based on equality, which is absent between owner and owned. Therefore, qisas of a limb is not established for a limb? But a slave is executed for a free man because [the text cuts off].
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on what necessitates qisas and what does not. The author first quotes al-Quduri's matn that qisas is wajib for killing any person whose blood is perpetually protected (mahqun al-dam 'ala al-ta'bid). The commentary explains that this includes Muslims and dhimmis but excludes apostates, rebels, harbis, and musta'mins. The condition of perpetual protection is necessary to eliminate the suspicion that the victim's blood was permissible (mubah) and to ensure equality (musawat) between killer and victim. The text then discusses the specific case of a person who converts to Islam in dar al-harb: although he becomes protected, qisas is not taken because he only has temporary protection (ismat muwaqqata) until he enters dar al-Islam. Finally, the passage begins the famous Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on whether a free man can be executed for killing a slave. The Hanafi school holds that a free man is killed for a free man and also for a slave, based on general proofs (al-umumat) from the Quran and Sunnah that do not differentiate. The Shafi'i school argues from the Quranic verse 'The free for the free, and the slave for the slave' (Quran 2:178) that the juxtaposition implies no cross-execution. The text cuts off before the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof is given; the full response appears in subsequent pages, typically that the verse establishes the principle of equality without restriction, and that the slave's blood is protected, so the free man can be killed for him.

Key Terms
محقون الدم (mahqun al-dam): Whose blood is protected (inviolable) and cannot be shed without legal cause.
القصاص (al-qisas): Retaliation in kind for murder or bodily injury.
عصمت مقومة (ismat muqawwama): Permanent inviolability attained by residing in dar al-Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on executing a free man for killing his own slave?
A) The free man is not executed because of the verse 'al-hurr bi al-hurr'
B) The free man is executed for the slave based on general proofs
C) The free man is executed only if the slave was Muslim
D) The free man is executed only if the slave was a dhimmi

Key Takeaway
Qisas is wajib only when the victim is perpetually protected; additionally, the Hanafi school holds that a free man is executed for killing a slave, contrary to the Shafi'i school.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
6 min
Definition and Conditions of Qisas
Definition and conditions of qisas rule.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for qisas to be wajib and identify which persons qualify as permanently inviolable.

Core Idea
Qisas is wajib only when the victim is permanently inviolable and the killing is intentional.

This lesson presents the foundational ruling from Quduri's Mukhtasar on qisas (retaliation) for intentional killing. The passage establishes that qisas is not automatically triggered by any intentional killing; two precise conditions must be met. Understanding these conditions is essential for correctly applying the law of qisas and distinguishing it from other penalties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is qisas (retaliatory execution) for intentional killing. The ruling is that qisas becomes wajib when two conditions are present.
The passage states: 'Qisas is wajib by killing every person whose blood is permanently inviolable, when he is killed intentionally.'
2
Analyze the two conditions
First, the killing must be intentional ('amd). Second, the victim must be permanently inviolable (mahqoon al-dam 'ala al-ta'bid). The second condition has two purposes: to negate any suspicion that the victim's blood was permissible and to ensure equality between victim and killer.
Intentionality was explained earlier in Kitab al-Jinaayat. Permanent inviolability is the key focus here.
3
List examples of who qualifies and who is excluded
Qualified: Muslims and dhimmis, because their inviolability is permanent. Excluded: harbi kafir, apostate, rebel, and musta'min (temporary safe conduct). For these, qisas is not wajib.
The text explicitly lists these exceptions in the Urdu commentary.
4
Examine the nuance of mu'ammama vs muqawwama protection
A person who accepts Islam in Dar al-Harb gains mu'ammama (provisional) inviolability, but not muqawwama (definitive) inviolability, which requires residence in Dar al-Islam. Thus, qisas is not applied for killing such a person.
This distinction is crucial and is referenced from Kitab al-Siyar.

Source Text

ترجمہ باب ان امور کے بیان میں جو موجب قصاص ہیں اور جو نہیں ہیں

قال القصاص واجب بقتل كل محقون الدم على التابيد اذا قتل عمدا اما العمدية فلما بيناه واما حقن الدم على التابيد فلتنتفى شبهة الاباحة وتتحقق المساواة.

Kitab al-Jinaayat. Chapter: What necessitates qisas and what does not. Translation: Chapter on the explanation of those matters that cause qisas and those that do not. Explanation: The author has already mentioned the types of killing, among which is intentional killing which necessitated qisas, but it does not always make qisas obligatory; rather it sometimes does and sometimes does not. Therefore the need for detail arose. In this chapter, the author will explain its detail. From which killing does qisas become wajib? He said: Qisas is wajib by killing every person whose blood is permanently inviolable, when he is killed intentionally. As for intentionality, it is due to what we have explained. And as for the permanence of inviolability of blood, it is so that the suspicion of permissibility of blood is negated and equality is realized. Translation: Quduri said: Every person who is permanently inviolable of blood, from his killing qisas becomes wajib when he is killed intentionally. As for intentionality, it is due to the proof we have explained. And as for the permanence of inviolability of blood, it is so that the suspicion of permissibility of blood is negated and equality is realized. Explanation: In intentional killing, qisas will be wajib when the victim is a person whose blood is permanently inviolable, like a Muslim or a dhimmi, because the dhimmi's protection is also permanent. A harbi kafir, apostate, rebel, musta'min - all these are excluded from this list; therefore from their killing qisas will not be wajib. Now the author says that Quduri placed two restrictions: (1) Intentionality: its explanation has passed at the beginning of Kitab al-Jinaayat. (2) Permanently inviolable of blood: it has two reasons: (i) If this condition is not there, then the suspicion of the victim being permissible of blood remains, and with suspicion qisas is negated. (ii) So that equality can be established between the victim and the killer; the victim was inviolable of blood, so in exchange for him, the killer who is also inviolable of blood can be killed. Question: If a person becomes Muslim in Dar al-Harb, he also becomes permanently inviolable of blood, yet qisas is not taken from his killer? Answer: By just accepting Islam, he obtained mu'ammama protection (temporary inviolability), and muqawwama protection (permanent inviolability) is obtained from Dar al-Islam, and without acquiring muqawwama protection, qisas will not be taken. (And this research has passed in Kitab al-Siyar.)
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Quduri, commenting on the definition and conditions of qisas. The author first states that qisas is wajib for intentional killing of a person whose blood is permanently inviolable (mahqoon al-dam 'ala al-ta'bid). He then explains the two conditions: intentionality ('amadiyyah) and permanent inviolability. The reason for the second condition is twofold: to negate any suspicion that the victim's blood was permissible (thus removing the basis for qisas), and to ensure equality between victim and killer (both must be equally inviolable). Examples of those with permanently inviolable blood are Muslims and dhimmis. Excluded are harbi kafirs, apostates, rebels, and musta'mins (those given temporary safe conduct). The passage ends with a nuanced question: a person who converts to Islam in Dar al-Harb becomes inviolable, but qisas is not taken for his killing because he only acquires mu'ammama (provisional) inviolability, not muqawwama (definitive) inviolability, which requires residence in Dar al-Islam. The author refers to Kitab al-Siyar for further detail.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment equal to the injury inflicted, specifically capital punishment for intentional homicide.
محقون الدم (mahqoon al-dam): One whose blood is inviolable, i.e., it is unlawful to kill him without legal justification.
على التابيد ('ala al-ta'bid): Permanently; for all time, as opposed to temporary protection (e.g., musta'min).
عصمت مؤحمہ ('ismah mu'ammamah): Temporary or provisional inviolability granted to a person who accepts Islam in Dar al-Harb before migrating.
عصمت مقومہ ('ismah muqawwamah): Definitive inviolability that fully protects the person's life and property, requiring qisas if violated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) To ensure the killer is also inviolable and to negate any suspicion that the victim's blood was permissible.
B) To make the killing more severe.
C) To allow the killer to pay diyah instead.
D) To exclude dhimmis from qisas.

Key Takeaway
Qisas for intentional killing only applies when the victim's blood is permanently inviolable, ensuring justice and removing ambiguity.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
8 min
Free vs. Slave in Qisas: Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is on qisas for free killing slave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on qisas for a free person killing a slave, and explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof.

Core Idea
A free person is executed for killing a slave because equality in 'ismah suffices for qisas.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is: whether qisas applies when a free person kills a slave. The Hanafi school, relying on general Quranic commands, holds that qisas is due. Al-Shafi'i, citing the specific pairing in Quran 2:178 and the principle of equality, argues that it is not. Understanding this dispute illuminates the different usul methodologies each school employs.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that a free person is executed for killing a slave. This is based on general Quranic commands (e.g., 2:178, 5:45) and the principle that qisas relies on equality in 'ismah (inviolability).
'Ismah is determined by Islam or residence in Dar al-Islam, not by social status.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Al-Shafi'i holds that a free person is not executed for killing a slave. His position is based on the specific Quranic pairing 'the free for the free, the slave for the slave' (2:178) and the requirement of full equality between killer and victim.
Al-Shafi'i also uses an analogy from limbs: a free person's limb is not cut for a slave's limb.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Al-Shafi'i argues that the pairing in the verse implies that a free person is only accountable for a free victim. He also claims that qisas requires equality, which is absent between a free person (owner) and a slave (owned).
He further argues that since a free person's limb is not subject to qisas for a slave's limb, a fortiori the life should not be taken.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafis respond that the Quranic pairing is a specification by mention (takhsis bi al-dhikr), not a negation of unmentioned cases. Equality in 'ismah is sufficient for qisas, and both free and slave share this through Islam or abode.
The analogy from limbs is rejected because the rules for limbs differ; the life is protected by 'ismah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In Hanafi fiqh, if a free person kills a slave, qisas is due (unless pardoned). In Shafi'i fiqh, only diyah (blood money) is due.
This difference has practical consequences for judges and muftis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويقتل الحر بالحر والحر بالعبد للعمومات وقال الشافعي لا يقتل الحر بالعبد لقوله تعالى الحر بالحر والعبد بالعبد ومن ضرورة هذه المقابلة ان لا يقتل حر بعبد ولان مبنى القصاص على المساواة وهي منتفية بين المالك والمملوك ولهذا لا يقطع طرف الحر بطرفه وبخلاف العبد حيث يقتل بالحر لانه تفاوت الى نقصان ولنا ان القصاص يعتمد المساواة فى العصمة وهى بالدين او بالدار ويستويان فيهما وجريان القصاص بين العبدين يوذن بانتفاء شبهة الاباحة والنص تخصيص بالذكر فلا ينفى ما عداه
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور آزاد کو قتل کیا جائے گا آزاد کے بدلہ میں اور آزاد کو غلام کے بدلہ میں عمومات کی وجہ سے اور فرمایا شافعی نے کہ حر کو غلام کی وجہ سے قتل نہیں کیا جائے گا اللہ تعالیٰ کے فرمان الحر بالحر والعبد بالعبد کی وجہ سے اور اس مقابلہ کی ضرورت میں سے یہ بات ہے کہ آزاد کو غلام کے بدلہ نہ قتل کیا جائے۔ اور اس لئے کہ قصاص کی بنیاد مساوات پر ہے اور مساوات منتفی ہے آزاد اور غلام کے درمیان اور اسی وجہ سے غلام کے عضو کے بدلہ میں آزاد کا عضو نہیں کاٹا جاتا ہے بخلاف غلام کے بدلہ میں غلام، اس لئے کہ یہ دونوں برابر ہیں اور بخلاف غلام کے اس حیثیت سے کہ اس کو آزاد کے بدلہ قتل کیا جاتا ہے اس لئے کہ تفاوت نقصان کی طرف ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ قصاص اعتماد کرتا ہے عصمت میں برابری پر اور عصمت دین یا دار الاسلام کی وجہ سے ہوتی ہے اور ان دونوں میں یہ برابر ہیں اور دو غلاموں کے درمیان قصاص کا جاری ہونا خبر دیتا ہے اباحت دم کے شبہ کے منتفی ہونے کی اور نص ذکر کے اندر تخصیص ہے تو یہ مذکور کے ماعدا کی نفی نہیں کرے گی۔ تشریح امام شافعی اور صفیہ کے درمیان یہ مسئلہ مختلف فیہ ہے کہ آزاد کو غلام کے بدلہ قصاص میں قتل کیا جائے گا یا نہیں؟ امام شافعی کے یہاں نہیں قتل کیا جائے گا اور ہمارے نزدیک تک کیا جائے گا یہ اختلاف اس صورت میں ہے جب کہ مقتول غلام ہو اور قاتل آزاد ہو ورنہ اگر اس کے بر عکس ہو تو بالاتفاق قصاص ہے یا دونوں غلام ہوں تو بھی بالاتفاق قصاص ہے اور اگر دونوں آزاد ہوں تب بھی بالاتفاق قصاص ہے۔ مختلف فیہ مسئلہ میں ہماری دلیل ان دلائل کا عموم ہے جیسے كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمُ الْقِصَاصُ فِي الْقَتْلَىٰ اور جیسے وَكَتَبْنَا عَلَيْهِمْ فِيهَا أَنَّ النَّفْسَ بِالنَّفْسِ، اور جیسے الحمد قوو، امام شافعی نے اس آیت سے استدلال کیا ہے الحر بالحر والعبد بالعبد، یہاں غلام کا غلام سے اور حر کا حر سے مقابلہ بتاتا ہے کہ غلام کے بدلہ میں حر کو قتل نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ امام شافعی کی عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قصاص کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ قاتل اور مقتول کے درمیان مساوات ہو اور مالک اور مملوک اور قادر و عاجز میں کوئی مساوات نہیں ہے لہذا قصاص بھی نہ ہو گا۔ امام شافعی نے ایک دلیل یہ بھی بیان فرمائی کہ اگر آزاد شخص کسی غلام کا کوئی عضو کاٹ دے تو آزاد کا عضو قصاص میں نہیں کاٹا جائے گا حالانکہ عضو سے زیادہ محترم نفس ہے تو جب عضو میں قصاص نہیں لیا گیا تو نفس کے اندر بدرجہ اولی نہیں لیا جائے گا۔ امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ البتہ اگر دونوں غلام ہوں تو قاتل غلام سے قصاص لیا جائے گا کیونکہ دونوں برابر ہیں۔ سوال: اے امام شافعی! اگر غلام کسی آزاد شخص کو قتل کر دے تو غلام سے کیوں قصاص کے قائل ہو جب کہ یہاں قاتل و مقتول میں مساوات نہیں ہے؟ جواب... امام شافعی نے جواب دیا کہ ہاں مساوات تو نہیں ہے مگر یہاں کی اور قصور قاتل میں ہے اور اس کے عکس میں قصور ونقصان مقتول میں تھا اس وجہ سے میں نے اس تفاوت و نقصان کو جو قاتل میں ہے مانع قصاص شمار نہیں کیا ہے، یہ سب دلائل امام شافعی کے تھے۔
He said: The free person is killed for the free and the free for the slave, due to general proofs. And al-Shafi'i said: The free is not killed for the slave because of the verse: 'The free for the free, and the slave for the slave.' And from the necessity of this pairing is that a free person is not killed for a slave. And because the basis of qisas is equality, and it is absent between owner and owned, and for this reason a free person's limb is not cut for a slave's limb. But a slave is killed for a free person because the disparity is toward deficiency. Our proof: Qisas is based on equality in 'ismah (inviolability), which is by religion or by abode, and both are equal in these. And the application of qisas between two slaves indicates negation of suspicion of permissibility of blood. And the text is a specification by mention, so it does not negate what is other than it. Translation: Quduri said: The free person is killed in exchange for a free person and the free person in exchange for a slave, due to general proofs. And al-Shafi'i said: A free person is not killed for a slave because of Allah's saying: 'The free for the free, and the slave for the slave.' And from the necessity of this pairing is that a free person should not be killed for a slave. And because the basis of qisas is equality, and equality is absent between a free person and a slave, and for this reason a free person's limb is not cut for a slave's limb. But a slave is killed for a free person because the disparity is toward deficiency (i.e., the slave's deficiency in status does not prevent qisas when he kills a free person). Our proof: Qisas relies on equality in 'ismah, and 'ismah is by religion or by abode, and both are equal in these. And the application of qisas between two slaves indicates the negation of suspicion of permissibility of blood. And the text is a specification by mention, so it does not negate what is other than it. Explanation: This issue is disputed between Imam al-Shafi'i and the Hanafis: whether a free person is killed in qisas for a slave or not. With al-Shafi'i, he is not killed; with us, he is killed. This difference is when the victim is a slave and the killer is free. If the opposite (slave kills free), there is consensus on qisas. If both are slaves, also consensus on qisas. If both are free, also consensus. Our proof in the disputed issue is the generality of proofs like: 'Qisas is prescribed for you in cases of murder' (2:178) and 'We ordained for them: a life for a life' (5:45), and similar general texts. Al-Shafi'i deduces from the verse 'The free for the free, and the slave for the slave.' The pairing indicates that a free person is not killed for a slave. His rational proof: Qisas requires equality between killer and victim, and there is no equality between owner and owned, powerful and powerless, so qisas will not apply. He also argues: If a free person cuts off a slave's limb, the free person's limb is not cut in qisas, even though the life is more revered than a limb; if qisas is not taken for a limb, then a fortiori it should not be taken for life. He says that if both are slaves, qisas is taken because they are equal. Question to al-Shafi'i: If a slave kills a free person, why do you hold qisas from the slave, even though equality is absent? Answer: Yes, equality is absent, but here the deficiency is in the killer, whereas in the opposite case the deficiency was in the victim. Therefore I do not consider the disparity in the killer as an obstacle to qisas. These are all the proofs of al-Shafi'i.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis (followers of Abu Hanifa) and the Shafi'is (followers of al-Shafi'i) regarding whether a free person can be executed in qisas for killing a slave. The Hanafi position, based on general Quranic commands (such as 2:178 and 5:45), is that a free person can be executed for killing a slave because both share equality in 'ismah (inviolability)—either through Islam or residence in Dar al-Islam. The Shafi'i position, relying on the specific Quranic pairing in 2:178 ('The free for the free, the slave for the slave'), and on the principle of equality, holds that a free person cannot be executed for a slave. The Shafi'i also analogize from the case of limbs: if a free person's limb is not cut for a slave's limb, then life (which is more significant) should also not be taken. However, the Shafi'i makes an exception: if a slave kills a free person, qisas is applicable because the deficiency is in the killer, not the victim. The Hanafi response argues that the Quranic pairing is a specification by mention (takhsis), not a negation of other cases, and that equality in 'ismah suffices. The passage also clarifies points of consensus: qisas applies when the killer and victim are of the same status (free/free or slave/slave), and when a slave kills a free person (Shafi'i agrees due to deficiency in the killer).

Key Terms
عمومات ('umumat): General proofs (from Quran and Sunnah) that apply to all cases unless specified otherwise.
المساواة في العصمة (al-musawat fi al-'ismah): Equality in inviolability: both parties must have equal protection of life under Islamic law.
تخصيص بالذكر (takhsis bi al-dhikr): Specification by mention: the verse specifically mentions certain cases but does not negate others.
تفاوت إلى نقصان (tafawut ila nuqsan): Disparity toward deficiency: when the killer is of lower status than the victim, the inequality does not prevent qisas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary textual evidence used by Al-Shafi'i to argue that a free person should not be executed for killing a slave?
A) General Quranic commands like 'Kutiba alaykum al-qisas'
B) The specific verse 'Al-hurr bi al-hurr wa al-abd bi al-abd'
C) The principle of 'ismah
D) Consensus of the Companions

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a free person is executed for killing a slave based on general Quranic commands and equality in 'ismah, while Shafi'is require equal social status, citing the specific pairing in the Quran.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
10 min
Qiṣāṣ Between Free and Slave: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Dispute over whether a free person may be executed for a slave in retribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on qiṣāṣ for a free person killing a slave, explain the Hanafi proof based on equality in ʿiṣma, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the verse "al-ḥurru bil-ḥurri".

Core Idea
Qiṣāṣ requires equality in protection (ʿiṣma), not social status — both free and slave Muslims are equally protected.

The question of whether a free person can be executed for murdering a slave touches on the very definition of legal equality in Islamic criminal law. Two major schools — the Hanafis and Shafi'is — arrive at opposite conclusions based on how they interpret the Qur'anic verses on qiṣāṣ. In this lesson, we will unpack the arguments of both sides and see how the Hanafi school's principle of equality in ʿiṣma leads to the ruling that a free Muslim may be put to death for killing a slave Muslim.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling the Hanafi school holds regarding qiṣāṣ when a free person kills a slave.
The ruling applies when both are Muslims and resident in Dār al-Islam.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Which school disagrees and what is their ruling?
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the free person is not executed.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i dalil: the Qur'anic verse 'al-ḥurru bil-ḥurri wa'l-ʿabdu bil-ʿabd' and the analogy from limb qiṣāṣ.
They argue no equality in status.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school rebut these proofs? Focus on the redefinition of equality (ʿiṣma) and the rejection of mafhūm al-mukhālafa.
Also note the claim of abrogation by Imām Suyūṭī.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference in rulings between the two schools?
Hanafi: free executed; Shafi'i: only compensation.

سوال: اے امام شافعی ! اگر غلام کسی آزاد شخص کو قتل کر دے تو غلام سے کیوں قصاص کے قائل ہو جب کہ یہاں قاتل و مقتول میں مساوات نہیں ہے؟

قلت علامہ سیوطی نے در منشور میں اس آیت کو منسوخ قرار دیا ہے اور اس کا ناسخ النفس بالنفس کو قرار دیا ہے لہذا اس تحقیق کے مطابق آیت مذکورہ سے استدلال ہی صحیح نہ ہوگا۔
The chapter on injuries. Ashraf al-Bidaya Urdu commentary on Hidayah vol. 15. (Matn:) Our proof: Qiṣāṣ depends on equality in protection, which is by religion or by abode, and both are equal in these. The execution of qiṣāṣ between two slaves indicates the absence of any doubt of permissibility. The text specifies by mention, so it does not negate what is beyond. (Translation:) Al-Quduri said: The free person is killed for the free person and the free person is killed for the slave due to generalities. Al-Shafi'i said that a free person is not killed for a slave because of Allah's statement 'the free for the free and the slave for the slave' and because qiṣāṣ requires equality, which is absent between free and slave, and similarly the limb of a free person is not qisas'd for the limb of a slave, unlike slave for slave. Our proof: Qiṣāṣ relies on equality in protection, which is achieved by Islam or dar al-Islam, and both are equal in this. The execution of qiṣāṣ between two slaves indicates the negation of the doubt of permissibility. The text is a specification by mention, so it does not negate what is not mentioned. Explanation: This issue is disputed between Imam Shafi'i and us: whether a free person is killed in qiṣāṣ for a slave. According to Shafi'i, no; according to us, yes. This dispute is when the victim is a slave and the killer is free; otherwise, if the opposite, or both slaves, or both free, there is consensus. Our proof is the generality of verses like 'qiṣāṣ is prescribed for you in killing' and 'We prescribed for them that a life for a life' and [others]. Shafi'i argued from the verse 'the free for the free and the slave for the slave'. His rational proof is that qiṣāṣ requires equality and there is no equality between master and slave, capable and incapable. Also, if a free person cuts a slave's limb, his limb is not subject to qiṣāṣ, so a fortiori for life. He added that if both are slaves, qiṣāṣ applies. Question to Imam Shafi'i: If a slave kills a free person, why do you allow qiṣāṣ against the slave? Answer: There is no equality, but the deficiency is in the killer, unlike the previous case. These are Shafi'i's proofs. Then Hanafi proofs: Equality must be in protection, not status; both are Muslims in dar al-Islam, so equal. Also the consensus on qiṣāṣ between two slaves proves the slave's protection is complete. The response to the textual proof: The verse only specifies what it mentions; it does not negate what is not mentioned (non-existent opposite meaning). The commentary then cites the principle that specification by name does not negate the ruling for others, and this was done in the lesson of al-Husami. I say: Imam Suyuti declared this verse abrogated in al-Durr al-Manthur, with the abrogator being 'a life for a life'. So according to this research, the proof from that verse is invalid.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding whether a free person can be executed in retribution (qiṣāṣ) for killing a slave. The Hanafi position is that a free person may be executed for a slave, while the Shafi'i position is that he may not. The passage begins by quoting the matn (original text) from al-Quduri, then expands with the author's commentary. 
The Shafi'i school relies on the Qur'anic verse 'al-ḥurru bil-ḥurri wa'l-ʿabdu bil-ʿabd' (the free for the free, the slave for the slave), interpreting it to mean that qiṣāṣ only applies within the same status category. They also argue that qiṣāṣ requires complete equality between killer and victim, which does not exist between a free person and a slave—just as limbs are not subject to qiṣāṣ across these categories. 
The Hanafi school responds by redefining the requirement: qiṣāṣ requires equality in 'iṣma (protection), not in social status. Both free and slave Muslims are equally protected by Islam and residence in Dār al-Islam, so qiṣāṣ applies. The fact that qiṣāṣ is unanimously valid between two slaves proves that a slave's blood is fully protected. As for the Shafi'i proof text, the Hanafis argue that the verse merely specifies some cases without negating others; in Hanafi uṣūl, a specification by mention does not establish a negative implication (mafhūm al-mukhālafa is not accepted). The passage also notes that Imām Suyūṭī considered the verse abrogated by the hadith 'an-nafsu bin-nafs'. Thus, the Hanafi position is supported by both uṣūl and historical evidence.

Key Terms
قصاص (qiṣāṣ): Retaliatory justice equating the penalty with the crime, specifically execution for homicide.
عصمة (ʿiṣma): Inviolability of life and property; protection from being lawfully killed except for just cause.
تخصيص (takhṣīṣ): Specification of a general term; here, the verse specifies certain cases by mentioning them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because both are equally protected by Islam and Dār al-Islam.
C) Because the Qur'an explicitly says 'the free for the slave'.
D) Because the free person's social status is irrelevant in qiṣāṣ.

Key Takeaway
A free Muslim may be executed for killing a slave because they share equal protection (ʿiṣma) through Islam and Dār al-Islam, a principle the Hanafi school upholds against the Shafi'i objection.

Qisas — Retaliation

Qisas Between Muslim and Dhimmi: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Dispute over executing a Muslim for killing a dhimmi in retribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on qiṣāṣ for a Muslim who kills a dhimmi, explain the Shafi'i proof, and evaluate the Hanafi response based on textual evidence.

Core Idea
Prophetic practice overrides the general hadith: a Muslim is executed for a dhimmi because protection (iṣma) is equal.

In this lesson, we examine a classic inter-madhhab dispute: whether a Muslim may face qiṣāṣ (retributive execution) for killing a dhimmi (protected non-Muslim citizen). The Hanafi school, based on Prophetic practice and a nuanced understanding of equality in legal protection, affirms the execution. The Shafi'i school, relying on the general hadith 'A believer is not killed for a disbeliever,' denies it. We will follow the argument from Al-Hidayah, analyzing the proofs of both schools and their practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: the Hanafi school holds that a Muslim who kills a dhimmi is executed in qiṣāṣ.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that a Muslim is not executed for a dhimmi; the killer only pays diya and performs kaffara.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i proof is the hadith 'Lā yuqtalu mu'minun bi kāfir' and the argument that lack of religious equality creates doubt (shubha).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis cite the Prophet's own act of executing a Muslim for a dhimmi, argue that equality is in protection (iṣma) not religion, and reinterpret the Shafi'i hadith as referring to a combatant (ḥarbī) based on its context.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi law, a Muslim is executed; under Shafi'i law, only diya and expiation are required.

Commentary
This passage presents the second inter-madhhab dispute in this window: whether a Muslim may be executed in qiṣāṣ for killing a dhimmi (a non-Muslim citizen under Muslim protection). The Hanafi position is that the Muslim is executed for the dhimmi, while the Shafi'i position is that he is not. The passage begins by quoting the matn from al-Quduri, then provides the Shafi'i proof: the hadith 'Lā yuqtalu mu'minun bi kāfir' (A believer is not killed for a disbeliever) and the argument that there is no equality between the two parties, and disbelief creates a doubt (shubha) that prevents qiṣāṣ. The Hanafis counter with a narration that the Prophet ﷺ himself executed a Muslim for a dhimmi, establishing the rule by practice. They further argue that equality in protection (iṣma) is based on obligation (taklīf) and abode (dār), not religion, and that the permissibility of blood only applies to a combatant (ḥarbī), not a peaceful dhimmi. They also reinterpret the Shafi'i hadith, arguing that its context refers to a combatant, not a dhimmi, by noting the phrase 'wa lā dhu 'ahd' (nor a person of covenant) in another version, which shows the hadith is exclusive. The passage also addresses that the fact that a dhimmi is killed for a dhimmi (by consensus) negates any doubt about the dhimmi's blood protection. The text then begins an explanation (tashrīḥ) in Urdu but cuts off mid-sentence. It clarifies that the dispute is only when a Muslim kills a dhimmi; if a dhimmi kills a Muslim, or both are Muslim or both dhimmi, there is consensus. Imam Shafi'i, according to the passage, does not accept qiṣāṣ due to lack of equality, but the text becomes unclear.

Key Terms
ذمي (dhimmī): A non-Muslim living under Muslim rule with a covenant of protection (dhimmah), enjoying safety of life and property.
حربي (ḥarbī): A non-Muslim not under Muslim protection, with whom a state of war exists; his blood is not protected.
مساوات (musāwāt): Equality required for qiṣāṣ; Shafi'is see it as religious, Hanafis see it as protective (iṣma).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The dhimmi's family waives their right to qiṣāṣ.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a Muslim is executed in qiṣāṣ for a dhimmi because the basis of qiṣāṣ is equality in protection (iṣma), not religion, as demonstrated by Prophetic practice.

Qisas — Retaliation

Equality of Free and Slave in Qisas
Arguing for equality in ismah between free and slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for equality in qisas and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on mafhum mukhalaf.

Core Idea
Equality in qisas is based on inviolability (ismah), not social status — the slave's blood is fully protected.

The key question in this lesson is whether a free man can be executed for killing a slave. The Hanafi school argues that both are equal in inviolability (ismah) because both are Muslims in Dar al-Islam, so the free man's life is forfeit. The Shafi'i school objects, citing a Quranic verse that seems to require equality in freedom. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi response, focusing on the rejection of mafhum mukhalaf and the consensus on slave-slave qisas.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: the Hanafis hold that qisas applies when killer and victim are equal in ismah, regardless of free or slave status.
The Hanafi position is that both free and slave Muslims have full ismah because they are Muslims in Dar al-Islam.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that equality in social status is required; a free man is not killed for a slave.
The Shafi'i view is based on a literal reading of the Quranic verse and the principle of mafhum mukhalaf.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i dalil: the verse specifying 'free for free, slave for slave' implies that qisas is limited to like-for-like in freedom.
Shafi'is argue that mentioning the specific cases negates the ruling for unmentioned cases (mafhum mukhalaf).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that mafhum mukhalaf is not a valid proof. They also cite the consensus that qisas applies when both are slaves, proving the slave's ismah is complete.
Additionally, the verse may be abrogated by 'the soul for the soul' (al-Nafs bi al-Nafs).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis allow qisas of a free man for a slave; Shafi'is do not.
This affects actual legal proceedings in jurisdictions applying these schools.

Inviolability is obtained through Islam and the Abode of Islam. Here, both the free and the slave are Muslims and both are in the Abode of Islam, so both are inviolable and there is equality between them.
