Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the condition of equality in qisas, specifically whether a free man can be executed in retribution for killing a slave. The Hanafi position is that equality is based on inviolability (ismah), not on social status. Both free and slave Muslims have complete ismah because they are Muslims residing in Dar al-Islam. The commentator provides an additional proof: if both parties are slaves, qisas is unanimously applied, indicating that the slave's blood is fully protected. The text then refutes the Shafi'i argument that a specific Quranic verse (presumably mentioning free for free, slave for slave) restricts qisas to like-for-like in status. The Hanafi response is that the verse does not explicitly negate qisas between free and slave, and the principle of mafhum mukhalaf (converse meaning) is not accepted in the Hanafi school. Finally, a note from Allama Suyuti suggests the verse is abrogated by 'the soul for the soul' (al-Nafs bi al-Nafs), weakening the Shafi'i proof further.

Key Terms
عصمت (ismah): Inviolability or protection of life; the quality that makes one's blood unlawful to shed without legal cause.
مساوات (musawat): Equality between the killer and victim as a condition for qisas. Hanafis require equality in ismah, not in freedom or social status.
مفهوم مخالف (mafhum mukhalaf): The converse meaning of a text; the implication that a ruling mentioned for a specific case does not apply to other cases.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
8 min
Qisas for a Muslim Killing a Dhimmi: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute with proofs and counter-arguments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on qisas for a Muslim who kills a dhimmi and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
A Muslim is killed in qisas for a dhimmi because dhimmi's ismah is complete; kufr only permits blood of a harbi.

The Hanafi school holds that a Muslim who intentionally kills a dhimmi is subject to qisas (retributive execution). This lesson examines the foundational dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who argues that a believer is not killed for a disbeliever. We will dissect the proofs on both sides and understand the Hanafi response that limits the Shafi'i hadith to combatants (harbi) and affirms the full inviolability of a dhimmi.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the Hanafi position
Clearly articulate the contested ruling: Is qisas applied when a Muslim kills a dhimmi? State the Hanafi position that it is wajib.
The Hanafi position is from al-Quduri's matn.
2
Identify the Shafi'i proof and reasoning
Examine the Shafi'i evidence: the hadith 'لا يقتل مؤمن بكافر' and the rationale that kufr creates doubt (shubha) preventing qisas due to lack of equality.
Shafi'i also relies on the general principle of equality.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof and response
Study the Hanafi evidence: the specific action of the Prophet (killing a Muslim for a dhimmi), the arguments for equality in ismah through taklif or dar, and the distinction that kufr is only mubih for harbis.
The Hanafis interpret the Shafi'i hadith as referring to a harbi, not a dhimmi.
4
Compare the two proofs and identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Contrast the weight of evidence: specific Prophetic action vs. general hadith. Note the practical consequence: Hanafis execute, Shafi'is impose diyah only.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
Conclude why the Hanafi position is relied upon, citing the strength of direct Prophetic action and the consensus that a dhimmi is killed for a dhimmi.
The Hanafi position is supported by Zahir al-Riwayah.

مسلمان کو ذمی کے بدلے قصاص میں قتل کیا جائے گا یا نہیں ، احناف اور شوافع کے مابین الاختلاف
قال والمسلم بالذمى خلافا للشافعى له قول عليه السلام لا يقتل مومن بكافر لانه لا مساواة وقت الجناية وكذا الكفر مبيح فيورث الشبهة ولنا ما روى ان النبي عليه السلام قتل مسلما بذمى ولان المساواة في العصمة ثابتة نظرا الى التكليف او الدار والمبيح كفر المحارب دون المسالم والقتل بمثله يوذن بانتفاء الشبهة والمراد بماروى الحربي لسياقه ولا ذو عهد والعطف للمغايرة
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور قتل کیا جائے گا مسلمان ذمی کے بدلہ اختلاف ہے شافعی کا دلیل شافعی فرمان نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم ہے کہ کافر کے بدلہ مومن کو نہیں قتل کیا جائے گا اور اس لئے کہ بوقت جنایت ان دونوں کے درمیان کوئی مساوات نہیں ہے اور ایسے ہی کفر میسج ہے تو یہ شبہ پیدا کرے گا اور ہماری دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جو مروی ہے کہ نبی علیہ السلام نے ذمی کے بدلہ مسلمان کو قتل کیا اور اس لئے کہ مساوات عصمت میں ثابت ہے تکلیف یا دار کی جانب نسبت کرتے ہوئے اور صبیح محارب کا کفر ہے نہ کہ مسالم کا اور ذمی کا قتل کیا جانا اپنے مثل کے بدلہ شبہ کے ختم ہونے کی نفی کرتا ہے اور مراد اس حدیث سے جو شافعی نے روایت کی حربی ہے سیاق حدیث کی وجہ سے ( اور وہ ) ولا ذو عہد فی عبدہ ہے اور عطف مغایرت کے لئے ہوتا ہے۔
تشریح اگر مسلمان نے ذمی کوقتل کر دیا تو ذی کے بدلہ میں قصاصا مسلمان کو قل کیا جائے گا یا نہیں؟ اس میں بھی ہمارا اور شافعی کا اختلاف ہے۔ امام شافعی عدم مساوات کی وجہ سے قصاص کے قائل نہیں اور خفیہ قصاص کے قائل ہیں اور مساوات ثابت مانتے ہیں۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ حدیث میں ہے لا يقتل مؤمن بكافر (رواہ ابوداؤد ) اس سے صاف واضح ہے کہ کافر کے بدلہ میں مسلمان کو قتل نہیں کیا جائے گا کیونکہ ذمی کافر ہے اور بوقت قتل کفر اس میں موجود ہے اور کفر فی نفسہ اباحت کا سبب ہے تو اس میں عدم مساوات کا شبہ موجود ہے اور جب مشبہ پایا گیا تو قصاص ساقط ہو گیا۔ ہماری دلیل دار قطنی کی روایت ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ایک مسلمان کو قصاص میں قتل کیا تھا جس نے ذمی کو قتل کر دیا تھا۔ ه لان المساواة .. الخ - امام شافعی کے نزدیک نفس آدمیت حصول عصمت کا سبب ہے جس کی تفصیل ہدایہ جلد ثانی کتاب السیر - میں مذکور ہے اور ذمی بھی آدمی ہے اور وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ آدمی اس لئے پیدا کیا گیا ہے کہ وہ تکالیف شرعیہ کا مکلف ہو اور اس تکلیف کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ اس سے تعرض حرام۔ خلاصہ کلام امام شافعی کے نزدیک نفس آدمیت سے عصمت مؤشمہ ثابت ہو جاتی ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک عصمت مکر مہ اسلام سے حاصل ہوتی ہے اور عصمت مقومہ دارالاسلام سے حاصل ہوتی ہے تو ذمی آدمی بھی ہے اور دار الاسلام کا باشندہ بھی ہے تو امام پانی کے اعتبار سے دیکھیں جب بھی مسلمان اور ذمی میں مساوات ہے اور اگر منفیہ کے اعتبار سے دیکھیں جب بھی ان دونوں میں مساوات ہے الی التکلیف یعنی عند الشافعی او الدار یعنی عندنا اور امام شافعی یہ آپ نے جو فرمایا کہ کفر بیج ہے۔ یہ مطلقاً درست نہیں ہے بلکہ حربی کا کفر صیح ہے مسالم (ذمی ) کا کفر میسج نہیں ہے۔ اور جناب والا ذمی کو ذمی کے بدلہ میں بالاتفاق قتل کیا جاتا ہے۔ یقیل اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ اس کی عصمت دم میں کوئی شبہ نہیں ہے ورنہ قصاص جاری نہ ہوتا۔ رہی امام شافعی کی روایت کردہ حدیث تو وہاں کا فر سے مراد ربی ہے اور اس کے ہم بھی قائل ہیں کہ حربی کے بدلہ میں مسلمان کو قتل نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ پوری حدیث اس طرح ہے لا يقتل مؤمن بكافر ولا دو عهد في عهده يعني مسلمان کو اور ڈمی کو کافر کے بدلہ میں قتل نہیں کیا جائے گا حالانکہ اگر ذمی ذمی کو قتل کرے تو اس میں بالا تفاق قصاص واجب ہے اور یہاں فرمایا گیا ہے کہ ذمی کو کافر کے بدلہ قتل نہیں کیا جائے گا جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ یہاں کافر سے مراد کا فرحربی ہے۔ سوال یہ بھی تو ہو سکتا ہے کہ یہاں ذو عبد سے مراد مسلمان ہو اور مطلب یہ ہو کہ اگر کوئی مسلمان امان لے کر دار الحرب میں جائے اور وہاں کسی کا فر کو قتل کر دے تو اس نے حرام کیا لیکن وہ مسلمان اس کا فر کے بدلہ میں قتل نہیں کیا جائے گا ؟ جواب دو عہد کا مؤمن پر عطف ہے اور عطف مغامرت کو چاہتا ہے اس لئے ضروری ہے کہ ذوعہد سے غیر مومن مراد ہو اور وہ ذمی ہے باقی تفسیر ظاہر ہے۔ یہاں شراح کرام نے بہت طول سے کام لیا ہے اور عجیب عجیب باتیں لکھی ہیں۔
Will a Muslim be killed in qisas for a dhimmi? Difference between Hanafis and Shafi'is. He (al-Quduri) said: The Muslim is killed for the dhimmi, contrary to al-Shafi'i. His evidence is the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'A believer is not killed for a disbeliever' because there is no equality at the time of the crime. Similarly, disbelief is a permissibility (mubah) factor, so it creates a doubt. Our evidence is what is narrated that the Prophet, peace be upon him, killed a Muslim for a dhimmi. Also because equality in inviolability is established with respect to obligation (taklif) or the abode (dar). The permissibility factor is the disbelief of a combatant, not of a peaceful one. Killing him with his like indicates the removal of doubt. The intended meaning of what is narrated is the combatant (harbi) due to its context, and 'nor a person of covenant in his covenant', and the conjunctive is for differentiation. Translation: Al-Quduri said: A Muslim will be killed in exchange for a dhimmi; there is a difference with al-Shafi'i. Shafi'i's evidence: the Prophet's saying: 'A believer is not killed for a disbeliever' because there is no equality at the time of the crime, and similarly disbelief is a permissibly thing, so it creates doubt. Our evidence: the hadith narrated that the Prophet killed a Muslim for a dhimmi, and because equality in inviolability is established with regard to taklif or dar, and the permissibility factor is the disbelief of a combatant not a peaceful dhimmi, and that a dhimmi being killed for his like indicates the removal of doubt. The hadith narrated by Shafi'i refers to a harbi, due to its context: 'nor a person of covenant in his covenant', and the conjunction is for differentiation. Elaboration: If a Muslim kills a dhimmi, will the Muslim be killed in qisas for the dhimmi? Here too there is a difference between us and Shafi'i. Imam Shafi'i does not accept qisas due to lack of equality, but he does accept diyah. He says that equality is not established. Imam Shafi'i states: The hadith 'A believer is not killed for a disbeliever' (narrated by Abu Dawud) clearly shows that a Muslim will not be killed for a disbeliever because the dhimmi is a disbeliever, and at the time of the killing disbelief is present, and disbelief itself is a cause of permissibility, so there is a doubt of inequality, and when doubt exists, qisas is dropped. Our evidence: the narration of al-Daraqutni that the Prophet killed a Muslim in qisas who had killed a dhimmi. 'Because equality...' etc. According to Imam Shafi'i, being a human (Adam) is the cause of obtaining ismah, as detailed in al-Hidayah Volume 2, Book of Siyar. The dhimmi is also a human, and he says that humans are created to be obligated by shariah rulings, and for that obligation it is necessary that harming them be prohibited. In summary, for Imam Shafi'i, ismah is proven by being human. For us, ismah is obtained by Islam, and ismah is established by Dar al-Islam. So the dhimmi is both human and a resident of Dar al-Islam. So from the perspective of ismah, there is equality between Muslim and dhimmi. And if we look from the negative perspective, there is also equality. (The phrase 'ila al-taklif' refers to Shafi'i's view, and 'aw al-dar' refers to our view.) And Imam Shafi'i's statement that disbelief is a permissibility factor is not absolutely correct; rather, the disbelief of a harbi is a permissibility factor, not that of a dhimmi. And oh sir, a dhimmi is killed for a dhimmi by consensus. This is proof that there is no doubt in his ismah; otherwise qisas would not apply. As for the hadith narrated by Shafi'i, the 'disbeliever' there means a harbi, and we also hold that a Muslim is not killed for a harbi. The full hadith is: 'A believer is not killed for a disbeliever, and nor a person of covenant in his covenant.' This means a Muslim and a dhimmi will not be killed for a disbeliever. But if a dhimmi kills a dhimmi, qisas is wajib by consensus, and here it is said that a dhimmi will not be killed for a disbeliever, which indicates that 'disbeliever' here means a harbi. There is also the question: could it be that 'dhu 'ahd' here means a Muslim, and the meaning is that if a Muslim enters Dar al-Harb with aman and kills a disbeliever there, he has committed a sin but will not be killed in qisas? Answer: 'Dhu 'ahd' is conjoined to 'mu'min', and conjunction requires differentiation, so it is necessary that 'dhu 'ahd' refers to other than a believer, and that is the dhimmi. The rest of the interpretation is clear. The commentators have gone to great length and written strange things.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage addresses the inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding whether a Muslim is executed in qisas for killing a dhimmi (a non-Muslim under Muslim protection). The text begins by stating the Hanafi position from al-Quduri: a Muslim is killed for a dhimmi. It then presents the Shafi'i evidence: the hadith 'A believer is not killed for a disbeliever' and the argument that at the time of the crime, there is no equality because the victim is a disbeliever, and disbelief causes permissibility of blood, creating a doubt that invalidates qisas. The Hanafi response includes: (1) a specific hadith from al-Daraqutni that the Prophet actually killed a Muslim for a dhimmi; (2) equality in ismah is established either by the obligation of shariah (taklif) according to Shafi'i or by residence in Dar al-Islam according to Hanafis; (3) the permissibility factor (kufr as mubih) applies only to a harbi (combatant), not a dhimmi; (4) the Shafi'i hadith is interpreted to refer to a harbi, as the full text includes 'and nor a person of covenant in his covenant', which shows the exception for dhimmi; (5) the consensus that a dhimmi is killed for a dhimmi proves the completeness of a dhimmi's ismah. The commentator also clarifies that the Hanafi view is that ismah comes from Islam and Dar al-Islam, not just from being human, and that a dhimmi, though a disbeliever, is not like a harbi because he is under the protection of the Islamic state. The overall conclusion is that qisas is wajib for a Muslim who kills a dhimmi.

Key Terms
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim citizen of an Islamic state who is granted protection (dhimma) and has the right to practice his religion in exchange for payment of jizyah.
مبيح (mubih): That which makes permissible; here, the attribute of disbelief that makes shedding blood permissible in some contexts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) لا يقتل مؤمن بكافر
B) أن النبي قتل مسلما بذمي
C) النفس بالنفس
D) لا ذو عهد في عهده

Key Takeaway
A Muslim who kills a dhimmi is subject to qisas in Hanafi fiqh because the dhimmi's inviolability is complete, unlike a harbi.

No Qisas for Killing a Musta'min
Ruling with proof (ta'lil) — no qisas for musta'min

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas for killing a musta'min and explain the two-part reasoning (ta'lil) that justifies it.

Core Idea
A musta'min's blood is not perpetually protected, so qisas does not apply between a Muslim and a musta'min.

This lesson presents a concise ruling from al-Quduri: a Muslim who kills a musta'min is not subject to qisas. The reasoning is built on two legal grounds: the temporary nature of the musta'min's inviolability and the fact that his disbelief incites war. Understanding this ta'lil is key to distinguishing between different categories of non-Muslims in Hanafi criminal law.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the precise hukm: a Muslim is not killed in qisas for killing a musta'min.
2
Identify the first reason
The musta'min's blood is not perpetually protected (ghayr muhaqqan al-dam 'ala al-ta'bid).
Contrast with a dhimmi, whose protection is perpetual.
3
Identify the second reason
The musta'min's disbelief (kufr) incites war (haraab), and he intends to return to Dar al-Harb.
This indicates his fundamental enmity.
4
Connect to the condition of equality in ismah
Qisas requires equal inviolability (ismah) between victim and killer. Since the musta'min lacks perpetual ismah, the condition is not met.
Thus, the ruling is based on a missing condition, not on the act being permissible.

مستامن کے قتل سے قصاص واجب ہے یا نہیں
قال ولا يقتل بالمستا من لأنه غير محقون الدم على التابید و کذلک کفره باعث على الحراب لا نه على قصد الرجوع
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور مسلمان کو مستامن کے بدلہ میں قتل کیا جائے گا اس لئے مستامن تابید کے طریقہ پر محفوظ الدم نہیں ہے اور ایسے ہی اس کا کفر جنگ پر ابھارنے والا ہے اس لئے کہ مستامن لوٹنے کے قصد پر ہے۔
Is qisas wajib for killing a musta'min? He (al-Quduri) said: He (the Muslim) will not be killed for a musta'min, because the musta'min is not protected of blood perpetually, and similarly his disbelief is a motivator for war, because he intends to return. Translation: Al-Quduri said: A Muslim will not be killed in exchange for a musta'min, because the musta'min's blood is not protected on a permanent basis, and also his disbelief incites war, because he intends to return (to his country).
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from al-Quduri, stating that a Muslim is not executed in qisas for killing a musta'min (a non-Muslim who has been granted temporary safe passage into Muslim territory). The reasoning is twofold. First, the musta'min's blood is not protected perpetually (muhaqqan al-dam 'ala al-ta'bid). Unlike a dhimmi or a Muslim, the musta'min's protection is temporary and conditional; he is not a permanent resident of Dar al-Islam. Second, his disbelief is a cause for war (haraab), meaning that he is fundamentally an enemy, and his kufr is of the type that permits killing in some contexts. Additionally, the musta'min intends to return to Dar al-Harb, so his status is not that of a permanent protected person. Therefore, the condition of equality in ismah is not met, and qisas is not applied. This ruling distinguishes the musta'min from a dhimmi, who has perpetual protection through the dhimma contract.

Key Terms
مستأمن (musta'min): A non-Muslim who enters Dar al-Islam under a temporary grant of safety (aman), with the intention of returning to his home country.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a Muslim not killed in qisas for murdering a musta'min according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because a musta'min is not a human
B) Because a musta'min's blood is not perpetually protected
C) Because the musta'min is a disbeliever
D) Because the Muslim is forgiven

Key Takeaway
A Muslim is not executed in qisas for killing a musta'min because the musta'min's protection is temporary and his disbelief incites war, so the equality of ismah is absent.

Qisas — Retaliation

Qisas for Muslim Killing Dhimmi: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is over qisas for Muslim killing dhimmi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on qisas for a Muslim who kills a dhimmi, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and evaluate the Hanafi response based on the distinction between 'ismah mukarramah and muqawwamah.

Core Idea
A Muslim is not killed in qisas for a dhimmi because the dhimmi's inviolability is weaker, creating a doubt of inequality.

In this passage, al-Marghinani presents a foundational dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i over whether a Muslim who kills a dhimmi can be subject to qisas. The disagreement hinges on the nature of inviolability (ismah) and whether equality between killer and victim is absolute or graded. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies the Hanafi emphasis on the source of legal protection and its implications for retribution.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its core reasoning
Identify the Hanafi ruling: qisas is dropped for a Muslim who kills a dhimmi. The reason given is that the dhimmi's disbelief at the time of killing creates a 'shubhat 'adam al-musawat' (suspicion of inequality) because inviolability (ismah) is not at the same level as that of a Muslim.
The Hanafi position is based on the requirement of complete equality (musawat) in inviolability for qisas.
2
Present the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the essence of humanity (nafs al-adamiyya) is the cause of inviolability, so a dhimmi, being human, has full inviolability. Thus, a Muslim should be killed for killing a dhimmi.
Al-Shafi'i's proof is based on the idea that man is created for legal obligation, which requires protection against transgression.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response: the two types of 'ismah
The Hanafi response distinguishes between 'ismah mukarramah (from Islam) and 'ismah muqawwamah (from residence in Dar al-Islam). The dhimmi has only the latter, so his inviolability is not equal to that of a Muslim. Also, disbelief of a harbi is permissible but of a dhimmi is not, so the analogy fails.
This distinction is central to the Hanafi school's graded view of inviolability.
4
Examine the textual proofs
The Hanafi rely on a hadith from al-Daraqutni where the Prophet executed a Muslim for killing a dhimmi, showing that equality existed in that case. The Shafi'i hadith 'La yuqtalu mu'min bikafir' is interpreted by Hanafis to refer to a harbi, not a dhimmi, as confirmed by the conjunction structure and the consensus that a dhimmi is killed for a dhimmi.
Note the linguistic argument (conjunction implies diversity) used to dismiss the Shafi'i hadith.

Source Text

ہماری دلیل دارقطنی کی روایت ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ایک مسلمان کو قصاص میں قتل کیا تھا جس نے ذمی کو قتل کر دیا تھا۔
ه لان المساواة .. الخ - امام شافعی کے نزدیک نفس آدمیت حصول عصمت کا سبب ہے جس کی تفصیل ہدایہ جلد ثانی کتاب السیر - میں مذکور ہے اور ذمی بھی آدمی ہے اور وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ آدمی اس لئے پیدا کیا گیا ہے کہ وہ تکالیف شرعیہ کا مکلف ہو اور اس تکلیف کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ اس سے تعرض حرام۔
خلاصہ کلام امام شافعی کے نزدیک نفس آدمیت سے عصمت مؤشّمة ثابت ہو جاتی ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک عصمت مکرّمة اسلام سے حاصل ہوتی ہے اور عصمت مقوّمہ دارالاسلام سے حاصل ہوتی ہے تو ذمی آدمی بھی ہے اور دار الاسلام کا باشندہ بھی ہے تو امام کے اعتبار سے دیکھیں جب بھی مسلمان اور ذمی میں مساوات ہے اور اگر منفیہ کے اعتبار سے دیکھیں جب بھی ان دونوں میں مساوات ہے الی التکلیف یعنی عند الشافعی او الدار یعنی عندنا اور امام شافعی یہ آپ نے جو فرمایا کہ کفر مباح ہے۔ یہ مطلقاً درست نہیں ہے بلکہ حربی کا کفر مباح ہے مسالم (ذمی ) کا کفر مباح نہیں ہے۔ اور ذمی کو ذمی کے بدلہ میں بالاتفاق قتل کیا جاتا ہے۔ یہ دلیل اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ اس کی عصمت دم میں کوئی شبہ نہیں ہے ورنہ قصاص جاری نہ ہوتا۔ رہی امام شافعی کی روایت کردہ حدیث تو وہاں کافر سے مراد حربی ہے اور اس کے ہم بھی قائل ہیں کہ حربی کے بدلہ میں مسلمان کو قتل نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ پوری حدیث اس طرح ہے لا يقتل مؤمن بكافر ولا ذو عهد في عهده يعني مسلمان کو اور ذمی کو کافر کے بدلہ میں قتل نہیں کیا جائے گا حالانکہ اگر ذمی ذمی کو قتل کرے تو اس میں بالاتفاق قصاص واجب ہے اور یہاں فرمایا گیا ہے کہ ذمی کو کافر کے بدلہ قتل نہیں کیا جائے گا جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ یہاں کافر سے مراد کافر حربی ہے۔ سوال یہ بھی تو ہو سکتا ہے کہ یہاں ذو عهد سے مراد مسلمان ہو اور مطلب یہ ہو کہ اگر کوئی مسلمان امان لے کر دار الحرب میں جائے اور وہاں کسی کافر کو قتل کر دے تو اس نے حرام کیا لیکن وہ مسلمان اس کافر کے بدلہ میں قتل نہیں کیا جائے گا ؟
جواب ذو عهد کا مؤمن پر عطف ہے اور عطف مغایرت کو چاہتا ہے اس لئے ضروری ہے کہ ذو عهد سے غیر مومن مراد ہو اور وہ ذمی ہے باقی تفسیر ظاہر ہے۔ یہاں شارحین کرام نے بہت طول سے کام لیا ہے اور عجیب عجیب باتیں لکھی ہیں۔
Will be carried out because the dhimmi is a disbeliever and at the time of killing disbelief was present in him, and disbelief in itself is a cause of permissibility, so there is a suspicion of inequality, and when a doubt is found, qisas is dropped. Our proof is the narration of al-Daraqutni that the Prophet (peace be upon him) killed a Muslim in qisas for one who had killed a dhimmi. 'He because equality... etc.' - According to Imam al-Shafi'i, the essence of humanity is the cause of acquiring 'ismah, the detail of which is mentioned in al-Hidayah, vol. 2, Kitab al-Siyar, and the dhimmi is also a human, and he says that man was created so that he be obligated with legal duties, and for this obligation it is necessary that transgression against him be forbidden. In summary, according to Imam al-Shafi'i, 'ismah mushammah (probable inviolability) is established from the essence of humanity, and according to us, 'ismah mukarramah (honorable inviolability) is obtained from Islam, and 'ismah muqawwamah (effective inviolability) is obtained from Dar al-Islam. So the dhimmi is both a human and a resident of Dar al-Islam, so from the perspective of the Imam (i.e., Shafi'i) there is equality between Muslim and dhimmi, and from the perspective of negativity there is also equality between them, up to taklif (i.e., according to Shafi'i) or dar (i.e., according to us). And Imam al-Shafi'i's statement that disbelief is permissible is not absolutely correct; rather, the disbelief of a harbi is permissible, the disbelief of a musalim (dhimmi) is not permissible. And a dhimmi is killed for a dhimmi by consensus. This evidence is proof that there is no doubt in the inviolability of his blood, otherwise qisas would not be carried out. As for the hadith narrated by Imam al-Shafi'i, there 'kafir' refers to harbi, and we also agree that a Muslim is not killed for a harbi. The complete hadith is: 'La yuqtalu mu'minun bikafirin wa la dhu 'ahdin fi 'ahdihi', meaning a Muslim and a dhimmi are not killed for a disbeliever, although if a dhimmi kills a dhimmi, qisas is wajib by consensus, and it is stated here that a dhimmi is not killed for a disbeliever, from which it is understood that here 'kafir' means a harbi disbeliever. An objection: Could it be that here 'dhu 'ahd' refers to a Muslim, and the meaning is that if a Muslim enters Dar al-Harb with aman and kills a disbeliever there, he has committed a forbidden act, but that Muslim will not be killed for that disbeliever? Answer: 'Dhu 'ahd' is conjunction to 'mu'min', and conjunction requires diversity, so it is necessary that 'dhu 'ahd' refer to other than a Muslim, and that is the dhimmi. The remaining explanation is clear. The commentators have dealt at length and written strange things.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and al-Shafi'i regarding whether a Muslim is killed in qisas for killing a dhimmi. The author begins by stating the Hanafi position: qisas is dropped because the dhimmi is a kafir, and his disbelief at the time of killing creates a doubt of inequality (shubhat 'adam al-musawat). Since the effective cause ('illa) for qisas is equality in inviolability, and the dhimmi's inviolability is weaker, qisas falls. The Hanafi proof is a hadith from al-Daraqutni that the Prophet (peace be upon him) executed a Muslim for killing a dhimmi. The passage then explains al-Shafi'i's argument: the essence of humanity (nafs al-adamiyya) is the cause of inviolability; since a dhimmi is human, his blood is inviolable, so a Muslim should be killed for him. The Hanafi response distinguishes between two types of inviolability: 'ismah mukarramah (from Islam) and 'ismah muqawwamah (from Dar al-Islam). The dhimmi has the latter but not the former, so equality is not complete. They also rebut Shafi'i's claim that disbelief makes blood permissible: only a harbi's disbelief does so, not a dhimmi's. The hadith 'La yuqtalu mu'min bikafir' is interpreted to refer to a harbi, not a dhimmi, as evidenced by the consensus that a dhimmi is killed for a dhimmi. The passage ends with a discussion of the grammatical structure of the hadith to confirm that 'dhu 'ahd' means dhimmi, not Muslim.

Key Terms
عصمت (ismah): Inviolability or protection of blood; the text distinguishes between 'ismah mukarramah (from Islam) and 'ismah muqawwamah (from Dar al-Islam).
ذمی (dhimmi): A non-Muslim citizen of an Islamic state who has a covenant of protection (dhimma).
حربی (harbi): A non-Muslim who is at war with the Islamic state, i.e., not under a covenant.
مساوات (musawat): Equality between the killer and victim in terms of inviolability (ismah) for the application of qisas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is a Muslim not killed in qisas for killing a dhimmi?
A) Because the dhimmi is not a Muslim, and qisas only applies between Muslims.
B) Because the dhimmi's inviolability (ismah) is less than that of a Muslim, creating a doubt of inequality.
C) Because the dhimmi's blood is absolutely permissible (mubah).
D) Because the Prophet forbade killing a Muslim for a dhimmi.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that qisas for a Muslim killing a dhimmi is not applied due to a doubt of inequality arising from the lower degree of inviolability of the dhimmi, a position grounded in the distinction between 'ismah mukarramah and 'ismah muqawwamah.

Qisas — Retaliation

Qisas with Musta'min: Three Rulings and the Qiyas/Istihsan Conflict
Three rulings on qisas with musta'min victims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi rulings on qisas involving a musta'min and explain why istihsan overrides qiyas in the musta'min-musta'min case.

Core Idea
A musta'min's temporary blood protection means no qisas for killing him; between musta'min, istihsan drops qisas due to mutual permissibility.

The musta'min is a non-Muslim who enters Muslim lands with temporary aman. His status raises questions about qisas (retaliation) if he is killed or kills another. This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies three distinct rulings: when the victim is a musta'min, and when both killer and victim are musta'min. You will work through the proofs, including the tension between qiyas and istihsan that defines the final Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three victim-perpetrator pairs
The text considers three scenarios: Muslim kills musta'min, dhimmi kills musta'min, and musta'min kills musta'min. For each, note whether qisas is wajib or not.
The perpetrator's legal status matters.
2
Understand the reasoning for no qisas when Muslim or dhimmi kills musta'min
The reason is that the musta'min's blood is not permanently protected (ghayr mahqun al-dam ala al-ta'bid). His disbelief incites war because he intends to return to dar al-harb.
Temporary protection does not establish full ismah.
3
Analyze the musta'min-musta'min case: qiyas vs. istihsan
By qiyas, qisas would be wajib due to equality in inviolability. But istihsan overrides because both are mubah al-dam (their killing is permissible) due to lack of permanent protection, so qisas is dropped to avoid perpetuating killing among non-citizens.
This is the key conflict: qiyas requires qisas, istihsan drops it.
4
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The text clearly prefers istihsan. Therefore, a musta'min is not killed in qisas for killing another musta'min. The same applies when a Muslim or dhimmi kills a musta'min: no qisas.
Diyah may still be due, but the passage focuses on qisas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مستامن کے قتل سے قصاص واجب ہے یا نہیں
قال ولا يقتل بالمستا من لأنه غير محقون الدم على التابید و کذلک کفره باعث على الحراب لا نه على قصد الرجوع
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور مسلمان کو مستامن کے بدلہ میں قتل کیا جائے گا اس لئے مستامن تابید کے طریقہ پر محفوظ الدم نہیں ہے اور ایسے ہی اس کا کفر جنگ پر ابھارنے والا ہے اس لئے کہ مستامن لوٹنے کے قصد پر ہے۔
تشریح مستامن کی حفاظت دم میں دوام نہیں ہے لہذا اگر کسی مسلمان نے مستامن کو قتل کر دیا تو قصاص واجب نہ ہوگا اور وہ واپسی کا ارادہ رکھتا ہے تو اس کا کفر اس کو حراب پر برانگیختہ کرنے والا ہے۔
ذمی کومستامن بدلے قصاص میں قتل کیا جائے گا یا نہیں
ولا يقتل الدمى بالمستامن لما بينا ويقتل المستا من با لمستا من قياسا للمساواة ولا يقتل استحسانا
لقيام المبيح
ترجمہ اور ذمی کومستامن کے بدلہ قتل نہیں کیا جائے گا اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور مستامن کو مستامن کے بدام قتل کیا جائے گا ابطور قیاس کے مساوات کی وجہ سے اور استحسانا قتل نہیں کیا جائیگا۔ میچ کے قائم ہونے کی وجہ سے۔
تشریح اگر ڈمی نے مستامن کو قتل کر دیا تو مستامن کے بدلہ ذمی کو قتل نہیں کیا جائے گا کیونکہ مستامن محفوظ الدم دوانا نہیں ہے۔ اگر مستامن نے مستامن کو قتل کر دیا تو اس سے دو قول ہیں۔ کس کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں میں مساوات ہے اس لئے قتل کر دیا جائے۔ اور استحسان کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ ان میں میسیج قتل موجود سے لیڈ اقصاص ند لیا جائے۔
Is qisas wajib for killing a musta'min? He (al-Quduri) said: And he (a Muslim) is not killed for a musta'min because the musta'min is not permanently protected in blood, and likewise his disbelief incites war because he intends to return. Translation: Al-Quduri said: A Muslim is not killed for a musta'min because the musta'min is not permanently protected in blood, and similarly his disbelief incites war because the musta'min intends to return. Commentary: The protection of the musta'min's blood is not permanent, so if a Muslim kills a musta'min, qisas is not wajib, and since he intends to return, his disbelief incites war. Will a dhimmi be killed in qisas for a musta'min? And a dhimmi is not killed for a musta'min for the reason we have stated. And a musta'min is killed for a musta'min by qiyas due to equality, and by istihsan he is not killed due to the existence of the permissible (mubah). Translation: And a dhimmi is not killed for a musta'min for the reason we have stated. And a musta'min is killed for a musta'min by qiyas due to equality, and by istihsan he is not killed due to the existence of the permissible (killing).
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage presents three rulings concerning musta'min (a non-Muslim granted temporary safe passage into Muslim lands). First: If a Muslim kills a musta'min, no qisas is wajib because the musta'min's blood is not permanently protected (he will return to dar al-harb). Second: If a dhimmi kills a musta'min, no qisas is wajib for the same reason. Third: If a musta'min kills another musta'min, there are two positions: by qiyas, qisas is wajib because they are equal in status; but by istihsan, qisas is not wajib because both are equally 'permissible to kill' (mubah al-qatl) in the sense that neither has permanent protection. The relied-upon position is the one of istihsan, as the text indicates. The commentary also notes that the musta'min's disbelief incites war, so his blood is not fully protected.

Key Terms
مستامن (musta'min): A non-Muslim given temporary protection (aman) to enter Muslim lands; he intends to return to dar al-harb.
محقون الدم (mahqun al-dam): One whose blood is protected; i.e., killing him is prohibited. The musta'min is not mahqun al-dam on a permanent basis.
حراب (hirab): War; the musta'min's disbelief incites war because he is not loyal to the Islamic state.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; here it would extend qisas to musta'min-musta'min based on equality.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas due to a stronger consideration; here the existence of mubah (permissible killing) prevents qisas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling by istihsan, if a musta'min kills another musta'min, what is the consequence?
A) Qisas is wajib because of equality.
B) Qisas is not wajib because both are mubah al-dam due to lack of permanent protection.
C) Diyah is wajib but not qisas.
D) The Muslim ruler must execute both.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that no qisas is due for killing a musta'min because the musta'min's blood is not permanently protected, and istihsan overrides qiyas in musta'min-musta'min cases.

Qisas — Retaliation

Equality in Qisas: Basis of Inviolability
List of cases where qisas applies despite personal differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for qisas regarding differences between killer and victim and apply it to cases involving gender, age, and physical condition.

Core Idea
Qisas requires equality in inviolability, not in personal attributes.

This passage from al-Hidayah explains the Hanafi position that qisas is carried out even when the killer and victim differ in gender, age, health, or sanity. The proof is found in the general texts (umumat) of the Quran and Sunnah, which command qisas without making exceptions. Understanding this principle prevents the misconception that such differences preclude retribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the list of cases
Read through the enumerated pairs: man/woman, adult/child, healthy/blind, complete limbs/deficient limbs, sane/mad. Recognize that each pair involves a difference in a personal attribute.
The common theme is that the attribute is irrelevant for qisas.
2
Locate the proof and rationale
Note that the author cites 'general texts' (umumat) as the primary evidence, then provides a secondary rationale: requiring equality in attributes would close the door of qisas, leading to unchecked killing.
The rationale is a secondary support (sadd al-dhara'i').
3
Extract the condition for qisas
From the text and commentary, deduce that the only condition for equality is shared inviolability (ismah), defined by Islam and residence in Dar al-Islam.
This is the Hanafi position; other schools may require additional equality.
4
Apply to a new scenario
Consider whether a healthy person is killed for a blind person. According to this passage, yes, because both are Muslims in Dar al-Islam.
The ruling is consistent across all listed differences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور قتل کیا جائے گا مرد کو عورت کے بدلہ اور بڑے کو چھوٹے کے بدلہ اور تندرست کو اندھے کے بدلے اور اپاہج کے بدلہ اور ناقص الاطراف کے بدلہ اور مجنون کے بدلہ عمومات کی وجہ سے اور اس لئے کہ عصمت کے علاوہ تفاوت کا اعتبار کرنے میں قصاص کا امتناع ہے اور آپس کے مال اور آپس میں ایک دوسرے کو ہلاک کرنے کا ظہور ہے۔
تشریح جب مساوات کا مدار اسلام اور دار الاسلام پر رکھا ہے تو جب یہ مدار پایا جائے وہیں قصاص لیا جائے گا خواہ مرد نے عورت کو قتل کیا ہو یا اس کے برعکس اور خواہ بالغ نے بچہ کو قتل کیا ہے اور خواہ تندرست آدمی نے اندھے اور اپاہج کوقتل کیا ہو۔ اور خواہ سالم الاعضاء نے ناقص الاعضاء کوقتل کیا ہو۔ اور خواہ سالم اور دماغ نے مجنون کو قتل کیا ہو کیونکہ نصوص میں عموم ہے اور اگر عصمت کے علاوہ دیگر چیزوں میں مساوات کا اعتبار کیا جائے تو پھر تو قصاص کا دروازہ ہی بند ہو جائے گا اور جب قصاص نہیں لیا جائے گا تو پھر آپس میں جنگ و جدال اور قتل کا دروازہ کھلے گا اور آپس میں ایک دوسرے کو بلاک کرے گا۔
And a man is killed for a woman, and an adult for a child, and a healthy person for a blind person and a disabled person, and one with complete limbs for one with deficient limbs, and for a mad person, due to general texts (umumat), and because if differences beyond inviolability are considered, qisas would be prevented, and mutual hatred and killing would become apparent. Commentary: When the basis of equality is placed on Islam and Dar al-Islam, then when this basis is found, qisas will be carried out, whether a man killed a woman or vice versa, and whether an adult killed a child, and whether a healthy person killed a blind and disabled person, and whether one with complete limbs killed one with deficient limbs, and whether a sane person killed a mad person, because the texts are general. And if equality is considered in things other than inviolability, then the door of qisas would close, and when qisas is not taken, then the door of war and conflict and killing would open, and they would kill each other.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage enumerates several cases where qisas is applicable despite apparent differences between the killer and the victim. The rule is that as long as both parties share the same foundational inviolability (based on Islam and residence in Dar al-Islam), qisas is wajib. Thus, a man is killed for a woman, an adult for a child, a healthy person for a blind or disabled person, a person with complete limbs for one with deficient limbs, and a sane person for a mad person. The proof is the general texts (umumat) that command qisas without specifying such distinctions. Additionally, if we required equality in every aspect (e.g., physical condition), qisas would almost never be applicable, leading to chaos and unchecked killing. The commentary emphasizes that the only requirement is equality in the basis of inviolability (ismah), not in personal attributes.

Key Terms
عمومات (umumat): General texts from the Quran and Sunnah that command qisas without making exceptions for gender, age, or physical condition.
مساوات (musawat): Equality in the basis of inviolability (Islam/Dar al-Islam), not in personal attributes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is a healthy person killed in qisas for killing a blind person?
A) No, because the blind person is less valuable.
B) Yes, because both share the same basis of inviolability.
C) No, because qisas requires physical equality.
D) Yes, but only if the blind person requested it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires only equality in inviolability (Islam/Dar al-Islam) for qisas, not equality in personal attributes like gender, age, or physical condition.

Father Not Killed for Son in Qisas: The Hanafi Exception
Ruling that a father is not killed in qisas for killing his son, with hadith proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas for a father who kills his son, cite the primary hadith proof, and explain the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam Malik.

Core Idea
A father is never killed in qisas for his child – the hadith 'لا يقاد الوالد بولده' is an absolute bar.

This passage addresses a key exception to the general principle of qisas: when the killer is a father and the victim is his son. The Hanafi school holds that the father is exempt from capital retaliation, basing this on a specific hadith of the Prophet. The text also notes that Imam Malik disagrees, though his full argument is cut off in our source.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its category
Determine what is being ruled upon: the father's liability for killing his son. The ruling is that qisas (capital retaliation) is not applied to the father.
The ruling is an exception to the general qisas verse 'النفس بالنفس'.
2
Locate the hadith proof
The author cites the hadith 'لا يقاد الوالد بولده' (A father is not subjected to qisas for his child). Understand its direct implication for the ruling.
The hadith is the primary proof; its generality is key.
3
Note the ikhtilaf with Imam Malik
The text explicitly says this hadith is a proof against Malik. Recognize that Imam Malik held that a father can be killed in qisas in some circumstances (e.g., intentional killing).
The passage cuts off, but the Maliki view is that the hadith applies only to accidental killings.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafi school says father pays diyah only; Maliki school allows qisas in some cases. This difference stems from how each school interprets the hadith's scope.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi (relied upon) in the school.

Source Text

ولا يقتل الرجل بابنه لقوله عليه السلام لا يقاد الوالد بولده وهو با طلاقه حجة على ما لك في قوله يقاد اذا
ترجمہ اور قتل نہیں کیا جائے گا مرد کو اس کے بیٹے کے بدلہ اس لئے کہ حضور علیہ السلام کا فرمان ہے کہ والڈ کو اس کے بچہ کے بدلہ قصاص نہیں کیا جائے گا اور یہ حدیث صراحت کے ساتھ اس بات پر دلیل ہے کہ مالک کے قول کے خلاف جو فرماتے ہیں کہ قصاص کیا جائے گا جب...

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling that a father is not killed in qisas for killing his son. The proof is the hadith of the Prophet: 'La yuqadu al-walid bi waladihi' (A father is not subjected to qisas for his child). The text also notes that this hadith is an explicit argument against Imam Malik, who holds that qisas is applicable in some cases (the text cuts off, but the Maliki position is that a father can be killed for his son under certain conditions). The Hanafi school relies on the general implication of the hadith that the father's authority and compassion prevent qisas; instead, diyah is wajib.

Key Terms
والد (walid): Father (parent). The hadith uses this term to include the father.
قود (qawad): Qisas; retaliation by taking life.
ولد (walad): Child; offspring. In the hadith, it means the son (or child).
دية (diyah): Blood money; financial compensation paid to the heirs of the victim in lieu of qisas.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a father is never killed in qisas for killing his child, based on the explicit hadith of the Prophet.

Qisas — Retaliation

8 min
Qisas and Istihsan: The Musta'min Case
States rulings on qisas when a musta'min is killed by a dhimmi or another musta'min

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school overrides qiyas with istihsan when a musta'min kills another musta'min, and state the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Istihsan overrides qiyas when a mubeeh exists — the musta'min's blood is not permanently inviolable.

In this passage from al-Hidayah, the author presents two competing legal arguments regarding qisas when a musta'min kills another musta'min. By analogy (qiyas), equality of protection would demand qisas. But the Hanafi school prefers istihsan, because the musta'min's temporary status introduces a mubeeh (permissibility to kill) that breaks the analogy. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and shows how istihsan operates in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The passage addresses two scenarios: dhimmi killing musta'min, and musta'min killing musta'min. The first is settled (no qisas); the second is the focus.
The first ruling is based on the principle already established that the dhimmi's blood is more protected than the musta'min's.
2
Understand the qiyas argument
The qiyas is based on equality (musawah) between killer and victim. Since both are musta'mins, they have the same temporary protection, so qisas would apply by analogy to the rule for two Muslims.
Equality is a strong analogical ground in Hanafi fiqh, but it can be overridden.
3
Recognize the istihsan override
The Hanafi school introduces istihsan because there is a mubeeh — a legal ground that permits killing the musta'min (e.g., he may be returning to dar al-harb). This mubeeh undermines the equality premise.
Istihsan is not a weaker method; it is a preferred approach when a stronger cause exists.
4
State the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that qisas is not applied; the killer is punished for violating the aman but not executed for qisas.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position from the core Hanafi texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يقتل الذمي بالمستأمن لما بينا ويقتل المستأمن بالمستأمن قياسا للمساواة ولا يقتل استحسانا لقيام المبيح
And the dhimmi is not killed for the musta'min for what we have stated. And the musta'min is killed for the musta'min by analogy due to equality, and he is not killed by istihsan due to the existence of the permissibility.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on qisas when a musta'min (a non-Muslim given temporary protection) is killed. The author first states that a dhimmi (permanent non-Muslim resident) is not executed for killing a musta'min because the musta'min's blood is not permanently protected (as explained earlier). Then, regarding a musta'min killing another musta'min, two opinions are presented: by qiyas (analogy based on equality between the two) qisas would apply, but by istihsan (juristic preference) it is not applied because there is a mubeeh (a legal permission to kill) – presumably because the musta'min is from dar al-harb and his blood is not inviolable, especially if he intends to return. The relied-upon Hanafi position is the istihsan ruling, which overrides qiyas. This shows the priority of istihsan over qiyas when a stronger cause exists.

Key Terms
مستأمن (musta'min): A non-Muslim who enters dār al-Islam with a temporary guarantee of safety (amān)
ذمي (dhimmī): A non-Muslim permanently residing in dār al-Islam under the pact of dhimmah
استحسان (istihsān): Juristic preference that abandons qiyās in favor of a stronger evidence or cause

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafī school not apply qiṣāṣ when a musta'min kills another musta'min, even though they are equal?
A) Because the musta'min's blood is not permanently protected due to a mubeeḥ.
B) Because they are not Muslims.
C) Because the dhimmī has more rights.
D) Because the musta'min is considered a combatant.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafī fiqh, istihsān overrides qiyās when a mubeeḥ exists, so a musta'min is not subjected to qiṣāṣ for killing another musta'min.

Qisas — Retaliation

Qisas Between Genders, Ages, and Physical Conditions
Establishes qisas between different categories of Muslims based on equal inviolability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that qisas applies equally regardless of gender, age, or physical condition and explain the two proofs (general texts and rational argument) that support this position.

Core Idea
Equal inviolability of all Muslims is the sole criterion for qisas; disparities in other attributes do not prevent retaliation.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes a fundamental principle of Hanafi qisas law: a Muslim may be executed in retaliation for killing any other Muslim, regardless of differences in gender, age, or physical condition. The author presents two arguments—one from general Quranic and hadith proofs, and a rational consideration that any other rule would undermine the deterrent purpose of qisas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling: list the pairs mentioned
Read the passage and note the specific pairs where qisas applies: man for woman, adult for child, healthy for blind/chronically ill, complete limbs for deficient limbs, sane for insane.
2
Locate the first proof: the general texts (al-umumat)
These are Quranic verses like 'And in retaliation there is life' (2:179) and 'The life for the life' (5:45) which are general and not restricted by gender, age, or condition. The Hanafi school takes these texts literally (zahir).
3
Locate the second proof: the rational argument
The passage states that if we considered disparities in matters other than inviolability (isma), qisas would often be impossible, leading to increased violence and mutual destruction (takatul wa tafani).
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Some schools, like the Shafi'i, do not allow a man to be killed for a woman in qisas because they consider a woman's life less valuable. The Hanafi school responds that the general texts and rational argument support equality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقتل الرجل بالمرأة والكبير بالصغير والصحيح بالأعمى والزمن وبناقص الأطراف وبالمجنون للعمومات ولأن في اعتبار التفاوت فيما وراء العصمة امتناع القصاص وظهور التقاتل والتفاني
And the man is killed for the woman, and the adult for the child, and the healthy for the blind and the chronically ill, and the one with complete limbs for the one with deficient limbs, and for the insane, due to the general proofs, and because considering disparity in matters beyond inviolability would prevent qisas and would give rise to mutual fighting and destruction.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is a ruling stating that qisas applies universally among Muslims regardless of physical or social differences. The author lists specific pairs: a man can be executed for killing a woman, an adult for a child, a healthy person for a blind or chronically ill person, a person with complete limbs for one with deficient limbs, and a sane person for an insane person. The evidence is 'the general proofs' (العمومات) from the Quran and Sunnah that command qisas without specifying equality in these attributes. The second reason is a rational argument: if we consider disparities in matters other than inviolability (which is equal for all Muslims), it would effectively prevent qisas in many cases, leading to increased violence and murder (التقاتل والتفاني). The Hanafi school thus holds that the only basis for qisas is equal inviolability (عصمة) and residence in dar al-Islam.

Key Terms
عصمة (isma): Inviolability or protection of life; the quality that makes a person's life sacred and protected by law
عمومات (umumat): General proofs from Quran and Sunnah that are universal in scope

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why would considering disparity in matters beyond inviolability prevent qisas?
A) Because it would lead to many exceptions.
B) Because it would make qisas impossible in many cases and increase violence.
C) Because the Quran prohibits discrimination.
D) Because it contradicts the Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, qisas is universal among Muslims because all share equal inviolability (isma), regardless of gender, age, or physical condition, as established by general scriptural proofs and a rational argument against unnecessary exceptions.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
8 min
Father Not Killed for Son: The Qisas Exception
Ruling with proof on the qisas exception for parents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a father is not executed for his son, cite the prophetic hadith as proof, explain the rationale of causation, and apply the rule to all ascendants.

Core Idea
A father is not killed for his son because he is the cause of the son's life — the hadith is general.

Qisas (retributive justice) is the default for intentional homicide, but the Hanafi school recognizes a permanent exception: a parent is never executed for killing their child. This exception is rooted in a specific prophetic hadith and supported by a powerful rationale: the father is the efficient cause of the child's existence. In this lesson, we explore the primary proof, its logical underpinning, and how it extends to all ascendants. We also examine the brief but significant dispute with Imam Malik over the method of killing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its scope
The passage states clearly that a man is not killed for his son. Understand that this is an exception to the general law of qisas. The rule covers all types of killing, not just specific methods.
The rule also applies to all ascendants: grandfathers, grandmothers, etc.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The proof is the prophetic hadith: 'لا يقاد الوالد بولده' (A parent is not subjected to retaliation for his child). Note that the Hanafi school takes this hadith in its absolute generality (itlaq).
The hadith is general in wording, covering both father and mother.
3
Understand the rationale (illah)
The text provides a rational argument: the father is the cause (sabab) of the son's life. It would be legally absurd for the son to bring about the father's annihilation (ifna'). This rationale reinforces the hadith and clarifies why the exception is permanent.
This rationale is used to extend the rule to all ascendants, as they are also causes of life.
4
Apply the extension to ascendants
The text explicitly states that grandfathers (from both sides), mothers, and grandmothers are treated like the father. Why? Because they too are causes of the descendant's life through lineage.
The rule applies regardless of how far the relationship is ('even if they ascend').
5
Contrast with the opposite case and the Maliki dispute
The opposite case (son killing father) is not exempted: a son is executed because no such preventing factor exists. Also, note the dispute with Imam Malik: he allows qisas when the father slaughters (dhabh) the child. The Hanafi response is that the hadith is general and the rationale applies to all killings equally.
This difference is a practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of interpreting the hadith as general versus restricted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يقتل الرجل بابنه لقوله عليه السلام لا يقاد الوالد بولده وهو باطلاقه حجة على مالك في قوله يقاد اذا ذبحا و لا نه سبب لحيائه فمن المحال ان يستحق له افناؤه ولهذا لا يجوز له قتله وان وجده في صف الاعداء مقاتلا او زانيا وهو محصن والقصاص يستحقه المقتول ثم يخلفه وارثه والجد من قبل الرجال او النساء وان على هذا بمنزلة الأب وكذا الوالدة والجدة من قبل الاب او الام قربت ام بعدت لما بينا ويقتل الولد لعدم المسقط
And the man is not killed for his son due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'A parent is not subjected to retaliation for his child.' And this, by its generality, is a proof against Malik in his statement that he is subjected to retaliation if he slaughters him. And because he (the father) is the cause of his (the son's) life, so it is impossible that he (the son) deserves his (the father's) annihilation. For this reason, it is not permissible for him (the son) to kill him (the father) even if he finds him fighting in the enemy ranks or committing adultery while he is muhsan. And qisas is deserved by the killed person, then his heir inherits it. And the grandfather, from the side of men or women, even if they ascend, is in the position of the father in this regard. Likewise, the mother and the grandmother, from the father's side or mother's side, whether near or far, for what we have stated. And the child is killed (for the father) due to the absence of any preventing factor.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the exception to qisas: a father is not executed for killing his child. The primary proof is the hadith 'لا يقاد الوالد بولده' (a parent is not subject to retaliation for his child). The author notes that this hadith is general and therefore refutes Imam Malik's view that qisas applies if the father slaughters the child (as opposed to other methods of killing). The underlying rationale (علة) is that the father is the cause of the son's existence (سبب لحيائه); it would be absurd for the son to cause the father's annihilation. This rationale extends to all ascendants: grandfathers, great-grandfathers, etc., regardless of whether they are from the father's or mother's side, and also grandmothers and great-grandmothers. The passage confirms that such relatives are in the same position as the father. However, the opposite is not true: a son can be killed for killing his father because there is no such preventing factor (عدم المسقط). The passage also mentions that a son is not permitted to kill his father even if he finds him fighting as an enemy or committing adultery while muhsan, emphasizing the sanctity of the father's life.

Key Terms
لا يقاد الوالد بولده (la yuqad al-walid bi waladih): The prophetic statement that a parent is not subject to qisas for killing his child
سبب لحيائه (sabab li hayatih): The father is the efficient cause of the child's life through procreation
مسقط (musqit): A factor that prevents or removes the obligation of qisas

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary rationale for the rule that a father is not killed for his son?
A) The father's testimony is not accepted.
B) The father is the cause of the son's life, so it is impossible for the son to deserve the father's annihilation.
C) The Quran specifically exempts fathers.
D) The father is always forgiven by the son's heirs.

Key Takeaway
A father (and all ascendants) is never executed for killing his child, based on the prophetic hadith and the rationale that the parent is the cause of the child's life.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
6 min
Father Not Executed for Killing His Son
Defining the Hanafi ruling that a father is not subject to qisas for killing his son

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a father is not executed for killing his son, explain the proof from the hadith, and contrast the Maliki position.

Core Idea
A father is never executed for killing his son, regardless of method, due to the hadith and the father's role as cause of life.

In Hanafi criminal law, retaliation (qisas) is the default punishment for intentional homicide. However, a unique exception exists when the killer is the father and the victim is his son. This lesson examines the ruling, its proof from the Sunnah, and the underlying principle that prevents the son or his heirs from demanding the father's execution.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from al-Quduri: a man is not killed for his son. This is the base ruling.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith: 'La yuqad al-walid bi waladihi' (A father is not killed for his son). This is a primary proof.
The hadith is narrated by Tirmidhi and others; it is ahad but accepted in practice.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The negation 'la yuqad' indicates that qisas is not established against the father. The hadith is general and applies to any method of killing.
4
Note the ikhtilaf with Imam Malik
Imam Malik holds that if a father slaughters his son, qisas is applicable. The Hanafi response is that the hadith is general and overrides this analogy.
The Maliki view is based on qiyas and a different interpretation.
5
Analyze the Hanafi reasoning
The father is the cause of the son's life (sabab al-hayah). Therefore, it is legally inconceivable that the son should have a right to annihilate his own cause. This principle also explains why the son cannot kill his father even in extreme situations.
The reasoning is based on aql and maslaha.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا يقتل الرجل بولده لقول عليه السلام لا يقتل الوالد بولده. وهو حجة على مالك في إطلاقه لقوله: يقتل إذا ذبحه. ولأن الأب سبب حياة الابن فلا يستحق إفناءه فلا يجوز قتله. ولو وجده في صف الأعداء مقاتلاً أو زانياً وهو محصن. والقصاص يستحقه المقتول ثم يخلفه وارثه. والجد من قبل الرجال أو النساء وإن علا بمنزلة الأب وكذا الوالدة والجدة من قبل الأب أو الأم قربت أم بعدت. ويقتل الولد بعدم المسقط.
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور مرد اپنے بیٹے کے بدلہ قتل نہیں کیا جائے گا نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان، لا یقاد الوالد بولدہ کی وجہ سے اور یہ حدیث اپنے اطلاق کی وجہ سے مالک پر حجت ہے ان کے یہ فرمانے میں کہ قصاص لیا جائے گا جب کہ باپ نے اسے ذبح کر دے اور اس لئے کہ باپ بیٹے کے احیاء کا سبب ہے تو محال ہے یہ بات کہ بیٹے کے لئے باپ کے افتاء کا استحقاق ہو۔ اور اسی وجہ سے بیٹے کے لئے باپ کو قتل کرنا جائز نہیں ہے اگر چہ باپ کو دشمنوں کی صف میں قتال کرنے والا پائے یا زنا کرتے پائے حالانکہ باپ محصن ہو اور قصاص کا مستحق مقتول ہوتا ہے پھر مقتول کا فریضہ اس کا وارث ہوتا ہے اور جد مردوں اور عورتوں کی جانب سے اگر چہ اور اوپر ہو اس باب میں باپ کے درجہ میں ہے اور ایسے ہی والدہ اور جدہ باپ کی جانب سے ہوں یا ماں کے قریب ہو یا بعید اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور باپ کے بدلہ بیٹے کو قتل کیا جائے گا مسقط ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح اگر باپ نے لڑکے کو قتل کر دیا تو قصاص نہیں لیا جائے گا کیونکہ ترمندی میں حدیث ہے کہ باپ سے اپنے بچے کے بدلہ قصاص نہیں لیا جائے گا۔ لہذا ذبح کرے یا اور طریقہ سے قتل کرے سب اس میں داخل ہیں لہذا یہ حدیث اپنے عموم کی وجہ سے امام مالک کے خلاف حجت ہے انہوں نے کہا ہے کہ قصاص نہیں لیا جائے گا لیکن اگر باپ نے بچہ کوذبح کیا ہو تو قصاص لیا جائے گا۔ اور دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ بیٹے کی زندگی کا سبب باپ ہے تو بیٹے کو یہ استحقاق نہیں ہو سکتا کہ باپ کو ختم کر دے یہی تو وجہ ہے کہ اگر باپ گفار کی فوج میں جنگ کے لئے آیا ہوا ہے اور قتال کر رہا ہے تب بھی شریعت نے بیٹے کو یہ حق نہیں دیا کہ باپ کو قتل کرے جس کی تفصیل" کتاب السیر میں مذکور ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر باپ نے محصن ہونے کے باوجود زنا کیا اور بیٹے نے دیکھا تو بیٹے کو جائز نہیں کہ باپ کو قتل کرے۔
سوال قصاص تو بیٹے کے ورثہ کا حق ہوگا بیٹے کوتو یہ حق نہیں تھا کہ باپ کو قتل کرے مگر یہاں تو ورثہ سحق بنے ہیں؟ جواب اولا استحقاق قصاص مقتول کے لئے ہوتا ہے پھر اس کی نیابت وخلافت میں یہ حق اس کے ورثہ کو مانتا ہے اور یہاں جب اصل ہی کو حق نہیں ملا تو اس کے خلیفہ کو کیسے مل جائے گا۔ دادا، پردادا ، سکٹر دادا، نانا، پڑنا نا، سکڑ نا نا وغیرہ باپ کے حکم میں ہیں اور ماں اور دادی ، پردادی اور نانی پرنانی وغیرہ بھی باپ کے درجہ میں ہیں، اور دلیل وہی ہے جو مذکور ہے، البتہ اگر لڑکے نے باپ کو قتل کر دیا تو یہاں کوئی مسقط نہیں اس لئے بیٹے کو قصاص میں قتل کیا جائے گا۔
He said: A man is not killed for his son, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'A father is not killed for his son.' And it is a proof against Malik in its generality, because of his saying: he is killed if he slaughters him. And because the father is the cause of the son's life, so the son cannot deserve his annihilation; therefore it is not permissible for him to kill him, even if he finds him in the enemy's ranks fighting, or fornicating while he is muhsan. And qisas is deserved by the killed person, then his heir succeeds him. And the grandfather from the father's side or the mother's side, however high, is in the position of the father. Similarly the mother and the grandmother from the father's side or the mother's side, whether near or far. And the son is killed (for the father) because there is no disqualifier.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding qisas (retaliation) when a father kills his son. The base text from al-Quduri states that a man is not executed for killing his son. The proof is the hadith: 'A father is not killed for his son.' This hadith is general and applies whether the father slaughters the son or kills him in any other way. It is a proof against Imam Malik, who held that qisas is applicable if the father slaughters the son. The Hanafi reasoning is that the father is the cause (sabab) of the son's life, so it is inconceivable that the son should have a right to annihilate his father. Therefore, even if the son finds the father fighting among the enemy or committing zina while muhsan, the son cannot kill him. The right to qisas belongs to the victim, then passes to his heirs. Since the victim (the son) never had the right against his own father, the heirs (who would inherit that right) also do not acquire it. Grandfathers from both paternal and maternal lines are treated like the father, as are mothers and grandmothers. However, if a son kills his father, there is no disqualifier, so the son is executed in qisas.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment for homicide or bodily injury, specifically execution for murder.
محصن (muhsan): A person who has previously experienced valid sexual intercourse in a valid marriage, making zina punishable by stoning.
وترث (yarith): He inherits; here referring to the heir who inherits the right to demand qisas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Hanafi law not allow a son to kill his father even if the father is fighting the Muslims?
A) Because the father is more important than the son
B) Because the father is the cause of the son's life, so the son cannot deserve to annihilate him
C) Because the father has immunity as a parent
D) Because the son cannot inherit qisas

Key Takeaway
A father is never executed for killing his son in Hanafi law, based on the hadith and the principle that the father is the cause of the son's existence.

Qisas — Retaliation
beginner
6 min
Master Not Executed for Killing His Slave
Stating the ruling that a master is not executed for killing his own slave, mudabbar, or mukatab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the specific situations in which qisas is not applied in master-slave relationships and explain the underlying legal principles such as indivisibility of qisas and sanctity of fatherhood.

Core Idea
A master cannot be executed for killing his own slave because the right of qisas cannot be against oneself.

This lesson presents a series of clear rulings from al-Quduri on exceptions to qisas in cases involving slaves and family relations. Understanding these exceptions is crucial for correctly applying Islamic criminal law, as they highlight fundamental principles: ownership cancels qisas, qisas is indivisible, and fatherhood commands respect.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Recall that qisas (retributive execution) is normally applied for intentional killing of a free person. Here, the text lists exceptions.
The exceptions are based on the relationship between killer and victim.
2
List the exceptions involving ownership
Identify the four cases: (1) master kills his own slave, (2) master kills his mudabbar, (3) master kills his mukatab, (4) master kills the slave of his child.
In each case, the killer is the owner or the owner's relation.
3
Explain the rationale for ownership exceptions
The reason given is that the killer cannot claim qisas against himself (for his own slave) nor can his child claim against him (for child's slave).
The right to qisas would effectively be against oneself.
4
Analyze the jointly owned slave case
If a co-owner kills a jointly owned slave, qisas is not applied because qisas is indivisible (la yatajazzā). The right to qisas cannot be split among co-owners.
This applies even if the other co-owner wants qisas.
5
Understand the fatherhood sanctity exception
If a son inherits a right to qisas against his father (e.g., father killed mother), that right drops due to the sanctity/honour of fatherhood (hurmat al-ubuwwah).
This protects the father from execution by his child.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا يقتل الرجل بعبده ولا مدبره ولا مكاتبه ولا بعبد ولده لا نه لا يستوجب لنفسه على نفسه القصاص ولا ولده عليه و كذالا يقتل بعبد ملك بعضه لان القصاص لا يتجزى قال ومن ورث قصاصاً على ابيه سقط لحرمة الابوة .
ترجمه قدوری نے فرمایا اور قتل نہیں کیا جائے گا مرد اپنے غلام کے بدلہ اور نہ اپنے مدبر کے بدلہ اور نہ اپنے مکاتب کے بدلہ اور نہ اپنے بچے کے غلام کے بدلہ اس لئے کہ آقا استحقاق نہیں رکھتا اپنے ہی لئے اپنے اوپر قصاص کا اور نہ اس پر اس کا بچہ اور نہ ہی قتل کیا جائے گا ایسے غلام کے بدلہ میں جس کے بعض کا وہ مالک ہو گیا ہو اس لئے کہ قصاص غیر متجری ہے۔ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جو وارث ہوا قصاص کا اپنے باپ پر قصاص ساقط ہو جائے گا ابوت کے احترام کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح اگر مولی نے اپنا غلام قتل کر دیا ہوتو قصاص نہیں لیا جائے گا اور مدبر اور مکاتب کا بھی یہی حکم ہے کیونکہ قصاص کا وارث بھی مولیٰ ہے اور لیا بھی جا رہا ہے مولیٰ سے اور یہ باطل ہے۔ اور اگر اپنے لڑکے کا غلام قتل کیا ہو تو بھی قصاص نہ ہوگا کیونکہ بیٹا بھی باپ پر قصاص کا مستحق نہیں ہو سکتا۔ ایک مشترک غلام ہے جس کو ایک شریک نے قتل کر دیا تو اس سے قصاص نہیں لیا جائیگا کیونکہ قصاص غیر متجری ہے۔ اور اگر لڑکے کو حق قصاص میراث میں ملا ہو تب بھی قصاص نہ ہوگا کیونکہ ابوت کا احترام اس کو مانع ہے مثلا لڑکے کی ماں کو قتل کر دیا اور بیٹا اس کا وارث ہے قصاص ساقط ہو جائے گا۔
He said: A man is not killed for his slave, nor his mudabbar, nor his mukatab, nor for the slave of his child, because he does not deserve qisas against himself, nor does his child deserve it against him. Similarly, he is not killed for a slave of which he owns a part, because qisas is indivisible. He said: And whoever inherits qisas against his father, it falls due to the sanctity of fatherhood.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings from al-Quduri regarding situations where qisas is not applicable. The key principle is that a person cannot be executed for killing his own property. Thus, a master is not executed for killing his own slave, mudabbar (a slave promised freedom upon the master's death), or mukatab (a slave under a contract of manumission). Similarly, if a person kills a slave owned by his child, he is not executed because the child also cannot claim qisas against his father (as per the previous ruling). If a slave is jointly owned and one co-owner kills him, qisas is not applied because qisas is indivisible and cannot be split among co-owners. Finally, if a son inherits a right to qisas against his father (e.g., the father killed someone whose right to qisas passed to the son), that right is dropped due to the respect owed to fatherhood. The commentary explains that in all these cases, the right of qisas would effectively be against oneself or against a father, which is not permissible.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the master's death, by the master's declaration (tadbir).
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract of manumission (kitabah) with the master, agreeing to pay a sum for freedom.
لا يتجزى (la yatajazzā): Indivisible; meaning qisas cannot be split into parts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is qisas not applied when a co-owner kills a jointly owned slave?
A) Because co-owners have no right to qisas
B) Because qisas is indivisible
C) Because the slave is not fully owned by the killer
D) Because the other co-owner may forgive

Key Takeaway
A master is never executed for killing his own slave because the right to qisas would be against oneself; similarly, qisas is dropped in cases of partial ownership, family relations, and fatherhood sanctity.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate

Method of Qisas Execution: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Resolving the disagreement between Hanafi and Shafi'i on the method of execution in qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on qisas execution, cite its proof, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and identify the practical difference between the two rulings.

Core Idea
Qisas is carried out only by a sword (weapon) – the method is fixed, not matched to the crime.

How should a murderer be executed in Islamic law? Should the method mirror the killing, or should it be a standard humane method? This passage from al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi view that qisas is restricted to the sword (or any weapon causing quick death), in contrast to Imam al-Shafi'i who insists on exact resemblance. Understanding this ikhtilaf reveals how different schools balance the principles of equality, textual proof, and practical mercy.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: qisas is executed only with a sword (or weapon). Note that the Hanafi school sets a single method regardless of how the victim was killed.
The text says 'لا يستو في القصاص الا بالسيف' – qisas is not carried out except with a sword.
2
Identify the Shafi'i opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the execution method must exactly match the killer's method, provided it is a permissible (shar'i) act. If the victim was drowned, the killer should be drowned; if killed by stoning, the killer should be stoned.
This is based on the Quranic principle of equality in retaliation (المساواة).
3
Examine the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i argument rests on the principle of musawah (equality), derived from the Quranic verse 'And if you punish, then punish with the like of that with which you were afflicted' (16:126) and the general spirit of qisas.
The passage quotes the Shafi'i reasoning: 'مبنى القصاص على المساواة' – qisas is built on equality.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response has two parts. First, a specific hadith explicitly limits qisas to the sword: 'لا قودا لا بالسيف' (No qisas except with a sword). Second, imitating the exact method can lead to either excess (if the method was torturous) or failure to achieve the objective (if the method was non-lethal), in which case decapitation would still be needed, making exact imitation redundant.
The hadith is given priority over general analogy. The Hanafis consider any weapon that causes quick death as equivalent to a sword.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Under Hanafi law, all homicide executed by qisas are carried out by a swift weapon (sword, gun, etc.) regardless of the killing method. Under Shafi'i law, if the killer used a permissible method (e.g., drowning), the execution uses that same method; if the method was impermissible (e.g., burning), then a different method is used.
The Hanafi approach ensures a single uniform method, avoiding the need to judge the permissibility of the killing method.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا يستو في القصاص الا بالسيف وقال الشافعي يفعل به مثل ما فعل ان كان فعلا مشروعا فان مات فيها والا تحرر قبته لأن مبنى القصاص على المساواة ولنا قوله عليه السلام لا قودا لا بالسيف والمرادبه السلاح ولان فيما ذهب اليه استيفاء الزيادة أو لم يحصل المقصود بمثل ما فعلى فيحز فيجب التحر زعنه كما في كسر العظم
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا قصاص نہیں لیا جائے گا مگر تلوار سے اور فر مایا نشانی نے کہ قاتل کے ساتھ اسی طرح برتاؤ کیا جائے گا جو کہ قاتل نے کیا ہے بشرطیکہ فعل مشروع ہو پس اگر قاتل اس سے مر گیا تو فبہا اور نہ اس کی گردن کاٹ دی جائے اس لئے کہ قصاص کی بنیاد امساوات پر ہے اور ہماری دلیل فرمان نبی علیہ السلام ہے قصاص نہیں ہے مگر تلوار سے ہتھیار مراد ہے اور اس لئے کہ اس طریقہ میں جس کی جانب شافعی گئے زیادہ وصول کرنا ہے اگر قاتل کے فعل کے مثل سے مقصود حاصل نہ ہو تو پھر گردن کائی جائے گی تو اس سے بچنا واجب ہوگا جیسے ہڈی توڑنے میں۔
تشریح حنفیہ کے نزدیک صرف ہتھیار سے قصاص لیا جائے خواہ تلوار ہو یا بندوق، امام شافعی کے نزدیک یہ ہے کہ جو فعل قاتل نے کیا ہے اگر وہ مشروع فعل ہو تو قاتل کے ساتھ بھی ایسے ہی کیا جائے پھر اگر وہ اس سے مر جائے تو ٹھیک ورنہ اس کے بعد اس کی گردن کاٹ
He said: Qisas is not carried out except with a sword. And al-Shafi'i said: He should be treated exactly as he did, if that act was lawful (shar'i). Then if he dies from it, fine; otherwise, his neck is struck, because qisas is based on equality. Our proof is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'No qisas except with a sword' — the meaning is weapon. And because in what he (al-Shafi'i) went to, there is attainment of excess, or the objective is not achieved by doing exactly what he did, so [in that case] his neck must be struck, so it is necessary to avoid that, just as in breaking a bone.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the method of executing qisas. The Hanafi school, based on the hadith 'No qisas except with a sword', restricts execution to a sword (or any weapon that kills swiftly). Imam al-Shafi'i, however, argues that the method of execution should match the method of killing, as long as it is a shar'i act (i.e., not haram like burning). The Shafi'i basis is the principle of equality (musawah) in qisas. The Hanafi response is twofold: first, the hadith explicitly limits qisas to the sword (weapon). Second, imitating the killer's exact method may either involve excess (if the method was torturous) or fail to achieve the goal (if the victim died by a non-lethal method), in which case decapitation is needed anyway. To avoid either problem, they restrict to sword. The commentary notes that Hanafis allow any weapon (sword, gun, etc.) as long as it causes a quick death. In case of breaking a bone, qisas is not applied because of the danger of excess, as per the matn earlier.

Key Terms
قود (qawad): Another word for qisas, specifically execution in homicide cases.
فعل مشروع (fi'l mashru'): An act that is legally valid and not prohibited, e.g., killing by sword is mashru', but killing by poison or burning is not.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi proof for restricting qisas to the sword?
A) The Qur'anic verse of equality
B) The hadith 'No qisas except with a sword'
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) Qiyas on breaking bones

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school restricts qisas execution to the sword based on the explicit hadith 'La qawada illa bis-sayf', prioritizing textual specificity over the general principle of equality.

Qisas — Retaliation
