Qisas Exemptions: Master's, Father's, and Joint Ownership Cases
Multiple rulings on qisas exemptions with reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five cases where qisas is not applied according to the Hanafi school and explain the legal reasoning (sabab) for each exemption.

Core Idea
Qisas drops when the killer and the heir are the same, or when the killer is the father, or when qisas cannot be divided.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents several rulings where the law of qisas does not apply, despite an intentional killing. These exceptions are rooted in two core principles: legal incapacity (the killer cannot owe qisas to himself) and the sanctity of fatherhood (hurmat al-abuwah). Let us examine each case and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the killer and victim in each ruling.
The passage lists five scenarios: master kills own slave (including mudabbar, mukatab), father kills child's slave, co-owner kills jointly owned slave, and son inherits qisas against father. Name the relationship in each.
2
Determine the reason for qisas exemption.
For each scenario, the passage gives a legal cause. For master killing own slave: the master is the heir, so qisas would be taken from himself. For father: the sanctity of fatherhood. For joint slave: qisas cannot be divided. For inherited qisas: same sanctity.
3
Apply the principle to analogous cases.
Think about whether these rules extend to other relationships, e.g., mother killing child, or owner killing a partially owned animal (for injury, not homicide). The Hanafi position is specific to these cases.
The principle of indivisibility of qisas is key.
4
Contrast with the general rule of qisas.
Remember that qisas is normally required for intentional killing. These are exceptions. Understand that the burden shifts to diyah (blood money) in these cases.

قال ولا يقتل الرجل بعبده ولا مدبره ولا مكاتبه ولا بعبد ولده لأنه لا يستوجب لنفسه على نفسه القصاص ولا ولده عليه وكذا لا يقتل بعبد ملك بعضه لأن القصاص لا يتجزأ قال ومن ورث قصاصاً على أبيه سقط لحرمة الأبوة. ترجمه: قدوری نے فرمایا اور قتل نہیں کیا جائے گا مرد اپنے غلام کے بدلہ اور نہ اپنے مدبر کے بدلہ اور نہ اپنے مکاتب کے بدلہ اور نہ اپنے بچے کے غلام کے بدلہ اس لئے کہ آقا استحقاق نہیں رکھتا اپنے ہی لئے اپنے اوپر قصاص کا اور نہ اس پر اس کا بچہ اور نہ ہی قتل کیا جائے گا ایسے غلام کے بدلہ میں جس کے بعض کا وہ مالک ہو گیا ہو اس لئے کہ قصاص غیر متجری ہے۔ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جو وارث ہوا قصاص کا اپنے باپ پر قصاص ساقط ہو جائے گا ابوت کے احترام کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح: اگر مولی نے اپنا غلام قتل کر دیا ہو تو قصاص نہیں لیا جائے گا اور مدبر اور مکاتب کا بھی یہی حکم ہے کیونکہ قصاص کا وارث بھی مولیٰ ہے اور لیا بھی جا رہا ہے مولیٰ سے اور یہ باطل ہے۔ اور اگر اپنے لڑکے کا غلام قتل کیا ہو تو بھی قصاص نہ ہوگا کیونکہ بیٹا بھی باپ پر قصاص کا مستحق نہیں ہو سکتا۔ ایک مشترک غلام ہے جس کو ایک شریک نے قتل کر دیا تو اس سے قصاص نہیں لیا جائیگا کیونکہ قصاص غیر متجری ہے۔ اور اگر لڑکے کو حق قصاص میراث میں ملا ہو تب بھی قصاص نہ ہوگا کیونکہ ابوت کا احترام اس کو مانع ہے مثلا لڑکے کی ماں کو قتل کر دیا اور بیٹا اس کا وارث ہے قصاص ساقط ہو جائے گا۔
He said: A man is not killed for his slave, nor his mudabbar, nor his mukatab, nor for his child's slave, because he does not deserve qisas against himself, nor does his child have qisas against him. Similarly, he is not killed for a slave of which he owns a part, because qisas is not divisible. He said: And whoever inherits qisas against his father, the qisas drops due to the sanctity of fatherhood. Translation: Quduri said: And a man will not be killed for his slave, nor for his mudabbar, nor for his mukatab, nor for his child's slave, because the master does not have the right to qisas against himself, nor does his child have it against him. And he will not be killed for a slave of which he owns a part, because qisas is indivisible. Quduri said: And whoever inherits qisas against his father, the qisas drops due to the sanctity of fatherhood. Commentary: If the master killed his own slave, qisas will not be taken, and the same ruling applies to the mudabbar and mukatab, because the master is the heir of qisas and it would be taken from him, which is invalid. If a man killed his child's slave, qisas will not be taken because the child cannot be entitled to qisas against his father. If a jointly-owned slave is killed by one of the co-owners, qisas is not taken from him because qisas is indivisible. If a son inherits a right to qisas against his father, qisas drops due to the sanctity of fatherhood; e.g., the son's mother is killed and the son is her heir, qisas is dropped.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage states multiple rulings from the Hanafi school regarding when qisas (retaliation) is not applied. First, a master who kills his own slave, mudabbar (slave whose manumission is deferred after master's death), or mukatab (slave who has contracted to buy his freedom) is not subject to qisas. The reason is that the master himself is the heir of the slave, so the demand for qisas would effectively be from the master against himself, which is legally impossible. Similarly, if a man kills his child's slave, the father is not executed because the child cannot claim qisas against his own father. Third, if a person kills a slave in which he holds a partial share (joint ownership), qisas is not applied because qisas cannot be divided into fractions. Finally, if a person inherits a right to qisas against his own father, that right is nullified due to the sanctity of fatherhood; for example, if a son's mother is killed and the son inherits the right to qisas against his father (the killer), the qisas is dropped. These rulings are based on the principles of legal capacity and the indivisibility of qisas.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for homicide or injury; the legal right to execute the killer.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose manumission is deferred until after the master's death.
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract (kitabah) with his master to purchase his freedom by paying installments.
حرمة الأبوة (hurmat al-abuwah): The inviolable sanctity of fatherhood that prevents qisas being applied against a father for killing his descendant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a man kills his own mudabbar (slave with deferred manumission) intentionally, what is the ruling regarding qisas?
A) He is executed because the killing is intentional.
B) He is not executed because the mudabbar is still property and he is the heir.
C) He must pay diyah but not qisas only if the slave had no free heirs.
D) He is exempted only if he did not use a weapon.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, qisas is not applied when the killer is the victim's sole heir, or the father, or when qisas would be indivisible.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
8 min
Hanafi vs. Shafi'i: How to Execute Qisas
Presents the dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is on how qisas is executed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the method of qisas execution, explain the Hanafi proof (hadith and rational argument), and evaluate the dispute's practical consequence.

Core Idea
Qisas is executed by sword only, not by mimicking the killer's act, because exact replication risks excess.

The method of executing qisas (retaliatory punishment) is a point of legal debate between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The Hanafis, relying on a prophetic hadith, restrict execution to a sword (or any weapon). The Shafi'is, emphasizing strict equivalence (musawah), hold that the killer should be subjected to the same act he committed, provided that act was legally permissible. This passage from Al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi case against the Shafi'i position, using both textual proof and rational analogy to warn against the risk of excessive punishment.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the clear ruling: qisas is carried out only with a sword (or any weapon). Note that the Hanafis do not replicate the killer's method.
The hadith 'No qisas except with the sword' is the key textual evidence.
2
State the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i requires treating the killer as he treated the victim, if that act was permissible (e.g., crushing with a stone). If it does not kill, the neck is cut.
The Shafi'i rely on the principle of musawah (equality).
3
Identify each school's proof
Hanafi proof: hadith + rational argument that exact replication may cause excess. Shafi'i proof: qiyas based on musawah – the killer's act must be matched.
Both schools use the same Quranic basis for qisas but differ in its application.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i argument
The Hanafis argue that exact replication is impractical: if the killer's method does not cause death, a second execution is needed, resulting in greater punishment than the crime. This is analogous to the prohibition of qisas for bones (other than teeth) where precise equivalence is impossible.
The Hanafi response is rooted in the avoidance of excess (ghuluw) and practical certainty.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
In practice, Hanafis execute by sword/weapon; Shafi'is use the same method as the killer if it was permissible (e.g., stoning), otherwise also by sword.
Both schools end up with execution by sword in most cases, except where the killer used a permissible method that can be exactly replicated.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا يستوفى القصاص إلا بالسيف وقال الشافعي يفعل به مثل ما فعل إن كان فعلاً مشروعاً فإن مات فيها وإلا حزت عنقه لأن مبنى القصاص على المساواة ولنا قوله عليه السلام لا قود إلا بالسيف والمراد به السلاح ولأن فيما ذهب إليه استيفاء الزيادة أو لم يحصل المقصود بمثل ما فعل فيحز فيجب التحرز عنه كما في كسر العظم. ترجمه: قدوری نے فرمایا قصاص نہیں لیا جائے گا مگر تلوار سے اور فرمایا شافعی نے کہ قاتل کے ساتھ اسی طرح برتاؤ کیا جائے گا جو کہ قاتل نے کیا ہے بشرطیکہ فعل مشروع ہو پس اگر قاتل اس سے مر گیا تو فبہا اور نہ اس کی گردن کاٹ دی جائے اس لئے کہ قصاص کی بنیاد مساوات پر ہے اور ہماری دلیل فرمان نبی علیہ السلام ہے قصاص نہیں ہے مگر تلوار سے ہتھیار مراد ہے اور اس لئے کہ اس طریقہ میں جس کی جانب شافعی گئے زیادہ وصول کرنا ہے اگر قاتل کے فعل کے مثل سے مقصود حاصل نہ ہو تو پھر گردن کائی جائے گی تو اس سے بچنا واجب ہوگا جیسے ہڈی توڑنے میں۔ تشریح: حنفیہ کے نزدیک صرف ہتھیار سے قصاص لیا جائے خواہ تلوار ہو یا بندوق، امام شافعی کے نزدیک یہ ہے کہ جو فعل قاتل نے کیا ہے اگر وہ مشروع فعل ہو تو قاتل کے ساتھ بھی ایسے ہی کیا جائے پھر اگر وہ اس سے مر جائے تو ٹھیک ورنہ اس کے بعد اس کی گردن کاٹ دی جائے کیونکہ قصاص کی بنیاد مساوات پر ہے۔ لہذا مساوات کا یہی طریقہ ہے۔ اور فعل مشروع یہ کہ قاتل نے بھاری پتھر سے کچل کر مارا ہو اور اگر فعل غیر مشروع ہو مثلاً قاتل نے مقتول کی مقعد میں لاٹھی یا نیز گھسا کر اس کو مارا ہو یا عورت کی شرمگاہ میں نیزہ داخل کر کے اس کو مارا تو امام شافعی بھی مساوات کے قائل نہیں ہیں۔ ہماری دلیل ایک تو ابن ماجہ کی حدیث ہے کہ قصاص تلوار یعنی ہتھیار سے لیا جائے اور دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ مساوات کی صورت اگر اختیار کی جائے گی تو زیادتی لازم آئے گی کیونکہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ وہ طریقہ اختیار کرنے سے جو قاتل نے اختیار کیا تھا ہوسکتا ہے کہ قاتل نہ مرے تو پھر اس کو قتل کرنا پڑے گا تو قاتل کے ساتھ اس کی حرکت سے زیادہ حرکت ہوئی اور یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس کی مثال ہڈی توڑنا ہے اگر دانت توڑا ہو تو قصاص ممکن ہے کیونکہ دانت محدود ہے اور اگر دانت کے علاوہ اور ہڈی توڑی ہو تو معلوم نہیں کہ قصاص میں کتنی بڑی توڑی جائے گی اگر اتنی ہی ہڈی قاتل کی توڑی جائے جتنی اس نے توڑی تھی یا اس سے کم تو جائز ہے اور اگر زیادہ توڑی جائے تو جائز نہیں ہے اور چونکہ یہاں یہ اطمینان نہیں ہے کہ زیادہ ہڈی نہیں ٹوٹے گی اس وجہ سے ہڈی کا قصاص جائز نہیں ہے تا کہ حق سے زیادہ وصول نہ ہو۔ اسی طرح جب قاتل کے فعل سے زیادہ وصول کرنا لازم آتا ہو تو جائز نہ ہوگا۔
He said: Qisas is not carried out except with the sword. And al-Shafi'i said: Do to him as he did, if his act was permissible (shar'i). If he dies from it, fine; otherwise, his neck is cut, because the foundation of qisas is equivalence. And our proof is the Prophet's statement: 'No qisas except with the sword' – meaning weapon. And because in what al-Shafi'i adopted there is extraction of excess, or the objective is not achieved by doing like what he did, so he must be cut, thus it is necessary to be cautious, as in breaking a bone. Translation: Quduri said: Qisas will not be taken except with a sword. And al-Shafi'i said: The killer will be treated as he treated, provided the act was permissible; if the killer dies from it, well and good, otherwise his neck is cut, because the basis of qisas is equality. And our proof is the statement of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'There is no qisas except with a sword' meaning weapon. And because in the method that al-Shafi'i adopted, there is extraction of excess; if the objective is not achieved by doing like what he did, then the neck is cut, so it is necessary to avoid that, like breaking a bone. Commentary: According to the Hanafis, qisas is only taken with a weapon, whether sword or gun. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, the killer should be treated exactly as he treated, if the act was permissible; if the killer does not die from that, then his neck is cut, because the basis of qisas is equality. So this is the way of equality. A permissible act is when the killer crushed the victim with a heavy stone. If the act was impermissible, such as inserting a stick or spear into the victim's rectum or a woman's private parts, then al-Shafi'i does not require equality. Our proof: first, the hadith of Ibn Majah that qisas is taken with a sword/weapon. Second, if equality is chosen, excess necessarily results, because it is possible that the method used by the killer does not cause death, then the killer would have to be executed (additionally), resulting in a greater punishment than the victim received, which is not permissible. An example is breaking a bone: if a tooth is broken, qisas is possible because the tooth is limited. But if a bone other than a tooth is broken, it is not known how much bone should be broken in qisas; if exactly as much is broken, it is permissible, but if more, it is not permissible, and since there is no certainty against excess, qisas for bone is not allowed. Similarly, whenever excess is inevitable, it is not permissible.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the method of executing qisas. The Hanafi position, attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa and his school, holds that qisas must be carried out exclusively with a sword (or any weapon such as a gun, by analogy). The proof is a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) reported in Sunan Ibn Majah: 'There is no qisas except with the sword,' interpreted as meaning any weapon. The rational argument is that if we try to replicate the exact method of killing (as the Shafi'is propose), there is a risk of exceeding the limit, because the intended equal punishment may not kill the offender, requiring a second act, which would be a greater punishment than the crime. This is analogous to the Hanafi ruling that qisas is not applied for breaking bones (other than teeth) because the exact measure cannot be determined without risk of excess. The Shafi'i school (Imam al-Shafi'i) argues that qisas should be based on complete equivalence (musawah), so the offender should be subjected to the same type of act that he committed, provided the act was legally permissible (e.g., crushing with a stone). If the act does not kill, then execution by sword follows. The Hanafi response counters that the risk of excess makes this approach unsound. Note that both schools agree that if the initial killing method was impermissible (e.g., sexual assault), equality is not required.

Key Terms
مساواة (musāwāh): Equivalence; the principle that the punishment in qisas should match the crime exactly.
قود (qawad): A synonym for qisas (retaliation) in some contexts; used in the hadith 'لا قود إلا بالسيف'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Consensus of the companions.
B) The Quranic verse on qisas.
C) A hadith: 'No qisas except with the sword.'
D) Analogical reasoning from divorce.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school restricts qisas execution to the sword (or weapon) to avoid the risk of excess inherent in exact replication of the killer's method, a position grounded in the hadith and rational caution.

Qisas for a Mukatab: Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qisas for a mukatab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad on qisas for a mukatab, and explain the basis for the dispute using the concept of sabab al-istifa.

Core Idea
When the cause for qisas is ambiguous between wala and milk, qisas is not established.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning qisas for a mukatab (a slave under a manumission contract) who is intentionally killed and leaves sufficient wealth to pay the kitabah, with no heir except his master. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the shaykhayn) rule that the master can claim qisas, while Imam Muhammad denies it. Understanding this ikhtilaf requires analyzing the sabab (cause) for claiming qisas and how ambiguity affects legal entitlements.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: the master has qisas. What is their implicit reasoning (the master is heir, wealth suffices for freedom)?
The shaykhayn consider the mukatab effectively free, so the master inherits via wala.
2
Identify Imam Muhammad's opposing view
Muhammad denies qisas. State his explicit reasoning: the cause (sabab) is confused between wala (if free) and milk (if slave).
The mukatab's intermediate status creates uncertainty about the basis of claim.
3
Analyze Muhammad's analogy
Examine the analogy of the slave-girl: if one claims sale and the other claims marriage, intercourse is not lawful due to conflicting causes. Similarly, when the cause for qisas is ambiguous, it should not be applied.
This is an argument from qiyas: conflicting sabab blocks the claim.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference? Under the shaykhayn's view, the master can demand qisas (or pardon). Under Muhammad's view, only diyah (blood money) is due.
The dispute affects the killer's punishment and the master's remedy.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
Which position is relied upon in the school? The text presents the shaykhayn's view first and it is considered the stronger position (mufta bihi).
Later Hanafi authorities generally follow Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

قال وإذا قتل المكاتب عمداً وليس له وارث إلا المولى وترك وفاء فله القصاص عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف قال محمد لا أرى في هذا قصاصاً لأنه اشتبه بسبب الاستيفاء فإنه الولاء إن مات حراً والملك إن مات عبداً وصار كمن قال لغيره بعتني هذه الجارية بكذا وقال المولى زوجتها منك لا يحل له وطؤها لاختلاف السبب كذا هذا. ترجمه: قدوری نے فرمایا کہ اور جب کہ مکاتب عمداً قتل کیا گیا اور آقا کے علاوہ اس کا کوئی وارث نہ ہو اور اس نے بدل کتابت کے برابر مال چھوڑا ہو تو ابو حنیفہ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک آقا کے لئے قصاص ہوگا، اور فرمایا محمدؐ نے میں اس میں قصاص جائز نہیں سمجھتا اس لئے کہ وصولیابی کا سبب مختلف ہو گیا اس لئے کہ وصول ولاء ہے اگر مکاتب آزاد ہو کر مرا ہو اور وصول ملک ہے اگر وہ غلام ہونے کی حالت میں مرا ہو اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے کسی نے اپنے غیر سے کہا کہ تو نے مجھے یہ باندی اتنے میں بیچی ہے اور مولی کہے کہ میں نے تجھ سے اس کا نکاح کیا ہے تو اختلاف سبب کی وجہ سے اس کے لئے اس باندی سے وطی کرنا حلال نہیں ہے ایسے ہی یہ ہے۔ تشریح: مکاتب کو کسی نے عمداً قتل کر دیا اور مکاتب نے کما کر اتنا مال چھوڑا ہے جس سے بدل کتابت ادا ہو جائے اور آقا کے علاوہ کوئی اس کا وارث نہیں ہے تو آقا کو قصاص لینے کا حق ہے یا نہیں ؟ اس میں اختلاف ہے حضرات شیخین فرماتے ہیں کہ آقا کو قصاص لینے کا حق ہے۔ اور امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ قصاص لینے کا حق نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہاں قصاص لینے کا سبب مختلف ہے اور سبب کا اختلاف ایسا ہے جیسے مستحق کا اختلاف اور مستحق کے اختلاف کی صورت میں قصاص نہیں لیا جاتا تو یہاں بھی قصاص نہیں لیا جائے گا۔
He said: And when a mukatab is killed intentionally and he has no heir except the master, and he leaves sufficient (wealth to pay kitabah), then the master has qisas according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: I do not consider any qisas in this case, because the cause of execution (istifa) is confused: for it is wala if he dies free, and ownership if he dies a slave. And it becomes like one who said to another: 'You sold me this slave-girl for such-and-such,' and the master says, 'I married her to you,' so it is not lawful for him to have intercourse with her due to the difference in cause. Similarly here. Translation: Quduri said: When a mukatab is killed intentionally and he has no heir except the master, and he leaves wealth equal to the kitabah, then Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the master has qisas. Muhammad said: I do not consider qisas valid in this case, because the cause of taking qisas has become confused: for the taking is wala if the mukatab dies free, and ownership if he dies a slave. And this is like a case where someone says to another: 'You sold me this slave-girl for such-and-such,' and the master says, 'I married her to you,' so intercourse with her is not lawful due to the difference of cause. Similarly here. Commentary: A mukatab is killed intentionally, and the mukatab has earned enough wealth to pay the kitabah, and he has no heir other than the master. Should the master have the right to qisas? There is a dispute: the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) say the master has the right to qisas. Imam Muhammad says he does not have the right to qisas, because here the cause of taking qisas is different, and the difference in cause is like the difference in the entitled person, and when the entitled person is different, qisas is not taken; so here too qisas will not be taken.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a mukatab (a slave under a manumission contract) who is intentionally killed. The key condition is that the mukatab leaves sufficient wealth to pay the remaining kitabah (contract price) and has no heir except his master. The two senior imams, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, rule that the master can claim qisas against the killer. Their reasoning is that the master is the heir of the mukatab, and since the mukatab's wealth suffices to complete the kitabah, the mukatab is considered to have fulfilled the contract, thus the master inherits his right to qisas. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani disagrees, arguing that the cause (sabab) for claiming qisas is ambiguous. The mukatab's status is between freedom and slavery: he will be treated as free (so the heir inherits through wala) if he dies free, or as a slave (so the master inherits through ownership) if he dies a slave. This conflict in potential causes (wala vs. milk) prevents a definitive claim to qisas, analogous to a case where two contradicting claims are made about a slave-girl (sale vs. marriage), rendering sexual intercourse unlawful. Since the cause for qisas is not settled, Muhammad considers qisas inapplicable. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as indicated by the term 'shaykhayn' (the two masters).

Key Terms
ولاء (walā): The right of inheritance that a former master has over a freed slave's estate; also used for the relationship of patronage.
سبب الاستيفاء (sabab al-istīfā): The cause or basis for claiming qisas; here, it refers to the reason the master would have the right to take qisas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the dispute over qisas for a mukatab, what is Imam Muhammad's reason for denying qisas?
A) The mukatab's family inherits qisas.
B) The cause for claiming qisas is confused between wala and milk.
C) The master is not an heir.
D) The mukatab did not die free.

Key Takeaway
The dispute hinges on whether the sufficient wealth removes the ambiguity of the mukatab's status; the shaykhayn say yes, Muhammad says no.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
8 min
The Requirement of Exact Equivalence in Qisas
ruling with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why qisas is not applicable when exact equivalence cannot be ensured, and identify the two proofs the Hanafi school uses to support this principle.

Core Idea
Qisas requires exact equivalence—when uncertain, diyah replaces execution.

Qisas, the retaliatory punishment, is founded on the principle of musawah (exact equivalence). The Hanafi school holds that if the killer's method cannot be replicated perfectly without risk of exceeding the original harm, or if the injury is not precisely measurable, qisas is invalid. Instead, the victim's heirs receive diyah (blood money). This lesson unpacks the reasoning, including the hadith 'al-qisas bi al-sayf' and the rational argument against excess.

Guided Path
1
State the foundational principle
Begin by noting that qisas is based on musawah—the punishment must exactly match the crime. This is the bedrock of the school's approach.
2
Distinguish permissible vs. impermissible methods
Identify the examples: crushing with a heavy stone (mashru') and inserting a stick into the rectum (ghayr mashru'). For impermissible methods, even Imam Shafi'i agrees qisas is off the table.
The impermissible methods are those that are themselves haram.
3
Examine the Hanafi proofs
Two proofs are given: (a) the hadith 'al-qisas bi al-sayf' indicating a standard weapon-based method, and (b) the rational argument that replicating the killer's method risks fatal excess—if the method fails to kill the killer, further action would exceed the original harm.
The hadith is ahad, so zanni in thubut, but accepted in this ruling.
4
Apply the logic to bone-breaking
Teeth are limited and measurable, so qisas is possible; other bones are not precisely measurable, so qisas is impermissible to avoid the risk of breaking more than was broken.
This illustrates the principle of avoiding ziyadah (excess).
5
Formulate the mufta bihi
Conclude: Whenever exact equivalence is uncertain (impermissible method, unmeasurable injury, risk of excess), qisas is replaced by diyah. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
Based on al-Marghinani's tarjih in al-Hidayah.

دی جائے کیونکہ قصاص کی بنیاد مساوات پر ہے۔ لہذا مساوات کا یہی طریقہ ہے۔ اور فعل مشروع یہ کہ قاتل نے بھاری پتھر سے کچل کر مارا ہو اور اگر فعل غیر مشروع ہو مثلاً قاتل نے مقتول کی مقعد میں لاٹھی یا نیز گھسا کر اس کو مارا ہو یا عورت کی شرمگاہ میں نیزہ داخل کر کے اس کو مارا تو امام شافعی بھی مساوات کے قائل نہیں ہیں۔ ہماری دلیل ایک تو ابن ماجہ کی حدیث ہے کہ قصاص تلوار یعنی ہتھیار سے لیا جائے اور دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ مساوات کی صورت اگر اختیار کی جائے گی تو زیادتی لازم آئے گی کیونکہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ وہ طریقہ اختیار کرنے سے جو قاتل نے اختیار کیا تھا ہوسکتا ہے کہ قاتل نہ مرے تو پھر اس کو قتل کرنا پڑے گا تو قاتل کے ساتھ اس کی حرکت سے زیادہ حرکت ہوئی اور یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس کی مثال ہڈی تو ڑنا ہے اگر دانت تو ڑا ہو تو قصاص ممکن ہے کیونکہ دانت محدود ہے اور اگر دانت کے علاوہ اور ہڈی توڑی ہو تو معلوم نہیں کہ قصاص میں کتنی بڑی توڑی جائے گی اگر اتنی ہی ہڈی قاتل کی توڑی جائے جتنی اس نے توڑی تھی یا اس سے کم تو جائز ہے اور اگر زیادہ توڑی جائے تو جائز نہیں ہے اور چونکہ یہاں یہ اطمینان نہیں ہے کہ زیادہ ہڈی نہیں ٹوٹے گی اس وجہ سے ہڈی کا قصاص جائز نہیں ہے تا کہ حق سے زیادہ وصول نہ ہو۔ اسی طرح جب قاتل کے فعل سے زیادہ وصول کرنا لازم آتا ہو تو جائز نہ ہوگا۔
It is given because the basis of qisas is equivalence. Thus this is the method of equivalence. And the prescribed act is that the killer killed by crushing with a heavy stone. But if the act is impermissible, e.g., the killer inserted a stick or spear into the victim's rectum and killed him, or inserted a spear into a woman's private parts and killed her, then Imam Shafi'i also does not uphold equivalence. Our proof: first, the hadith of Ibn Majah that qisas is taken with a sword, i.e., a weapon; second, if equivalence is adopted, excess becomes necessary because it is possible that by the method the killer used, the killer might not die, then he would have to be killed, resulting in a greater act than his, and this is not permissible. An example is breaking a bone: if a tooth is broken, qisas is possible because the tooth is limited; but if a bone other than a tooth is broken, it is not known how much of the bone should be broken in qisas. If the same amount of bone is broken as was broken, or less, it is permissible; but if more is broken, it is not permissible. Since there is no certainty that more bone will not be broken, qisas for bone is not permissible, so that more than the right is not taken. Similarly, when taking more than the killer's act becomes necessary, it is not permissible.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and includes an inter-madhhab reference. It explains the Hanafi position on the requirement of exact equivalence (musawah) in qisas. The author begins by stating that qisas is based on equivalence. Therefore, the method of execution must match the method used by the killer. The prescribed (mashru') act is when the killer used a heavy stone to crush the victim; that method can be replicated. However, if the method was impermissible (ghayr mashru'), such as inserting a stick or spear into the rectum or private parts, then even Imam al-Shafi'i agrees that equivalence cannot be applied. The Hanafi proof is two-fold: first, a hadith from Ibn Majah stating that qisas is to be carried out with a sword (a standard weapon); second, a rational argument: if equivalence is attempted via a similar method, there is a risk of excess—the killer might not die from that method, requiring further action, which would exceed the original harm. The same rationale applies to bone-breaking: teeth are limited and measurable, so qisas is possible; other bones are not precisely measurable, so qisas is not allowed for fear of exceeding. This demonstrates the Hanafi principle that whenever there is uncertainty of exact equivalence, qisas is replaced by diyah.

Key Terms
مساوات (musawah): Exact equivalence between the act of the killer and the punishment of qisas, both in method and extent.
فعل مشروع (fi'l mashru'): A legally permissible method of killing, such as crushing with a heavy stone, which can be replicated exactly in qisas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school prohibit qisas for breaking a bone other than a tooth?
A) Because bones are not mentioned in the Quran.
B) Because there is no certainty of exact equivalence, leading to risk of excess.
C) Because it is forbidden to break bones in general.
D) Because diyah is always preferred over qisas for bones.

Key Takeaway
Qisas requires exact equivalence; when equivalence cannot be ensured, diyah substitutes.

Qisas — Retaliation

Qisas for a Murdered Mukatab: The Dispute Between the Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qisas for a murdered mukatab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad on qisas for a murdered mukatab, identify their respective proofs, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of the dispute.

Core Idea
When the cause of entitlement is ambiguous, qisas is blocked; unless the ruling is one, then cause ambiguity is irrelevant.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad over whether the master of a murdered mukatab can claim qisas. The disagreement hinges on how to treat ambiguity in the legal cause (sabab) of entitlement when the status of the deceased (free or slave) is uncertain. The two shaykhs argue that since the master is definitely entitled on both assumptions, the difference in cause does not matter. Imam Muhammad counters that the ambiguity in the cause itself prevents qisas, analogizing to a case of conflicting contracts over a slave-girl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Determine the exact ruling in question and which Hanafi imams hold which position. The disputed issue is whether the master of a murdered mukatab, who leaves sufficient property and has no other heir, is entitled to qisas. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say yes; Imam Muhammad says no.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; all three imams base their rulings on the same usul principles but differ in their application to this case.
2
State Imam Muhammad's proof
Imam Muhammad argues that the cause of entitlement is ambiguous: if the mukatab died free, it is wala'; if he died a slave, it is ownership. Since his exact status is unknown, the cause is uncertain, and qisas is not taken. He analogizes to a case where a slave-girl is claimed to be either sold or married to a man — intercourse is not allowed due to conflicting causes.
Muhammad's analogy rests on the idea that differing causes lead to a dispute over entitlement, similar to a dispute between two claimants.
3
State the Shaykhayn's proof
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf respond that the master is certainly entitled on both assumptions (free or slave), the entitled person is known, and the ruling (qisas) is one and the same. Therefore, the underlying difference in cause does not affect the entitlement. They distinguish their case from Muhammad's analogy because there the rulings (permissibility of intercourse via milk vs. nikah) are different, whereas here the ruling is identical.
The key distinction is that in the slave-girl case, the two possible causes lead to different legal rulings; here they lead to the same ruling (qisas).
4
Analyze the analogy
Examine why the Shaykhayn reject Muhammad's analogy. In the slave-girl case, if the contract is sale, the man owns her and intercourse is permissible as property; if marriage, intercourse is permissible as marriage but with different rights. The rulings are distinct (ownership vs. marriage). In the mukatab case, whether the cause is wala' or ownership, the result is the same: the master gets qisas. Hence, the analogy fails.
The Shaykhayn's reasoning is that a difference in cause does not matter when the legal effect (hukm) is identical.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical consequence of the dispute. According to the mufta bihi position (Shaykhayn), the master can claim qisas when he is the sole potential heir. However, if the mukatab has any other heir (e.g., a free son), qisas is not taken because the entitled person becomes uncertain (master if slave, other heir if free).
The second scenario in the passage shows that when other heirs exist, even the Shaykhayn agree qisas is not taken, because the uncertainty is about the person entitled, not just the cause.

مکاتب عمدا قتل کر دیا گیا جس کا وارث سوائے مولیٰ کے اور کوئی نہیں اور اس کے پاس اتنی رقم تھی جس سے بدل کتابت ہوسکتا ہو تو قصاص کا حقدار کون ہے
قال واذا قتل المكاتب عمدا وليس له وارث الا المولى وترك وفاء فله القصاص عندابي حنيفة و ابي يوسف قال محمد لا ارى فى هذا قصاصا لانه اشتبه بسبب الاستيفاء فانه ان الاء ان مات حرار الملك ان مات عبد وصار كمن قال لغيره بعتني هذه الجارية بكذا وقال المولى زوجتها منك لا يحل له وطيها لاختلاف السبب كذا هذا
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا کہ اور جب کہ مکاتب عمدا قتل کیا گیا اور آقا کے علاوہ اس کا کوئی وارث نہ ہو اور اس نے بدل کتابت کے برابر مال چھوڑا ہو تو ابو حنیفہ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک آقا کے لئے قصاص ہوگا، اور فرمایا محمد نے میں اس میں قصاص جائز نہیں سمجھتا اس لئے کہ وصولیابی کا سبب مختلف ہو گیا اس لئے کہ وصول ولاء ہے اگر مکاتب آزاد ہو کر مرا ہو اور وصول ملک ہے اگر وہ غلام ہونے کی حالت میں مرا ہو اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے کسی نے اپنے غیر سے کہا کہ تو نے مجھے یہ باندی اتنے میں بیچی ہے اور مولی کہے کہ میں نے تجھ سے اس کا نکاح کیا ہے تو اختلاف سبب کی وجہ سے اس کے لئے اس باندی سے وطی کرنا حلال نہیں ہے ایسے ہی یہ ہے۔ تشریح مکاتب کو کسی نے عمدا قتل کر دیا اور مکاتب نے کما کر اتنا مال چھوڑا ہے جس سے بدل کتابت ادا ہو جائے اور آقا کے علاوہ کوئی اس کا وارث نہیں ہے تو آقا کو قصاص لینے کا حق ہے یا نہیں؟ اس میں اختلاف ہے حضرات شیخین فرماتے ہیں کہ آقا کو قصاص
لینے کا حق ہے۔
اور امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ قصاص لینے کا حق نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہاں قصاص لینے کا سبب مختلف ہے اور سبب کا اختلاف ایسا ہے جیسے مستحق کا اختلاف اور مستحق کے اختلاف کی صورت میں قصاص نہیں لیا جاتا تو یہاں بھی قصاص نہیں لیا جائے گا۔
کیونکہ اگر مانیں کہ وہ آزادی کی حالت میں مرا ہے تو قصاص لینے کا سبب ولاء ہے اور اگر یہ مانیں کہ وہ غلام ہو کر مرا تو قصاص لینے کا سبب ملک ہے اور اس کی مثال یہ ہے کہ آقا نے اپنی باندی کے بارے میں کہا کہ میں نے اس سے تیرا نکاح کیا ہے اور وہ کہے کہ نہیں بلکہ تو نے مجھے اس کو اتنے میں فروخت کیا ہے تو اس کے لئے اس باندی سے وطی جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ سبب مختلف ہے اور ایسے ہی یہاں بھی جب سبب کا اختلاف ہے تو جیسے وطی جائز نہیں ایسے ہی قصاص بھی جائز نہیں ہے یہ امام محمد کی دلیل ہے۔
شیخین کی دلیل
ولهما أن حق الاستيفاء للمولى بيقين على التقديرين وهو معلوم والحكم متحد و اختلاف السبب لا يفضي الى المنازعة ولا الى اختلاف حكم فلا يبالى به بخلاف تلك المسألة لان حكم ملك اليمين يغاير حكم النكاح ترجمہ اور شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مولیٰ کے لئے دونوں تقدیروں پر یقین کے ساتھ وصولیابی کا حق ہے اور مولیٰ معلوم ہے اور حکم ایک ہے اور سبب کا اختلاف نہ منازعت کی جانب مفضی ہے اور نہ اختلاف حکم کی جانب تو اختلاف سبب کی پرواہ نہیں کی جائے گی ۔ بخلاف اس مسئلہ کے اس لئے کہ ملک یمین کا حکم مغائر ہے۔ تشریح شیخین کی دلیل ہے کہ مولی کو قصاص لینے کا حق ہے کیونکہ وہ آزاد مرے یا غلام دونوں صورتوں میں مولی کو قصاص لینے کا حق ہے اور مستحق یعنی مولی بھی معلوم ہے اور حکم بھی متحد ہے یعنی قصاص وصول کرنا۔ اور سبب کے اندر اگر چہ اختلاف ہے لیکن اس کی کوئی پرواہ نہیں کی جائے گی اس لئے اس کی وجہ سے حکم میں اختلاف نہیں ہے اور نہ اختلاف سبب مفضی الی المنازعت ہے اور جو مسئلہ دلیل میں امام محمد نے پیش فرمایا ہے اس کی بات اور ہے کیونکہ وہاں حکم میں مغایرت ہے اس لئے کہ ملک یمین کا حکم اور ہے اور ملک نکاح کا اور ہے۔ کیونکہ ملک یمین کا حکم یہ ہے کہ وہ مملوکہ ہو جس میں حلت تابع ہے اور ملک اور رقبہ اصل ہے اور تابع معدوم کے درجہ میں ہوتا ہے اور نکاح میں حلت مقصود ہے۔
اگر مکاتب کے مولیٰ کے علاوہ ورثاء بھی موجود ہوں تو قصاص کا کیا حکم ہے
ولو ترک وفاء وله وارث غير المولى فلا قصاص وان اجتمعوا مع المولى لا نه اشتبه من له الحق لا نه المولى ان مات عبدا والوارث ان مات حرا اذ ظهر الاختلاف بين الصحابة رضى الله عنهم فى موته على نعت الحرية او الرق بخلاف الأولى لان المولى متعين فيها ترجمہ اور اگر مقتول عمد مکاتب نے بدل کتابت کے برابر مال چھوڑا ہو اور آقا کے علاوہ اس کا کوئی اور وارث ہو تو قصاص نہیں ہے اگر چہ ورثا، آقا کے ساتھ جمع ہو جائیں۔ اس لئے کہ وہ شخص مشتبہ ہو گیا جس کا حق ہے اس لئے کہ وہ ( من لہ الحق ) مولی ہے اگر مکاتب غلام مرا ہو اور وارث ہے اگر وہ آزاد ہو کر مرا ہو اس لئے کہ صحابہ کرام رضی اللہ عنہم میں اختلاف ظاہر ہوا ہے اس کے حریت یا رقیت پر مرنے کی صفت کے اوپر، بخلاف پہلی صورت کے اس لئے کہ اس میں مولی متعین ہے۔
A mukatab was killed intentionally. He had no heir except the master, and he had enough property to complete the kitaba. Who is entitled to qisas? He (al-Quduri) said: And when the mukatab is killed intentionally and he has no heir except the master and leaves sufficient property, then according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf he has the right to qisas. Muhammad said: I do not see any qisas in this case because the cause of taking becomes ambiguous. Because the taking is wala if he died free, and it is ownership if he died a slave. It is like when someone says to another: 'You sold me this slave-girl for such-and-such,' and the master says: 'I married her to you' — it is not permissible for him to have intercourse with her due to the difference in cause. Thus this case. Translation: al-Quduri said: When the mukatab is killed intentionally and has no heir except the master, and leaves property equivalent to the kitaba, then according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf the master gets qisas. Muhammad said: I do not consider qisas valid in this case because the cause of taking is different: it is wala if he died free, and it is ownership if he died a slave. This is like a case where someone says to another, 'You sold me this slave-girl for such,' and the master says, 'I married her to you' — due to conflict of cause, intercourse is not halal for him. Similarly here. Explanation: A mukatab is killed intentionally and has acquired enough property to pay the kitaba, and has no heir but the master. Is the master entitled to qisas? There is disagreement: the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) say yes. Imam Muhammad says no, because the cause of taking qisas is different. The difference in cause is like difference in the entitled person. When the entitled person is uncertain, qisas is not taken. So here too. Because if we consider that he died free, the cause is wala; if he died a slave, the cause is ownership. An example: a master says about his slave-girl, 'I married her to you,' and the other says, 'You sold her to me' — intercourse is not permitted due to conflicting causes. So here too: when the cause conflicts, just as intercourse is not permissible, so qisas is not permissible. This is Imam Muhammad's proof. The proof of the two shaykhs: And for them is that the right of taking for the master is certain on both estimates, and he is known, and the ruling is one, and difference in cause does not lead to dispute nor to difference in ruling, so it is not considered. Unlike that other issue, because the ruling of ownership by right hand (milk al-yamin) is different from the ruling of marriage. Translation: And the proof of the two shaykhs is that the master has a certain right to take qisas on both assumptions, the master is known, and the ruling is one (qisas). Difference in cause does not lead to conflict nor to difference in ruling, so it is not considered. Unlike that issue, because the ruling of milk al-yamin differs from that of marriage. Explanation: The proof of the two shaykhs is that the master has the right to qisas because whether he died free or slave, the master is entitled. The entitled person (master) is known, and the ruling is one (taking qisas). Even if the cause differs, it is not considered because it does not affect the ruling or cause conflict. The issue raised by Imam Muhammad is different because there the rulings differ: milk al-yamin has a different ruling than marriage. In milk al-yamin, the female slave becomes owned, and permissibility of intercourse is subordinate; ownership of the person is primary. In marriage, permissibility is the primary objective. If the mukatab has other heirs besides the master, what is the ruling? And if he leaves sufficient property and has an heir other than the master, then there is no qisas, even if they join with the master, because the person entitled is uncertain: the master if he died a slave, and the heir if he died free. This is because the Companions differed regarding his death as free or slave. Unlike the first case, because there the master is definite.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding qisas for a murdered mukatab. The issue arises when a mukatab (a slave under a contract of manumission) is intentionally killed, and he leaves property sufficient to pay the kitaba (contract price), with no heir except his master. The question is whether the master can claim qisas or not. The text opens with a ruling from al-Quduri's matn, citing the disagreement. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the master is entitled to qisas, while Muhammad al-Shaybani rejects it. Muhammad's reasoning is based on the ambiguity of the cause (sabab) of taking qisas. The mukatab's status at death is uncertain: if he died free (having effectively become free due to his ability to pay), the master's right to qisas arises from wala (patronage); if he died a slave, the right arises from ownership (milk). Since the exact status is unknown, the cause is ambiguous. Muhammad analogizes this to a case where two people claim different contracts (sale vs. marriage) over the same slave-girl — neither can claim sexual intercourse because the cause is disputed. Similarly, here, the master cannot claim qisas because the cause is unclear. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) counter that regardless of the mukatab's status, the master is definitely the one entitled to qisas. The ruling (hukm) is one: qisas. The uncertainty in the cause does not affect the ruling because the master is known and the object is the same. The distinction from Muhammad's analogy is that in the slave-girl case, the rulings (permissibility of intercourse via ownership vs. marriage) are different; here the ruling (qisas) is the same. Thus, the difference in cause is irrelevant. The passage then adds a second scenario: if the mukatab has other heirs besides the master, then no qisas is allowed at all, even if the master joins with them. This is because the person entitled becomes uncertain: if the mukatab died a slave, the master is entitled; if he died free, the other heir is entitled. Since the Companions differed on whether to presume freedom or slavery at death, the entitlement is ambiguous, and qisas is not applied. This contrasts with the first scenario where only the master could possibly be entitled, making him definite.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract (kitaba) with his master to pay a certain sum in exchange for freedom.
ولاء (wala'): The right of inheritance and patronage that a former master has over a freed slave (mawla).
وفاء (wafa'): Sufficient property left by the mukatab to pay the kitaba (contract price).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, when does the master of a murdered mukatab get qisas?
A) When the master is the sole heir and the mukatab leaves sufficient property.
B) When the mukatab died free.
C) When no other heir exists regardless of property.
D) Never, because a mukatab is a slave.

Key Takeaway
The master's right to qisas for a murdered mukatab is certain on both assumptions of freedom or slavery; only when other heirs appear does the entitlement become uncertain, blocking qisas.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
12 min
Qisas for a Mukatab with Only Master as Heir: Dispute Between Imam Muhammad and the Two Shaykhs
Intra-Hanafi dispute with qiyas reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the opposing arguments of Imam Muhammad and the two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) regarding qisas for a mukatab with only the master as heir, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of their disagreement.

Core Idea
When a mukatab is killed, his master's right to qisas is certain in both scenarios; difference in cause does not create a dispute.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute on the right to claim qisas when a mukatab is intentionally killed and leaves property equal to the kitabah, with the master as the sole heir. The uncertainty over whether the mukatab died free or a slave leads to conflicting legal causes (wala' vs. milk). Imam Muhammad argues that this uncertainty prevents qisas, analogizing to a case where a slave-girl's status is disputed. The two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) counter that the master's right is certain in both scenarios, so the difference in cause is irrelevant. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to analyze qiyas (analogical reasoning) and tarjih (preference) within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the uncertainty
The mukatab is killed and leaves property exactly equal to the kitabah (the amount he owed for emancipation). Since it is unknown whether he had already paid and become free, or died before payment and remained a slave, his status at death is uncertain. The master is his only heir.
If he died free, the cause for qisas is wala' (clientage); if he died a slave, the cause is milk al-yamin (ownership).
2
Understand Imam Muhammad's argument and his analogy
Imam Muhammad argues that because the cause is uncertain (wala' or milk), qisas cannot be claimed, just as in the case of a slave-girl where a master claims to have married her to a man but the man claims to have bought her. In that case, intercourse is prohibited because the cause (marriage vs. ownership) is conflicting. Here too, qisas should be prohibited.
The common element is that conflicting causes prevent the establishment of the right.
3
Analyze the two Shaykhs' rebuttal
The two Shaykhs respond that the analogy fails because in the slave-girl case, the rulings (intercourse under marriage vs. ownership) are fundamentally different—one makes permissibility the primary aim, the other makes it subordinate. But in the qisas case, the ruling is the same (qisas) regardless of the cause. Since the right of the master is certain in both estimates, the difference in cause does not lead to a difference in ruling and should be ignored.
The Shaikhayn's position is that certainty of the right outweighs uncertainty of the cause.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
According to Imam Muhammad, the master cannot claim qisas, so the killer must pay diyah (blood money). According to the two Shaykhs, the master can claim qisas, potentially leading to the execution of the killer. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that of the two Shaykhs.
The tarjih is based on the strength of the majority view and the principle that certainty overrides doubt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ولهما أن حق الاستيفاء للمولى بيقين على التقديرين وهو معلوم والحكم متحد و اختلاف السبب لا يفضي الى المنازعة ولا الى اختلاف حکم فلا يبالی به بخلاف تلك المسألة لان حکم ملك اليمين يغاير حکم النكاح

تشریح: شیخین کی دلیل ہے کہ مولی کو قصاص لینے کا حق ہے کیونکہ وہ آزاد مرے یا غلام دونوں صورتوں میں مولی کو قصاص لینے کا حق ہے اور مستحق یعنی مولی بھی معلوم ہے اور حکم بھی متحد ہے یعنی قصاص وصول کرنا۔ اور سبب کے اندر اگر چہ اختلاف ہے لیکن اس کی کوئی پرواہ نہیں کی جائے گی اس لئے اس کی وجہ سے حکم میں اختلاف نہیں ہے اور نہ اختلاف سبب مفضی الی المنازعت ہے اور جو مسئلہ دلیل میں امام محمد نے پیش فرمایا ہے اس کی بات اور ہے کیونکہ وہاں حکم میں مغامرت ہے اس لئے کہ ملک یمین کا حکم اور ہے اور ملک نکاح کا اور ہے۔ کیونکہ ملک یمین کا حکم یہ ہے کہ وہ مملوکہ ہو جس میں حلت تابع ہے اور ملک اور رقبہ اصل ہے اور تابع معدوم کے درجہ میں ہوتا ہے اور نکاح میں حلت مقصود ہے۔
Because if we assume that he died in a state of freedom, then the cause for taking qisas is wala', and if we assume that he died as a slave, then the cause for taking qisas is milky. And its example is that a master said about his slave-girl, 'I married her to you,' and the other says, 'No, rather you sold her to me for such amount,' then for him, sexual intercourse with that slave-girl is not permissible because the cause is different. Similarly here as well, when there is difference of cause, just as intercourse is not permissible, likewise qisas is not permissible. This is the proof of Imam Muhammad.
Proof of the two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf): And for them two, the right of execution (of qisas) belongs to the master with certainty in both estimations, and he (the master) is known, and the ruling is unified, and difference of cause does not lead to dispute nor to difference of ruling, so it is not taken into consideration, contrary to that matter because the ruling of milk al-yamin differs from the ruling of marriage.
Translation: And the proof of the two Shaykhs is that the master has the right of execution with certainty in both estimations, and the master is known, and the ruling is one, and difference of cause does not lead to dispute nor to difference of ruling, so difference of cause is not taken into consideration. Contrary to that matter because the ruling of milk al-yamin is different.
Explanation: The proof of the two Shaykhs is that the master has the right to take qisas because whether he died free or as a slave, in both cases the master has the right to take qisas, and the entitled person, i.e., the master, is known, and the ruling is also unified, i.e., executing qisas. And although there is difference in cause, it will not be taken into consideration because due to it there is no difference in ruling, nor does the difference of cause lead to dispute. And the matter that Imam Muhammad presented as proof is something else because there the ruling is different, because the ruling of milk al-yamin is different and the ruling of milk al-nikah is different. Because the ruling of milk al-yamin is that the owned woman is such that permissibility (of intercourse) is subordinate, and ownership and the corpus (raqabah) are the primary basis, and the subordinate is in the status of non-existent, whereas in marriage, permissibility is the intended purpose.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and the two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) regarding the right of qisas when a mukatab (a slave under contract of emancipation) is intentionally killed and leaves property equal to the kitabah, with only the master as his heir. The key issue is the legal cause for claiming qisas. Imam Muhammad argues that if the mukatab died free (because he could pay), the cause is wala' (clientage), but if he died a slave (because he could not pay), the cause is milky (ownership). Since these causes are different, and in a similar scenario—where a master claims to have married his slave-girl to a man, while the man claims to have bought her—intercourse is prohibited due to conflicting causes, similarly qisas should be prohibited here. The two Shaykhs counter that the master's right to qisas is certain in both scenarios; the entitled person (master) is known, and the ruling (qisas) is the same. Difference in cause does not lead to dispute or difference in ruling, so it is ignored. They distinguish Imam Muhammad's example: in the slave-girl case, the rulings of milk al-yamin (ownership) and marriage are fundamentally different—in ownership, permissibility of intercourse is subordinate to ownership of the corpus, while in marriage, permissibility is the primary aim—so that analogy does not apply here.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract of manumission (kitabah) with his master, agreeing to pay a sum in installments for his freedom.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment for intentional homicide, where the victim's legal heir has the right to demand execution of the killer.
ولاء (wala'): Clientage bond between a freed slave and his manumitter; gives the manumitter inheritance rights and, in this context, the right to claim qisas.
ملك يمين (milk al-yamin): Right of ownership over a slave; gives the master the right to claim qisas if the slave is killed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), what is the basis for allowing qisas when a mukatab dies and his master is the sole heir?
A) Because the mukatab was definitely a slave at death.
B) Because the master's right to qisas is certain in both scenarios, and the ruling is unified.
C) Because the cause of wala' and milky are identical.
D) Because Imam Muhammad's analogy with the slave-girl case is correct.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when the master is the sole heir of a mukatab killed, the master can claim qisas because his right is certain, even though the exact legal cause (wala' or milk) is uncertain.

Qisas — Retaliation

Qisas When Mukatab Has Other Heirs Besides Master
Stating the ruling when a mukatab leaves property and has other heirs besides the master

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas when a murdered mukatab has heirs other than the master and explain the reasoning based on ishtibah (ambiguity).

Core Idea
When a mukatab's status at death is uncertain, ambiguity (ishtibah) blocks qisas.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in qisas: the intentional killing of a mukatab who leaves sufficient property and has heirs besides the master. While in the previous case (only master as heir) the Shaikhayn allowed qisas, here the presence of other heirs creates an ambiguity about entitlement, leading to consensus among Hanafi jurists that qisas is not taken. The reason is the unresolved dispute among the Companions regarding the mukatab's status (free or slave) at death, which makes it impossible to determine the true heir entitled to qisas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The mukatab is killed intentionally, leaves property equal to the kitabah, and has at least one heir other than the master. This is the second case discussed in the text.
If only the master were the heir, the ruling would be different (the two Shaykhs would allow qisas).
2
State the ruling
There is no qisas, even if the other heirs join the master in demanding it. This is the unanimous position of the Hanafi school in this scenario.
The text uses 'fala qisas' (no qisas) to indicate the claim is void.
3
Understand the cause—ishtibah
The identity of the rightful claimant is ambiguous. If the mukatab died a slave, the master is entitled; if he died free, the other heirs are entitled. Because there is a known dispute among the Companions on whether a mukatab who leaves sufficient property becomes free at death or remains a slave, the true status is uncertain.
The Arabic term used is 'ishtibah' (اشتباه) – ambiguity due to conflicting possibilities.
4
Contrast with the earlier case
In the first case (master as sole heir), the master is the only possible claimant – no ambiguity. Therefore, the Shaikhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) ruled qisas is taken. Here, because of multiple claimants, the ruling changes.
This contrast highlights the principle: certainty of the heir is a requirement for qisas.
5
Memorize the ruling and its basis
Commit to memory: 'When a mukatab leaves sufficient property and has heirs besides the master, qisas is not taken due to ishtibah.' The proof is the ikhtilaf among the Companions (dalil naqli).
This is a memorization anchor – a key ruling that often appears in exam questions.

اور وہ غلام مرا ہے یا آزاد یہ صحابہ کرام رضی اللہ عنہم کا اختلافی مسئلہ ہے تو کسی صورت کو متعین کرنا دشوار ہے۔ اس لئے قصاص ختم کر دیا گیا اور پہلی صورت میں مستحق صرف مولی تھا اس لئے شیخین نے فرمایا کہ قصاص لیا جائیگا۔
If the mukatab leaves property equal to the kitabah and he has an heir other than the master, then there is no qisas, even if they (the other heirs) are together with the master, because the person who has the right is ambiguous. Because the master (has the right) if he died as a slave, and the heir (has the right) if he died as a free person, since there is a known difference among the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, regarding his death being in the description of freedom or slavery. Contrary to the first case because the master is determined (as the only heir) therein.
Translation: And if the intentional slain mukatab has left property equal to the kitabah and he has an heir other than the master, then there is no qisas even if the heirs are gathered with the master. Because the person who has the right has become ambiguous: that is, the master (has the right) if he died a slave, and the heir (has the right) if he died free. Because a difference has appeared among the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, regarding he died in the attribute of freedom or slavery. Contrary to the first case because the master is determined (as the only heir) therein.
Explanation: In the first case, when only the master was his heir, its ruling has been mentioned as disputed. And if besides the master, his other heirs are present, and the rest of the scenario is the same, then by consensus qisas will not be taken. Because in the first case, there was difference of cause and the ruling was unified, but here there is difference in the entitled person. In one scenario the master is entitled, and in one scenario the heirs of the slain mukatab are entitled. If it is assumed that he died free, then the heir is entitled; and if it is assumed that he died a slave, then the master is entitled. And whether he died a slave or free is a disputed matter among the Companions, so it is difficult to determine either scenario. Therefore, qisas is abolished. In the first case, the only entitled person was the master, so the two Shaykhs said that qisas will be taken.

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling when a mukatab is killed and leaves property equal to the kitabah, but has other heirs besides the master. Here, all Hanafi jurists agree that no qisas is taken. The reason is that the identity of the rightful claimant is uncertain: if the mukatab died a slave, the master is the heir; if he died free, the other relatives are the heirs. Because there was a difference among the Companions regarding whether a mukatab who leaves sufficient property is considered free or remains a slave until payment, this uncertainty prevents qisas. This contrasts with the previous case where the master was the only possible heir, so the Shaikhayn allowed qisas.

Key Terms
اشتباه (ishtibah): Ambiguity regarding the identity of the rightful claimant due to conflicting possibilities. In this case, the ambiguity arises because the mukatab's status at death (free or slave) is uncertain, and each possible status gives a different person the right to qisas.

Qisas for an Insolvent Mukatab: Master's Right
Ruling with contrast and qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas when a mukatab dies without property and explain why the master, not free heirs, has the right, while also distinguishing the case of a partially freed slave.

Core Idea
If a mukatab dies insolvent, his kitabah dissolves and he is a slave; thus, only his master has the right to qisas.

This lesson examines a specific ruling within Hanafi criminal law: the entitlement to qisas when a mukatab (a slave under a contract of manumission) is killed but leaves no property to fulfill his kitabah. The passage first establishes the unanimous Hanafi position, then contrasts it with the more nuanced case of a partially freed slave, revealing an intra-madhhab dispute. Understanding this ruling clarifies how the status of the deceased affects the right to retaliation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Case
Clearly state the scenario: a mukatab is killed, and he leaves no property that would cover the kitabah. Note that he has free heirs.
2
State the Ruling
According to all three Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), the master alone is entitled to qisas. The free heirs have no claim.
This is the unanimous (mujma‘) position in the Hanafi school.
3
Explain the Legal Cause (Illah)
The kitabah is dissolved because the mukatab is unable to pay. Consequently, he is deemed to have died as a slave. Since the master is the sole owner of a slave, only he has the right to demand qisas or accept diya.
The dissolution is due to inability (al-‘ajz), not death. If he had property, the kitabah would continue and he would be considered free, giving heirs the right.
4
Contrast with Partially Freed Slave
In the case of a mu‘taq al-ba‘d (partially freed slave) who dies insolvent, the partial freedom does not dissolve. Hence, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the master does not have full ownership, so qisas is not established. The Sahibayn, however, argue that freeing a part is like freeing the whole, so they would allow qisas.
This ikhtilaf shows the importance of whether freedom is revocable or not.
5
Extract the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference: in the mukatab case, the master definitely gets qisas; in the mu‘taq al-ba‘d case, it depends on which view is followed. Note that the mufta bihi position for the mu‘taq ba‘d is not stated here.
The passage only presents the dispute; it does not resolve it.

Source Text

اگر مکاتب بدل کتابت کے برابر مال نہ چھوڑ کر قتل ہوا تو قصاص کا حقدار آقا ہے
وان لم يترك وفاء وله ورثة احرار وحب القصاص للمولى فى قولهم جميعا لا نه مات عبدا بلا ريب لانفساخ الكتابة بخلاف معتق البعض اذا مات ولم يترك وفاء لان العتق في البعض لا ينفسخ بالعجز.
ترجمہ اور اگر مکاتب نے بدل کتابت کے برابر مال نہ چھوڑا ہو اور اس کے آزاد ورثہ ہیں تو مولیٰ کیلئے قصاص ہو گا تمام فقہاء کے قول میں۔ اس لئے کہ وہ کتابت فسخ ہونے کی وجہ سے بلاشبہ غلام مرا ہے بخلاف معتق البعض کے جب کہ وہ مر جائے اور سعایت کے برابر مال نہ چھوڑے اس لئے کہ بعض حصہ میں عشق عاجزی کی وجہ سے نسخ نہیں ہوتا۔
تشریح کسی مکاتب کو کسی نے عمد قتل کر دیا لیکن اس نے اتنا مال نہیں چھوڑا جو بدل کتابت کو پورا کر چکے۔ اور اس کے آزاد ورثہ موجود ہیں تو یہاں بالاتفاق آقا کیلئے قصاص ہو گا۔ کیونکہ جب وہ اداء کتابت سے عاجز ثابت ہوا تو عقد کتابت فسخ ہو گیا اور جب کتابت فسخ ہوگئی تو وہ غلام مرا ہے اور جب غلام مرا ہے تو حق قصاص فقط مولی کیلئے ہوگا۔ البتہ اگر ایک غلام دو شخصوں کے درمیان مشترک ہے اور ایک نے اپنا حصہ آزاد کر دیا اور دوسرے حصہ میں وہ کمائی کر رہا تھا کہ اس کو کسی نے عمد قتل کر دیا اور ابھی اتنا مال نہیں کمایا تھا جو اس مقدار کے برابر ہو جو اس کو کمانا تھا تو یہاں قصاص نہیں لیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک محق اگرچہ میجوری ہے لیکن اداء مال سے عاجزی کی وجہ سے معتق بعض منح نہ ہوگا۔ لہذا انجز غلام کی وجہ سے پورے غلام میں موجود مولی کی ملکیت ثابت نہ ہوگی۔
اور صاحبین کے نزدیک تو اعتاق بعض اعتناق کل ہے لہذا ان کے قول پر تو کوئی اشکال ہے ہی نہیں۔
If the mukatab does not leave property equal to the kitabah and his free heirs are present, then qisas belongs to the master according to the saying of all of them (the three imams). Because he died a slave without doubt due to the dissolution of the kitabah. Contrary to the partially freed slave (mu'taq al-ba'd) when he dies and does not leave property, because the freedom in a part does not dissolve due to inability.
Translation: And if the mukatab has not left property equal to the kitabah and he has free heirs, then the master will have qisas according to the saying of all the jurists. Because due to the dissolution of the kitabah, he died a slave without doubt. Contrary to the partially freed slave when he dies and leaves no property, because the freedom in a part does not dissolve due to inability.
Explanation: Someone intentionally killed the mukatab, but he has not left enough property to cover the kitabah, and he has free heirs. Here, by consensus, the master will have qisas. Because when he becomes unable to pay the kitabah, the contract of kitabah is dissolved, and when it is dissolved, he died a slave. And when he died a slave, the right to qisas is only for the master. However, if a slave is jointly owned by two persons, and one freed his share, and the other part he was working to earn, then someone intentionally killed him, and he had not yet earned enough to equal the amount he needed to earn, then here qisas will not be taken. Because according to Imam Abu Hanifa, although the right is [؟] due to inability to pay, the partial freedom does not dissolve. Therefore, due to the [؟] slave, the master's ownership over the entire slave is not established. And according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), freeing a part is freeing the whole, so there is no issue in their saying.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage states the rule when a mukatab is killed but leaves no property to cover the kitabah. In this case, the kitabah is dissolved because he is unable to pay, so he is conclusively considered a slave at death. Therefore, all three Hanafi imams agree that the master alone is entitled to qisas, regardless of any free heirs. The passage then contrasts this with the case of a partially freed slave (mu'taq al-ba'd), i.e., a slave who has been freed in part but still owes for the remainder. If such a person dies without enough property to pay for his remaining slavery, his partial freedom does not dissolve. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, since the partial freedom remains, the master does not have full ownership over him, and thus qisas is not established. According to the two companions (the Sahibayn), freeing a part is like freeing the whole, so they would allow qisas. This shows that the ruling for the mukatab without property is clear and unanimous, while the partially freed slave situation involves further intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract with his master to earn his freedom by paying a specified sum (kitabah).
كتابة (kitabah): The contract of manumission between a master and slave, where the slave pays a fixed amount over time in exchange for freedom.
معتق البعض (mu'taq al-ba'd): A slave who has been partially freed by his master, e.g., one half, while the other half remains in slavery; the slave works to earn money to buy the remaining portion.

Key Takeaway
A mukatab who dies without property is legally a slave at death, so his master—not free heirs—has the exclusive right to qisas.

Qisas — Retaliation

Qisas for Killed Mukatab Without Sufficient Property
Ruling on qisas when mukatab dies insolvent with free heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas when a mukatab dies insolvent and distinguish it from the case of a partially freed slave, applying the principle of rescission of kitabah.

Core Idea
If a mukatab dies insolvent, the master gets qisas; partial manumission is not rescinded.

When a mukatab (slave under contract) is killed, who has the right to demand retributive justice? This lesson examines a specific scenario: the mukatab dies without enough property to pay his kitabah, but leaves free heirs. The Hanafi school unanimously rules that the master, not the free heirs, is entitled to qisas. The key is that the kitabah contract is rescinded due to insolvency, reverting the mukatab to full slave status. This is contrasted with a mu'allaq ba'd (partially freed slave), where partial manumission is permanent and the free heirs inherit the qisas right.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the hukm? The master's right to qisas is established when a mukatab is killed and dies insolvent with free heirs.
The passage uses 'حق القصاص للمولى'.
2
Locate the 'illah (reason)
Why does the master get qisas? Because the mukatab died a slave due to rescission of kitabah (لانه مات عبدا بلا ريب لانفساخ الكتابة).
Inability to pay rescinds the contract, reverting slave status.
3
Compare with mu'allaq ba'd
How is the partially freed slave different? His manumission is not rescinded by inability (بخلاف معتق البعض... لان العتق في البعض لا ينفسخ بالعجز). Thus, free heirs inherit qisas.
Partial freedom is irreversible.
4
Note the unanimity
All Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree: 'في قولهم جميعا'.
Intra-madhhab consensus.
5
Evaluate the thamarah
Practical outcome: Free heirs do not get qisas if the mukatab died as a slave; the master is the sole heir for qisas.
Contrast with mu'allaq ba'd where free heirs prevail.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن لم يترك وفاء وله ورثة احرار وحق القصاص للمولى فى قولهم جميعا لانه مات عبدا بلا ريب لانفساخ الكتابة بخلاف معتق البعض اذا مات ولم يترك وفاء لان العتق في البعض لا ينفسخ بالعجز.
And if he does not leave sufficient (property) and he has free heirs, the right of qisas belongs to the master in all their statements, because he died a slave without doubt due to rescission of the kitabah, unlike the partially freed slave when he dies and does not leave sufficient, because manumission of a part is not rescinded by inability.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This is a ruling on qisas (retributive justice) when a mukatab (slave under contract of manumission) is killed. The passage compares two scenarios. First, if the mukatab is killed and does not leave enough property to cover the kitabah (written contract price), and he has free heirs, the master (sayyid) has the right to qisas according to all Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). The reasoning: since he could not pay, the kitabah is rescinded, so he died as a slave, thus the master is the only heir. Second, in contrast, if a mu'allaq ba'd (partially freed slave) dies without sufficient property, the master does not get qisas because the partial manumission is not rescinded by inability; the slave remains partially free, so the free heirs take precedence. The commentary emphasizes that in the first case the ruling is unanimous among the three. This distinction is based on the legal effect of rescission (faskh) in kitabah versus the irreversibility of partial manumission.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered a contract (kitabah) to purchase his freedom by paying installments.
بدل کتابت (badal al-kitabah): The agreed price for manumission in the kitabah contract.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
8 min
Qisas for a Killed Pledged Slave: Joint Consent Required
Ruling that qisas requires both rahin and murtahin to unite

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas for a marhun slave killed in the murtahin's possession and explain why both rahin and murtahin must jointly consent.

Core Idea
Qisas for a pledged slave requires both pledgor and pledgee to agree — neither can act alone.

When a pledged slave is killed while held by the creditor, who has the right to claim qisas? The Hanafi school rules that neither the pledgor nor the pledgee can act independently. Instead, both must unite and consent. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this joint requirement, balancing the pledgor's ownership with the pledgee's security interest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the ruling
Read the passage. The case: a marhun (pledged) slave is killed while in the possession of the murtahin (creditor-pledgee). The ruling: qisas is not obligatory (wajib) until both the rahin (debtor-pledgor) and murtahin come together and agree.
This is a conditional ruling — qisas is permissible only when the condition of joint consent is met.
2
Understand the dual reasoning (talil)
The passage gives two reasons. First, the murtahin has no ownership (la mulk lahu), so he alone cannot claim qisas. Second, if the rahin alone claimed qisas, it would void the murtahin's right to the debt (since the slave is collateral). Thus, joint action is needed.
The murtahin's right is a security interest, not ownership. Hence he cannot unilaterally pursue qisas.
3
Address the implicit objection
One might ask: since the murtahin's right is already attached to the slave, why doesn't qisas automatically drop that right? The answer: the right is contingent — the debt might still be paid or the slave released otherwise. So express consent from the murtahin is required to waive his interest.
This is a key nuance: the right is potential, not actual, until qisas is executed.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi position is that joint consent is necessary. Other schools may allow the rahin alone to claim qisas. This ikhtilaf stems from differing views on the nature of the murtahin's right.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is whether qisas can proceed without the murtahin's consent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا قتل عبدالرهن فى يد المرتهن لم يجب القصاص حتى يجتمع الراهن والمرتهن لان المرتهن لا ملک له فلا يليه والراهن لو تولاه البطل حق المرتهن فى الدين فيشترط اجتماعهما ليسقط حق المرتهن برضاه
And if a pledged slave is killed in the possession of the mortgagee, qisas is not obligatory until the mortgagor and mortgagee both come together, because the mortgagee has no ownership so he does not have authority over it, and if the mortgagor alone undertakes it, the right of the mortgagee in the debt is voided. So their meeting together is stipulated so that the right of the mortgagee is dropped by his consent.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for a marhun (pledged) slave who is killed while in the possession of the murtahin (creditor-pledgee). The ruling: qisas is not valid unless both the rahin (debtor-pledgor) and the murtahin are present and agree. The reason is twofold: first, the murtahin does not own the slave (he only has a security interest), so he cannot alone claim qisas. Second, if the rahin alone claimed qisas, that would invalidate the murtahin's right to the debt (since the slave is collateral). Therefore, both must join so that the murtahin's right is dropped with his own consent. The commentary also notes a possible objection: since the murtahin's right is already connected to the slave, why is it not automatically dropped? The answer: the right is still potential because the debt might be paid or the slave might be released by other means. Hence, express consent is needed.

Key Terms
رہن (rahn): Pledge; a contract where property is given as security for a debt.
مرتہن (murtahin): The creditor who holds the pledged property.
راہن (rahin): The debtor who gives the pledge.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment; life for life in homicide cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the rahin has no right in the slave
B) Because it would void the murtahin's right without his consent
C) Because qisas is not allowed for slaves
D) Because the murtahin owns the slave

Key Takeaway
Qisas for a pledged slave requires the joint consent of both the pledgor and the pledgee to protect the pledgee's security interest.
