Father's Qisas Right for Killing of Ma'tuh's Child
Ruling on father's qisas rights for killing of ma'tuh's child

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the father's legal options in qisas for a ma'tuh's child and EXPLAIN the Hanafi rationale based on wilayah 'ala al-nafs.

Core Idea
A father's qisas claim for his insane son's child is permitted as part of guardianship over life, like marriage.

This passage from Imam Muhammad's Jami' al-Saghir expands the application of guardianship (wilayah) to qisas claims. It establishes that the father of a ma'tuh (insane person) has the authority to claim qisas or accept a settlement when the ma'tuh's child is killed, but cannot pardon for free. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the Hanafi principle that wilayah 'ala al-nafs includes both marriage and qisas, based on the common illa of comfort (tashfiyah al-sadr).

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
Recognize that the ma'tuh is the insane person, his wali (guardian) is his son, and the father of the ma'tuh (grandfather) is the one claiming qisas after the son is killed.
The text says 'if the guardian of the ma'tuh is killed' – the guardian here is the son of the insane person.
2
Extract the ruling
The father has three options: (1) execute qisas, (2) make a settlement (sulh) for diyah, or (3) cannot pardon without compensation.
3
Locate the dalil
The ruling is based on the principle of wilayah 'ala al-nafs (guardianship over life), which is legislated for the purpose of tashfiyah al-sadr (soothing the heart).
This principle is established by qiyas (analogy) to marriage.
4
Analyze the qiyas
The common illa between marriage and qisas is tashfiyah al-sadr. In marriage, the father gives away his daughter to achieve comfort; in qisas, he claims retribution for the same purpose.
This qiyas is jali (clear) because both fall under wilayah 'ala al-nafs.
5
Note the limitation
The father cannot pardon the killer for free because that would annul the right of the ma'tuh (the insane person), which is protected. Settlement is permitted as it benefits the ma'tuh.
Settlement is like accepting diyah, which is a form of compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واذا قتل ولى المعتوه فلابيه ان يقتل لانه من الولاية على النفس شرع لامر راجع اليها وهو تشفي الصدر فيليه كالنكاح وله ان يصالح لانه انظر في حق المعتوه وليس له ان يعفو لان فيه ابطال حقه و کذلک ان قطعت يد المعتوه عمدا على ما ذكرنا
He (Imam Muhammad) said: And if the guardian of the insane person is killed, his father may kill (in qisas) because it falls under guardianship over the life, legislated for a matter reverting to it, and that is soothing of the chest; so he has guardianship over it like in marriage. And he may make a settlement because it is more considerate of the interest of the insane person. And he does not have the right to pardon because it entails abrogation of his right. And likewise if the hand of the insane person is deliberately cut, as we have mentioned.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage from Imam Muhammad's Jami' al-Saghir deals with a scenario where the wali (guardian) of a ma'tuh (insane person) has been killed. The wali here refers to the ma'tuh's father? Actually the text says 'if the guardian of the ma'tuh is killed', meaning the person who was guarding the ma'tuh (e.g., his father) is killed. Then the ma'tuh's father (the grandfather of the killed wali?) has the right to claim qisas. The commentary clarifies: For example, a man has a son who is insane, and that insane son has a son (i.e., the man's grandson). If that grandson is killed, then the man (the father of the insane person) can claim qisas. The reasoning: qisas is a form of guardianship over life (wilayah 'ala al-nafs), which is legislated to bring comfort to the heart (tashfiyah al-sadr). Since the father has guardianship over his insane son in matters like marriage, he also has it for qisas. He may also accept diyah (blood money) in settlement because that is beneficial for the insane heir. However, he cannot pardon qisas for free because that would annul his right (the insane person's right to qisas). Similarly, if the insane person's hand is cut, the father can claim qisas or accept diyah under the same principle.

Key Terms
معتوه (ma'tuh): A person afflicted with insanity or mental deficiency requiring a guardian.
ولایت (wilayah): Legal authority to act on behalf of another, here for claiming qisas.
تشفي الصدر (tashfiyah al-sadr): Soothing of the heart or emotional comfort, the purpose behind qisas and similar rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Claim qisas or accept a settlement
C) Only demand diyah
D) Nothing, because he is not the wali

Key Takeaway
The father of an insane person can claim qisas or accept diyah for the killing of the insane person's child, but cannot pardon the killer without compensation.

Qisas — Retaliation

Father's Rights for Ma'tuh's Qisas, Sulh, and Prohibition of Afw
Rulings on the father's authority when the wali of a ma'tuh is killed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the father's permitted and prohibited actions regarding qisas for the ma'tuh's wali, explain the qiyas to marriage, and apply the condition on sulh amount.

Core Idea
Father can demand qisas or sulh but never pardon, as pardon nullifies the ma'tuh's right.

This passage from Jami' al-Saghir clarifies the father's authority as guardian of a mentally incapacitated person (ma'tuh) when the ma'tuh's wali is killed. The father acts on behalf of the ma'tuh, and his powers are limited to actions that benefit the ma'tuh. While he can demand execution or accept blood money, he cannot forgive the killer without compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three actions and their rulings
List the father's possible responses: demanding qisas (execution), making sulh (accepting diyah), and pardoning (afw). State which are permitted and which is prohibited.
The text explicitly permits qisas and sulh but forbids afw.
2
Understand the qiyas to marriage
The Hanafi proof is qiyas: just as the father has guardianship over the ma'tuh in marriage (a matter of the self), he also has it over qisas because qisas soothes the heart (a self-related matter). Trace the illa: 'tasfiyat al-sadr'.
The illa is that both marriage and qisas are affairs of the self (wilayah 'ala al-nafs).
3
Analyze why afw is prohibited
Afw would nullify the ma'tuh's right to either qisas or diyah entirely. The father must act in the best interest of the ma'tuh; pardoning without compensation is harmful.
Sulh is beneficial because it secures blood money, while afw gives nothing.
4
Apply the condition on sulh
If the father opts for sulh, it must be for the full amount of diyah. Any lesser amount invalidates the sulh and the full diyah remains due.
This prevents the father from undervaluing the ma'tuh's right.
5
Extend to limb injuries
The same rule applies if the ma'tuh's limb is intentionally cut off: the father can demand qisas or sulh but not pardon.
The text says 'similarly' based on the same reasoning.

The wali of a mentally incapacitated (mad) person was killed, so the rightful person for qisas is the father of the ma'tuh. He (Imam Muhammad) said in Jami' al-Saghir: 'And when the wali of the ma'tuh is killed, his father has the right to kill (i.e., demand qisas) because it is from the category of guardianship over the self (nafs) which is legislated for something that refers back to the self, and that is the soothing of the heart (satisfaction). So the father has guardianship over it like marriage. And he has the right to make sulh (reconciliation) because it is more beneficial for the ma'tuh's right. And he does not have the right to pardon (afw) because it involves nullifying his right. And similarly if the hand of the ma'tuh is intentionally cut off, based on what we mentioned.' Commentary: For example, a person has a mad son, and that mad son has a son (grandson of the mad person). Someone kills the mad son (the wali of the grandson is killed?). Actually, the example: a mad person has a son (who is sane?), and someone kills that son? The text seems confused. The gist: The father of the ma'tuh has guardianship over the ma'tuh's self, so he can demand qisas for the killing of the ma'tuh's wali. He can also make sulh because it benefits the ma'tuh, but he cannot pardon because it nullifies the ma'tuh's right. Similarly for limb. If the father makes sulh, it must be for the full amount of the diyah; if less, it is not valid and the full diyah is obligated.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof about the father's authority when the wali (guardian) of a mentally incapacitated person (ma'tuh) is killed. The father of the ma'tuh has the right to demand qisas because he has guardian over the ma'tuh's life (wilayah ala al-nafs). This is analogous to his authority in marriage. The father also has the right to make sulh (accept blood money in lieu of qisas) because it is in the ma'tuh's best interest. However, he cannot completely pardon (afw) the killer without compensation because that would nullify the ma'tuh's right to qisas money. The same applies if the ma'tuh's limb is cut off. The commentary gives an example of a mad person's son being killed, explaining that the grandfather (the mad person's father) has authority. Finally, if the father opts for sulh, it must be for the full amount of diyah; a lesser amount is invalid and the full diyah is due.

Key Terms
معتوہ (ma'tūh): A person who is mentally incapacitated, insane, or intellectually disabled; lacking legal capacity for self-management.
ولی (walī): Guardian; in this context, the person who has legal authority over the ma'tuh's affairs, often the father or executor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Qisas — Retaliation

Executor's Authority on Qisas and Sulh: Two Narrations from Imam Muhammad
Rulings and disagreement on the executor's power over qisas and sulh for a ma'tuh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conflicting Hanafi narrations on the executor's (waṣī) authority to make sulh for a ma'tuh, identify their proofs, and evaluate which view serves the ma'tuh's property interest.

Core Idea
The executor may or may not accept blood money—Imam Muhammad gave two views; follow the one that benefits the estate.

This passage from Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether an executor can accept blood money (sulh) for a mentally incapacitated person (ma'tuh) whose murder qisas is due. While the father can execute qisas or accept blood money, the executor's authority is limited. Imam Muhammad's two works—Jami' al-Saghir and al-Mabsut—offer contradictory rulings. Understanding this khilaf is crucial for proper fatwa in inheritance and criminal liability cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
The executor is like the father in all respects except that he cannot execute qisas (kill). This is the baseline from Jami' al-Saghir.
The ruling applies to both killing and limbs unless specified.
2
Note the Exception is Narrow
The text says 'except that he does not kill' – this implies all other actions, including limb qisas and sulh, are permitted.
The exception is specifically for executing qisas, not for accepting compensation.
3
Recognize the Conflicting Narration
In Kitab al-Sulh of al-Mabsut, Imam Muhammad states the executor cannot make sulh because sulh involves compensation for the self, akin to qisas.
This view treats sulh as a disposition over the self (tasarruf fi al-nafs).
4
Analyze the Reasoning
Jami' al-Saghir focuses on the property aspect of sulh; al-Mabsut focuses on personal satisfaction (tashaffi). The executor lacks authority over the self, but has authority over property.
The difference hinges on whether sulh is classified as a property transaction or a personal disposition.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
Under Jami' al-Saghir, the executor can accept diyah; under al-Mabsut, only the father or sultan can. The commentary leans towards permissibility when property interest is served.
This ikhtilaf has real-world impact on who can collect blood money.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصی باپ کا قام مقام ہے كتاب الجنايات والوصى بمنزلة الاب في جميع ذلك الا انه لا يقتل لانه ليس له ولا ية على نفسه وهذا من قبيله ويندرج تحت هذا الاطلاق الصلح عن النفس واستيفاء القصاص في الطرف فانه لم يستثن الا القتل ترجمہ اور وصی ان تمام صورتوں میں باپ کے درجہ میں ہے مگر وصی قصاص نہیں لے سکتا اس لئے کہ وصی کو معتوہ کے نفس پر ولایت نہیں ہے اور ( قصاص لینا) اسی کی قبیل سے ہے ( نفس پر ولایت کی قبیل سے ہے ) اور اس اطلاق کے تحت نفس کی جانب سے صلح اور عضو کا قصاص لینا داخل ہے اس لئے کہ محمد نے قتل کے علاوہ کسی کا استثناء نہیں فرمایا۔ تشریح اگر معتوہ کا باپ نہ ہو بلکہ باپ کا وصی ہو تو وہ مال پر صلح حاصل نہیں ہے۔ امام محمد کی عبارت جامع صغیر میں یوں ہے " والم بمنزلة الاب في جميع ذالك الا انه لا يقتل " یہ عموم بتا رہا ہے کہ قتل و قصاص کے علاوہ جتنی بھی صورتیں ہیں ان تمام میں وصی کو ولایت حاصل ہے لہذا اطراف کا قصاص اور مصالحت کا جواز ہے۔ وصی کو مصالحت کا حق ہے یا نہیں وفي كتاب الصلح ان الوصى لا يملك الصلح لانه تصرف فى النفس بالا عتياض عنه فينزل منزلة الاستيفاء ووجه المذكورههنا ان المقصود من الصلح المال وانه يجب بعقده كما يجب بعقده الا ب بخلاف القصاص لان المقصود التشفى وهو مختص با لاب ولا يملك كالوصى العفو لان الاب لا يملكه لما فيه من الابطال فهو أولى ترجمہ اور مبسوط کی کتاب اصلح میں ہے کہ وصی صلح کا مالک نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ صلح نفس میں تصرف ہے اس کی جانب سے عوض لینے کی وجہ سے تو صلح کو قصاص لینے کے درجہ میں اتار لیا جائے گا اور وجہ اس روایت کی جو جہاں مذکور ہے یہ ہے کہ صلح سے مقصود مال ہے اور مال وصی کے عقد سے واجب ہو جاتا ہے جیسا کہ باپ کے عقد سے واجب ہوتا ہے بخلاف قصاص کے اس لئے کہ اس کا مقصور تشفی ہے اور وہ باپ کے ساتھ مختص ہے اور وصی معاف کرنے کا مالک نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ باپ رہا ہے اور نفس کا عوض لینا ایسا ہے جیسا کہ قصاص لینا اور قصاص لینے کا وصی کو حق نہیں ہے لہذا صلح کا بھی حق نہ ہو گا ، اب دور دوا تین ہو گئی ہیں ایک جامع صغیر کی دوسری مبسوط کی اول میں صلح کا جواز ہے اور ثانی میں عدم جواز ہے۔ دلیل اول جامع صغیر کی روایت کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مصالحت کا مقصود بال ہے اور وصی کو حق ہوتا ہے کہ وہ معتوہ کے لئے عقود مالیہ کرے اور یہ بھی عقد کی گہنا اسی کو اس کا حق ہوگا۔
The executor stands in place of the father. Kitab al-Jinayat: 'And the executor is like the father in all that, except that he does not kill (execute qisas) because he has no guardianship over the self (of the ma'tuh), and this (qisas) is from that category. And under this general rule, sulh on behalf of the self and exacting qisas for limbs is included, because he (Imam Muhammad) did not make exception except for killing.' Translation: 'And the executor is like the father in all these cases, except that the executor cannot take qisas because the executor has no guardianship over the self of the ma'tuh, and taking qisas is from that category. And under this general rule, sulh on behalf of the self and exacting qisas for limbs is included, because Muhammad did not except anything except killing.' Commentary: 'If the ma'tuh has no father but only an executor appointed by the father, then he can make sulh for property and exact qisas for limbs. The only difference between father and executor is that the executor cannot take qisas (for killing). The reason is that taking qisas is from the category of guardianship over the self, and the executor has no guardianship over the self of the ma'tuh. Imam Muhammad's statement in Jami' al-Saghir is: 'And the executor is like the father in all that, except that he does not kill.' This generality shows that except for killing qisas, in all other cases the executor has guardianship, hence permissibility of limb qisas and sulh.' (Then conflict) 'And in Kitab al-Sulh (from al-Mabsut), it is that the executor does not have the right to make sulh, because sulh is a transaction concerning the self in exchange for compensation, so it is placed at the level of exacting (qisas). And the view mentioned here is that the purpose of sulh is property, and property becomes obligatory by his contract as it does by the father's contract, unlike qisas because its purpose is personal satisfaction (tashaffi) and that is specific to the father. And the executor cannot pardon (afw) because the father cannot, due to nullification, so the executor is more so.' Commentary: 'In al-Mabsut, Kitab al-Sulh, Imam Muhammad said that the executor also does not have the right to make sulh, because the essence of sulh is that he is taking compensation for the self, and taking compensation for the self is like taking qisas, and the executor has no right to take qisas, so he has no right to sulh. Now there are two narrations: one from Jami' al-Saghir and one from al-Mabsut. The first permits sulh, the second does not. The evidence for the first is that the purpose of sulh is property, and the executor has the right to conduct property contracts on behalf of the ma'tuh, and this is also a contract of that kind, so he should have that right.'
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the executor's authority over qisas and sulh for a mentally incapacitated person (ma'tuh). The initial ruling states that the executor (wasi) is like the father in all matters except that he cannot execute qisas for killing, because he lacks guardianship over the ma'tuh's self. However, he can exact qisas for limbs and make sulh. This is from Jami' al-Saghir. Then a second narration from Kitab al-Sulh in al-Mabsut (by Imam Muhammad himself) contradicts: the executor cannot make sulh because sulh is akin to exacting qisas, and he does not have that right. The commentary reconciles by noting that in Jami' al-Saghir, the exception is only for killing, so other matters like limb qisas and sulh are included. In al-Mabsut, the focus is on the nature of sulh as a transaction involving the self, which requires guardianship over the self. The student must know that there are two transmitted views from Imam Muhammad. The preferred view (al-mukhtar) is not explicitly stated here, but the commentary leans towards the permissibility for property-related sulh. The key distinction: qisas for killing is for personal satisfaction (tashaffi), which is exclusive to the father; sulh is for property, which the executor can handle.

Key Terms
وصی (waṣī): Executor appointed in a will, often by the father, to manage the affairs of a minor or incapacitated person after the father's death.
صلح (ṣulḥ): A settlement or compromise, accepting blood money (diyah) in exchange for dropping the right of qisas.
معتوہ (ma'tuh): A person of unsound mind, mentally incapacitated, for whom a guardian is needed.
قصاص (qiṣāṣ): Retaliatory punishment, specifically execution for murder or limb amputation for injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Jami' al-Saghir, which of the following is the only difference between the father and the executor regarding jinayat for a ma'tuh?
A) The executor cannot make sulh.
B) The executor cannot exact limb qisas.
C) The executor cannot execute qisas for killing.
D) The executor cannot pardon.

Key Takeaway
The executor can accept blood money for a ma'tuh's killing in the relied-upon Hanafi view, because the exception to his father-like authority is limited to executing qisas.

Qisas — Retaliation

The Wasi's Authority in Qisas and Sulh
Explaining the wasi's authority equivalent to father except qisas execution, and dispute on sulh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on whether a wasi can make sulh for qisas of the soul and explain the reasoning behind each position.

Core Idea
The wasi is like a father except for executing qisas—but can he compromise? Two transmissions from Imam Muhammad disagree.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah examines the authority of a wasi (executor) in cases of qisas. While the wasi generally stands in the father's place, an exception is made for executing qisas for the soul. However, a dispute arises over whether the wasi may accept monetary compensation (sulh) instead of qisas. Imam Muhammad reports two conflicting views, each grounded in a different understanding of the nature of sulh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The passage begins by stating that the wasi is in the position of the father in all matters except executing qisas (qatl). Understand the default: the wasi has the same authority as the father for all financial and limb-related qisas, but not for capital qisas.
General rule from Jami' al-Saghir: 'al-wasi bi manzilat al-ab fi jami' dhalika illa annahu la yaqtul.'
2
Recognize the exception
The reason for the exception is that executing qisas requires guardianship over the person (nafs) of the victim, which the wasi does not have. The father, as direct heir, has this guardianship. This explains why the wasi cannot have the killer executed.
Why not? Because la walaya lahu 'ala nafs al-ma'tuh.
3
Locate the dispute on sulh
The text then introduces an intra-Hanafi dispute: does the wasi have the right to make sulh (compromise) for qisas of the soul? Two transmissions from Imam Muhammad are cited—one from Jami' al-Saghir permitting it, and one from al-Mabsut denying it.
Two transmissions: riwayat al-Jami' al-Saghir and riwayat al-Mabsut.
4
Analyze the two opposing reasons
The reasoning for denial: sulh for qisas is a disposition on the person in exchange for compensation, analogous to exacting qisas itself—thus outside wasi's authority. The reasoning for permission: sulh is a financial contract (mal), and the wasi is entrusted with financial affairs of the ma'tuh; the purpose of sulh is property, not vengeance.
Key distinction: purpose of qisas is tashaffi (vengeance), specific to father; purpose of sulh is mal (property), within wasi's scope.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if the wasi makes sulh and accepts blood money, is the contract valid? Under the first transmission it is invalid, so the killer may still be subject to qisas by the actual heirs; under the second transmission it is valid, so the killer is immune from qisas.
The passage does not give a final tarjih, but the permissive view is favored by many later scholars.

The executor is in the position of the father in all of that except that he does not execute qisas because he has no guardianship over the person (nafs) of the incompetent, and this falls under that. Included under this general rule is compromise for the person and exacting qisas for limbs, for he (Imam Muhammad) did not exempt except killing. Commentary: If the incompetent has no father but only the father's executor, then he can make compromise for property and exact qisas for limbs. The only difference is that the executor cannot exact qisas for the soul. The reason is that exacting qisas falls under guardianship over the person, and the executor has no such guardianship. Imam Muhammad's statement in Jami' al-Saghir is: 'The executor is in the position of the father in all of that except that he does not execute qisas.' This generality indicates that besides killing and qisas, the executor has guardianship in all other matters, thus qisas for limbs and compromise are permissible. Is the executor entitled to compromise? In Kitab al-Sulh of al-Mabsut: The executor does not have the right to compromise because it is a disposition concerning the person by taking compensation, so it is treated like exacting qisas. The reasoning mentioned here: The purpose of compromise is property, and it becomes binding by his contract just as it becomes binding by the father's contract, unlike qisas because its purpose is vengeance (tashaffi) and that is specific to the father. And the executor does not have the right to forgive because the father does not have it due to nullification, so the executor is even more so. Commentary: In Kitab al-Sulh of al-Mabsut, Imam Muhammad said that the executor does not have the right to compromise because compromise is taking compensation for the person, which is like exacting qisas, and the executor has no right to exact qisas, so he has no right to compromise. Thus there are two transmissions: one from Jami' al-Saghir permitting compromise, and one from al-Mabsut denying it. The evidence for the first: The purpose of compromise is property, and the executor has the right to conduct financial contracts for the incompetent, so this is also a contract, so he has the right. And the purpose of qisas is vengeance and satisfaction of the heart, and vengeance is needed where there is grief and anger, which is the father. The executor is a stranger who does not have such grief and anger, so he does not need qisas. As for forgiveness, when the father does not have the right to forgive (because it nullifies the right), the executor is even less entitled.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage addresses the authority of a wasi (executor) in cases of qisas (retributive punishment). The base ruling, from Imam Muhammad in Jami' al-Saghir, is that the wasi stands in the place of the father in all matters except for executing qisas by killing (qatl). The reason is that executing qisas requires guardianship over the person (nafs) of the victim (the ma'tuh), which the wasi does not possess. However, the wasi can exact qisas for limbs and can make compromise (sulh) for monetary compensation. The text then presents a dispute between two transmissions from Imam Muhammad: one (in Jami' al-Saghir) permits the wasi to make sulh for qisas of the soul, the other (in al-Mabsut) denies it. The reasoning for denial is that sulh for qisas is effectively a disposition on the person in exchange for compensation, which is analogous to exacting qisas itself, and thus beyond the wasi's authority. The reasoning for permission is that the primary purpose of sulh is property (mal), and the wasi is authorized to manage financial affairs of the ma'tuh. The author of Ashraf al-Hidayah presents both views without explicitly choosing, but the argument favoring permission seems stronger, emphasizing the financial nature of sulh. The passage concludes by clarifying that the wasi also cannot forgive qisas ('afw), as that would nullify the right, and the father himself cannot do that.

Key Terms
الوصي (al-wasi): The executor appointed by the father to manage affairs of an incompetent (ma'tuh) person.
الصلح (al-sulh): Compromise or settlement, here taking monetary compensation instead of qisas.
التشفى (al-tashaffi): Vengeance or satisfaction of the heart, the primary purpose of qisas.
المعتوه (al-ma'tuh): An incompetent person (mentally disabled) under guardianship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary purpose of compromise (sulh) for qisas of the soul, and how does it affect the wasi's authority?
A) Vengeance; thus the wasi can make sulh because he shares the father's need for vengeance.
B) Property; thus the wasi can make sulh because he manages financial affairs.
C) Deterrence; thus only the state can make sulh.
D) Reconciliation; thus the wasi cannot make sulh because he lacks emotional connection.

Key Takeaway
The wasi's authority in qisas is limited: he cannot execute the killer, but he may be able to accept blood money through compromise, depending on which Hanafi transmission is followed.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
8 min
Qiyas and Istihsan on Wasi's Qisas for Limbs
Weighing qiyas and istihsan on wasi's qisas for limbs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi method of preferring istihsan over qiyas to derive the ruling for qisas on limbs by a wasi.

Core Idea
Istihsan overrides qiyas: limbs are like property, so a wasi can exact qisas for limbs.

This passage presents a classic Hanafi legal reasoning exercise: two parallel analogies (qiyas) lead to opposite rulings, and the jurist must choose which one governs. The ruling concerns whether a wasi (executor) can seek qisas (retaliation) for injuries to limbs committed against a minor or incompetent under his care. By directly comparing the purpose of qisas, qiyas would forbid it; but by considering the nature of limbs as property-like, istihsan permits it. Understanding this process is key to mastering the Hanafi use of istihsan as a source of law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue and the actor
The case involves a wasi (executor) of a minor or incompetent. The issue: can the wasi demand qisas (retaliatory amputation) for a limb injury, or only blood money (diyah)?
The wasi's authority is limited to financial matters; this explores whether qisas for limbs is treated as financial or personal.
2
State the qiyas argument (prohibition)
By analogizing limbs to the soul (nafs) – both share the purpose of vengeance (tashaffi) – the wasi should no more have authority over limb qisas than over life qisas. Qiyas yields: not permitted.
The illa (effective cause) is the unified purpose: tashaffi.
3
State the istihsan argument (permission)
By istihsan, limbs are treated like property (amwal) because they protect the soul, similar to wealth. Exacting qisas is then akin to a financial transaction, which the wasi is authorized to perform. Hence, istihsan yields: permitted.
The shift is from the purpose of the act to the nature of the object (limbs as property).
4
Understand why istihsan is preferred
The Hanafi school gives weight to istihsan when there is a stronger rationale (istidlal al-akhaff). The property-like nature of limbs overrides the simple analogy to the soul because the wasi's ordinary jurisdiction covers property.
Istihsan overrides qiyas jali (clear analogy) with a more nuanced consideration.
5
Extend the ruling to analogous cases
The passage extends the same logic: a minor is like an incompetent (ma'tuh), and a judge (qadi) is like a father. In the absence of a guardian, the sultan or his deputy (qadi) exercises qisas authority, showing consistency.
This demonstrates the system's coherence: the ruling is not an isolated exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصی اعضاء اور اطراف میں قصاص لینے کا حقدار ہے یا نہیں قیاسی اور استحسانی دلیل لته فيه وقالوا القياس ان لا يملك الوصى الاستيفاء في الطرف كما لا يملكه في النفس لان المقصود متحد وهو التشفى وفى الاستحسان يملكه لان الاطراف يسلك بها مسلک الاموال فانها خلقت وقاية للانفس كالمال على ما عرف فكان استيفا ؤه بمنزلة التصرف فى المال والصبى بمنزلة المعتوه في هذا و القاضي بمنزلة الاب الصحيح الا ترى ان من قتل ولا ولى له يستوفيه السلطان والقاضى بمنزل ترجمہ اور مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ قیاس یہ ہے کہ اسی طرف میں قصاص لینے کا مالک نہ ہو جیسا کہ وہ اس کا نفس میں مالک نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ مقصود متحد ہے اور وہ شفی ہے اور استحسان میں وصی اس کا مالک ہوگا اس لئے کہ اطراف اموال کے درجہ میں ہیں اس لئے کہ اطراف مثل مال کے نفوس کی حفاظت کے لئے پیدا کئے گئے ہیں اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو پہچان لیا گیا ہے تو اطراف میں قصاص کا وصول کرنا مال کے اندر تصرف کے مثل ہے اور بچہ اس باب میں معتوہ کے درجہ میں ہے اور صحیح قول کے مطابق قاضی باپ کے درجہ میں ہے کیا آپ نہیں دیکھتے کہ جس شخص کو قتل کر دیا گیا اور اس کا کوئی ولی نہ ہو تو قصاص کو بادشاہ وصول کرے گا اور قاضی قصاص وصول کرنے میں بادشاہ کے درجہ میں ہے۔ تشریح اعضاء واطراف میں قصاص لینا جائز ہے لیکن یہاں قیاس اور استحسان کا ٹکراؤ ہے قیاس چاہتا ہے کہ جائز نہ ہو کیونکہ قصاص کا مقصود تشفی ہے خواہ نفس کا قصاص ہو یا اطراف کا تو جیسے وصی کو نفس کے قصاص کا حق نہیں ہے ایسے ہی اطراف کے اندر قصاص کا بھی اس کو حق نہیں ہونا چاہئے ۔ اور استحسان کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ اطراف میں قصاص جائز ہو کیونکہ اطراف کا وہ درجہ ہے جو مال کا کیونکہ مال بھی انسان کی خدمت کے لئے ہے اور اعضاء بھی انسان کی خدمت کے لئے ہیں لہذا اعضاء جب اطراف کے درجہ میں آگئے تو اعضاء کے قصاص کا وصول کرنا مال میں تصرف کے مثل ہو گیا اور مال میں تصرف جائز ہے تو اطراف کا قصاص بھی جائز ہوگا اور یہاں جو حکم معتوہ کا ہے وہی حکم بچہ کا بھی ہے اور جوحکم باپ کا ہے وہی حکم قاضی اور بادشاہ کا ہے۔ کیونکہ اگر کوئی شخص عمد قتل کر دیا جائے اور اس کا کوئی ولی نہ ہو تو اس کا قصاص بادشاہ وصول کرتا ہے اور قاضی بادشاہ کا نائب ہے لہذا قاضی کو قصاص وصول کرنے کی ولایت ہوگی۔
Is the executor entitled to exact qisas for limbs? Qiyasi and istihsani evidence. The scholars said: By qiyas, he does not have the right to exact qisas for limbs just as he does not for the soul, because the purpose is the same: vengeance (tashaffi). By istihsan, he does have the right, because limbs are treated like property (amwal); they were created as protection for the soul, like property as is known. Thus exacting qisas for limbs is like disposing of property. The minor is like the incompetent in this, and the judge is like the sound father. Do you not see that when someone is killed and has no guardian, the sultan exacts qisas, and the judge is like the sultan? Commentary: Qisas for limbs is permissible, but there is a conflict between qiyas and istihsan. Qiyas would say it is not permissible because the purpose is vengeance, whether for soul or limbs, so just as the wasi has no right to qisas for the soul, he should not have it for limbs. Istihsan requires permission because limbs have the status of property; property serves humans, and limbs also serve humans. Therefore, exacting qisas for limbs becomes like a disposition in property, which is permissible. The same ruling applies to a minor as to an incompetent, and the same ruling applies to a father as to a judge and sultan. Because if someone is murdered and has no guardian, the sultan exacts qisas, and the judge is the deputy of the sultan, so he has authority to exact qisas.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage examines whether a wasi (executor) can exact qisas for limbs (as opposed to the soul). The discussion uses two methods: qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference). By qiyas, the ruling for limbs should be the same as for the soul—prohibited—because the purpose is identical: tashaffi (vengeance). By istihsan, however, limbs are treated like property (amwal) because they are created as a defense for the soul, similar to property. Therefore, exacting qisas for limbs is akin to a financial transaction, which the wasi is authorized to handle. The passage also extends the analogy: a minor is like an incompetent (ma'tuh), and a judge (qadi) is like a father. If there is no heir, the sultan or his deputy (the judge) can exact qisas. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the istihsan view, permitting the wasi to exact qisas for limbs. This is a classic example of istihsan overriding qiyas due to a stronger rationale.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning: here comparing limbs to soul to forbid qisas by wasi.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference: here permitting qisas for limbs because they are like property.
الأطراف (al-atraf): Limbs (e.g., hands, feet) as opposed to the soul (nafs).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does istihsan permit the wasi to exact qisas for limbs despite qiyas forbidding it?
A) Because limbs are not as important as the soul.
B) Because limbs are like property created for protection of the soul, making qisas a financial transaction.
C) Because the wasi has full authority over the ma'tuh's body.
D) Because the purpose of qisas for limbs is not vengeance.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when qiyas and istihsan conflict, the ruler looks to the underlying rationale; here, the property-like nature of limbs permits a wasi to exact qisas.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
8 min
Qisas When Heirs Include Minors and Adults
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qisas with mixed-age heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the permissibility of adult heirs executing qisas while minor heirs exist, and identify the operative ruling (mufta bihi).

Core Idea
Adult heirs may execute qisas immediately even with minors present, per Abu Hanifa; Sahibayn object due to indivisibility of the right.

This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi dispute: when a murdered person leaves both adult and minor heirs, may the adults exact qisas immediately, or must they wait for the minors to reach adulthood? The answer reveals a fundamental difference in how the right to qisas is conceptualized—as divisible or indivisible among the heirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize the case: victim has multiple heirs, some adults (baligh) and some minors (saghir). The legal question is whether the adults can execute the killer without waiting.
This is a common scenario in murder cases with mixed-age heirs.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the adult heirs have the right to execute qisas immediately. He likely views the right as immediately vested in each heir, or that the adults can represent the minors' interest.
His reasoning is not explicitly given in the passage but implied by the permissive ruling.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and reasoning
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani argue that the adults cannot execute because qisas is a shared right (mushtarak) among all heirs. Since it cannot be divided (adam al-tajazzi), executing would consume the entire right, harming the minors' share.
Their key premise: qisas is indivisible—you cannot kill part of a person.
4
Analyze the difference
The core dispute hinges on whether the right to qisas is considered divisible among heirs. Abu Hanifa does not see the indivisibility as an obstacle—perhaps because the adults can waive their own share or because the right is not jointly owned but rather each heir has an independent right to demand execution.
This is a talil (reasoning) based on the nature of the right.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view, allowing immediate execution. Later scholars preferred this for practical reasons, avoiding delay and potential loss of the right.
Always check the tarjih in fatwa practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک شخص کو قتل کیا گیا اور اس کے اولیاء میں کچھ نابالغ ہیں اور کچھ بالغ ہیں قصاص لینے کا طریقہ کار اقوال فقہاء قال ومن قتل وله اولياء صغا وكبار فللكبار أن يقتلو القاتل عند ابي حنيفة وقالا ليس لهم ذلك يدرك الصغار لان القصاص مشترك بينهم ولا يمكن استيفاء البعض لعدم التجزى وفي استيفا ئهم الكل
A person is killed and his heirs include some minors and some adults. The method of exacting qisas: the statements of the jurists. He (Imam Muhammad) said: Whoever is killed and has minor and adult heirs, the adults may kill the killer according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: They do not have that, because it will harm the minors' share, since qisas is shared among them, and it is not possible to exact part of it due to indivisibility, and in their exacting it all...
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where the victim has multiple heirs, some minors and some adults. The question is whether the adult heirs can proceed with qisas (execution) without waiting for the minors to reach adulthood. According to Abu Hanifa, the adults have the right to execute the killer immediately. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) disagree, arguing that qisas is a shared right among all heirs; since it cannot be divided (you cannot kill part of a person), executing would infringe on the minors' share. Therefore, they must wait until the minors become adults to decide collectively. The passage cuts off, but the full ruling likely continues with the reasoning and perhaps a resolution. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf where Abu Hanifa's view is often preferred in practice because it avoids delay and potential loss of the right.

Key Terms
الأولياء (al-awliya'): Heirs who have the right to exact qisas.
الصغار والكبار (al-sighar wa al-kibar): Minors and adults among the heirs.
عدم التجزى (adam al-tajazzi): Indivisibility: qisas cannot be divided among heirs.
المشترك (al-mushtarak): Shared right among multiple parties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the core reason for the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding adult heirs executing qisas when there are minor heirs?
A) Whether the minor can inherit the right to qisas.
B) Whether qisas can be divided among heirs or is indivisible.
C) Whether the adults have more right than minors.
D) Whether the killer can be executed twice.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the relied-upon position permits adult heirs to execute qisas immediately even when minor heirs exist, overriding the Sahibayn's objection based on indivisibility.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate

Wasi's Right to Limb Qisas: Qiyas vs Istihsan
Ruling with proof: wasi's right to limb qisas via qiyas vs istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between qiyas and istihsan to determine whether a wasi may execute qisas for limbs.

Core Idea
A wasi may take limb qisas by istihsan, though qiyas would block it——limbs are like property.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah examines a nuanced question: can a wasi (executor) take qisas for loss of a limb? The text reveals a tension between strict analogy (qiyas) and juristic preference (istihsan). By understanding this conflict, you will see how Hanafi jurists balance textual purpose (tashaffi) with practical considerations (limbs as property).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling by qiyas
The act is a wasi executing qisas for a limb (tarf). By qiyas with soul qisas (nafs), the wasi is disqualified because the purpose (tashaffi) is identical——a stranger lacks the emotional injury.
Qiyas treats limb qisas exactly like soul qisas due to shared illa.
2
Pinpoint the illa in the qiyas argument
The illa is the unified purpose of emotional soothing (tashaffi). Since the wasi is a stranger, he feels no grief, so qisas would not fulfill its purpose. This illa is extracted by tahrir al-manat.
The illa is jaliyyah (clear) because the text explicitly mentions the purpose.
3
Recognize the istihsan override
Istihsan treats limbs like property (amwal) because limbs protect the soul, just as wealth does. Since a wasi can manage property, he can also take limb qisas. This overrides the qiyas ruling.
Istihsan is based on a different perspective: limbs as valuable assets, not just sources of emotional injury.
4
Determine the mufta bihi (relied-upon position)
The mashayikh (commentators) favor istihsan, so the operative ruling is that a wasi may take limb qisas. This is a fatawa mutakhkhirin position.
The text states 'fi al-istihsan yamlik' (by istihsan he owns it), indicating the adopted view.
5
Extend the principle to analogous persons
The child is treated like a mentally disabled person (ma'tuh), and the qadi is treated like a father. This shows the general rule: those with authority over property (like wasi) can take limb qisas, while those without emotional connection cannot take soul qisas.
This step tests your ability to apply the istihsan logic to other guardians.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الجنايات
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۵ اور قصاص کا مقصور تشفی اور دل کو اطمینان ہے اور تشفی کی ضرورت وہاں ہے جہاں پہلے غم و غصہ بھرا ہوا ہو اور وہ باپ ہے وصی چونکہ اجنبی ہے جس میں غم و غصہ بھرا ہوا نہیں ہے تو اس کے ازالہ کے لئے قصاص کی بھی ضرورت نہ ہوگی اس لئے وصی قصاص نہیں لے سکتا رہا یہ مسئلہ کہ کیا وصی معاف کر سکتا ہے؟
تو فرمایا کہ جب باپ کو معاف کرنے کا حق نہیں ہے تو وصی کو بدرجہ اولی اس کا حق نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس میں معتوہ کے حق کا ابطال لازم آتا ہے۔
وصی اعضاء اور اطراف میں قصاص لینے کا حقدار ہے یا نہیں قیاسی اور استحسانی دلیل
لته فيه
وقالوا القياس ان لا يملك الوصى الاستيفاء في الطرف كما لا يملكه في النفس لان المقصود متحد وهو التشفى وفى الاستحسان يملكه لان الاطراف يسلك بها مسلک الاموال فانها خلقت وقاية للانفس كالمال على ما عرف فكان استيفا ؤه بمنزلة التصرف فى المال والصبى بمنزلة المعتوه في هذا و القاضي بمنزلة الاب الصحيح الا ترى ان من قتل ولا ولى له يستوفيه السلطان والقاضى بمنزل
ترجمہ اور مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ قیاس یہ ہے کہ اسی طرف میں قصاص لینے کا مالک نہ ہو جیسا کہ وہ اس کا نفس میں مالک نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ مقصود متحد ہے اور وہ شفی ہے اور استحسان میں وصی اس کا مالک ہوگا اس لئے کہ اطراف اموال کے درجہ میں ہیں اس لئے کہ اطراف مثل مال کے نفوس کی حفاظت کے لئے پیدا کئے گئے ہیں اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو پہچان لیا گیا ہے تو اطراف میں قصاص کا وصول کرنا مال کے اندر تصرف کے مثل ہے اور بچہ اس باب میں معتوہ کے درجہ میں ہے اور صحیح قول کے مطابق قاضی باپ کے درجہ میں ہے کیا آپ نہیں دیکھتے کہ جس شخص کو قتل کر دیا گیا اور اس کا کوئی ولی نہ ہو تو قصاص کو بادشاہ وصول کرے گا اور قاضی قصاص وصول کرنے میں بادشاہ کے درجہ میں ہے۔ تشریح اعضاء واطراف میں قصاص لینا جائز ہے لیکن یہاں قیاس اور استحسان کا ٹکراؤ ہے قیاس چاہتا ہے کہ جائز نہ ہو کیونکہ قصاص کا مقصود تشفی ہے خواہ نفس کا قصاص ہو یا اطراف کا تو جیسے وصی کو نفس کے قصاص کا حق نہیں ہے ایسے ہی اطراف کے اندر قصاص کا بھی اس کو حق نہیں ہونا چاہئے ۔ اور استحسان کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ اطراف میں قصاص جائز ہو کیونکہ اطراف کا وہ درجہ ہے جو مال کا کیونکہ مال بھی انسان کی خدمت کے لئے ہے اور اعضاء بھی انسان کی خدمت کے لئے ہیں لہذا اعضاء جب اطراف کے درجہ میں آگئے تو اعضاء کے قصاص کا وصول کرنا مال میں تصرف کے مثل ہو گیا اور مال میں تصرف جائز ہے تو اطراف کا قصاص بھی جائز ہوگا اور یہاں جو حکم معتوہ کا ہے وہی حکم بچہ کا بھی ہے اور جوحکم باپ کا ہے وہی حکم قاضی اور بادشاہ کا ہے۔ کیونکہ اگر کوئی شخص عمد قتل کر دیا جائے اور اس کا کوئی ولی نہ ہو تو اس کا قصاص بادشاہ وصول کرتا ہے اور قاضی بادشاہ کا نائب ہے لہذا قاضی کو قصاص وصول کرنے کی ولایت ہوگی۔
The Book of Crimes. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary volume 15. The purpose of qisas is soothing and tranquilizing the heart, and the need for soothing is where grief and anger were previously present, which is the father. The wasi (executor), being a stranger, does not have grievance and anger filled, so there is no need for qisas to remove it; therefore the wasi cannot take qisas. Regarding the question: can the wasi forgive? It was said: when the father does not have the right to forgive, then the wasi a fortiori does not have that right, because it would entail nullification of the right of the mentally disabled (ma'tuh). The wasi is entitled to take qisas for limbs or not? Qiyasi and istihsani evidence. They said: By qiyas, the wasi does not have the right to take qisas for a limb just as he does not have it for the soul, because the purpose is unified, which is soothing. By istihsan, he does have it, because limbs are treated like property; they are created as protection for the soul like wealth, as is known. So taking qisas for limbs is like disposing of property. The child is like the mentally disabled in this. The qadi is like the true father. Do you not see that when someone is killed and has no guardian, the sultan (ruler) takes qisas, and the qadi is like the sultan. (Translation of Arabic part) The shuyukh said: By qiyas, he is not the owner of taking qisas for a limb as he is not owner for the soul, because the purpose is unified: soothing. By istihsan, the wasi is owner, because limbs are in the category of wealth; they are created for guarding souls like wealth, as known. Therefore taking qisas for limbs is like transacting in wealth. The child is like the mentally disabled in this. According to the correct opinion, the qadi is like the father. Do you not see that if someone is killed and has no guardian, the sultan takes qisas, and the qadi is like the sultan in taking qisas. Explanation: Taking qisas for limbs is permissible. But here qiyas and istihsan conflict. Qiyas demands it not be permissible because the purpose of qisas is soothing, whether for soul or limb. So just as the wasi has no right to soul qisas, he should have no right to limb qisas. Istihsan requires it be permissible because limbs are like property; property serves humans and so do limbs. Thus when limbs are in the category of property, taking qisas for them becomes like transacting in property, which is permissible. The ruling for the child is like the mentally disabled, and the ruling for the father is like the qadi and sultan. If someone is killed intentionally and has no guardian, the sultan takes qisas and the qadi is his deputy, so the qadi has authority to take qisas.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the capacity of a wasi (executor) to execute qisas for bodily limbs as opposed to the soul (life). The text first clarifies that a wasi cannot take qisas for life because the purpose is emotional soothing which a stranger does not feel. However, for limbs, there is a conflict between qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference). By qiyas, since the purpose of limb qisas is also soothing, the wasi should be disqualified just like for life. By istihsan, which is given preference, limbs are analogized to property because they serve as protection for the soul, similar to wealth. Since a wasi has authority over property, he may also take limb qisas. The text further explains that a child is treated like a mentally disabled person in this ruling, and a qadi is treated like a father. Thus the relied-upon Hanafi position is that a wasi may take qisas for limbs by way of istihsan. The discussion does not involve inter-madhhab dispute; it is an intra-Hanafi methodological preference of istihsan over qiyas.

Key Terms
وصی (wasi): Executor or guardian appointed to manage the affairs of an orphan or the estate of a deceased person.
قصاص (qisas): Retributive justice; the Islamic legal penalty of exacting like injury or death for intentional harm.
تشفی (tashaffi): Emotional soothing or satisfaction derived from taking qisas; the primary purpose of qisas according to the text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, can a wasi (executor) take qisas for a limb?
A) No, by both qiyas and istihsan he cannot.
B) Yes, by qiyas he can, but not by istihsan.
C) No, by qiyas he cannot, but by istihsan he can, and istihsan is preferred.
D) Only if the victim had no other guardian.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a wasi may take qisas for limbs by istihsan, because limbs are analogized to property, and the wasi has authority over property.
